▸ 19.1 Metabolic Medicine 6
▸ 19.1.1 Amyloidosis
[!info]
Amyloidosis = Extracellular Deposition of Misfolded Protein Fibrils (β-Pleated Sheets) → Organ Dysfunction. Classification by Precursor Protein: AL (Light Chain), AA (Serum Amyloid A), ATTR (Transthyretin), Others. Diagnosis = Tissue Biopsy + Congo Red (Apple-Green Birefringence) + Typing.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Classify amyloidosis by precursor protein (AL, AA, ATTR, others)
  • [ ] Recognise organ-specific clinical presentations
  • [ ] Apply diagnostic pathway: Biopsy + Congo Red + Typing (Mass Spec / IHC)
  • [ ] Apply type-specific management: AL (Chemo/SCT), AA (Anti-inflammatory), ATTR (Stabilisers/Silencers/Transplant)
  • [ ] Recognise key complications and monitoring

2. Classification by Precursor Protein

TypePrecursor ProteinSourceAssociated Conditions
AL (Primary)Immunoglobulin Light Chain (κ/λ)Plasma Cell DyscrasiaMultiple Myeloma, MGUS, Waldenström, B-Cell Lymphoma
AA (Secondary)Serum Amyloid A (SAA)Acute Phase ReactantChronic Inflammation: RA, IBD, TB, FMF, Bronchiectasis
ATTRv (Hereditary)Transthyretin (TTR) MutantGenetic (TTR Mutation)Familial Amyloid Polyneuropathy (FAP), Cardiomyopathy
ATTRwt (Wild-Type)Transthyretin (Wild-Type)Age-RelatedSenile Systemic Amyloidosis (Elderly Males; Cardiac)
ALECT2Leukocyte Chemotactic Factor 2UnknownRenal (Hispanic/Asian)
ApoAI/IIApolipoprotein A-I/IIGeneticRenal, Hepatic, Neuropathy
FibrinogenFibrinogen α-ChainGeneticRenal
LysozymeLysozymeGeneticRenal, GI, Hepatic

2. AL Amyloidosis (Primary / Light Chain)

Epidemiology & Pathogenesis

FeatureDetails
Incidence~9-12/million/year; Median Age 65
PathogenesisClonal Plasma Cells → Monoclonal Light Chain (κ > λ) → Misfolding → Fibril Deposition
Association10-15% Multiple Myeloma; 30-40% MGUS; Can Occur in Isolation

Clinical Manifestations

OrganFeatures
RenalNephrotic Syndrome (Proteinuria >3.5g/d), CKD, End-Stage Renal Disease
CardiacRestrictive Cardiomyopathy, HFpEF, Arrhythmias, Conduction Disease, Low Voltage ECG
NeurologicalPeripheral Neuropathy (Sensory > Motor), Carpal Tunnel Syndrome, Autonomic Neuropathy
HepaticHepatomegaly, Cholestasis, Elevated ALP
GIMacroglossia, GI Motility Disorders, Bleeding (Amyloid Vascular Fragility)
Soft TissuePeriorbital Purpura, Shoulder Pad Sign, Subcutaneous Nodules
HaematologicalFactor X Deficiency (Adsorption to Amyloid), Coagulopathy

Diagnosis

TestFinding
Tissue Biopsy + Congo RedApple-Green Birefringence (Gold Standard)
Mass Spectrometry / IHCAL-κ or AL-λ (Typing)
Serum Free Light Chains (FLC)Abnormal κ/λ Ratio (Abnormal Ratio; Normal Total)
Bone Marrow BiopsyClonal Plasma Cells (% Plasma Cells)
Cardiac MRI / EchoLate Gadolinium Enhancement, Granular Sparkling

Management

TherapyDetails
First-LineBorortezomib-Based (CyBorD, Dara-CyBorD) — Target Plasma Cells
Autologous SCTEligible: Age <70, Good PS, ≤2 Organ Involvement, Cardiac Stage I-II
SupportiveDiuretics, ACEi/ARB (Cautious), Compression Stockings, Anticoagulation (If Factor X Deficiency)
EmergingDaratumumab (Anti-CD38), CAR-T, Bispecific Antibodies

Prognosis

Stage (Mayo 2004)Median Survival
Stage I (Cardiac Biomarkers Normal)>10 Years
Stage II (One Elevated)~5 Years
Stage III (Both Elevated)~2 Years
Stage IV (Three Elevated)<1 Year

2. AA Amyloidosis (Secondary / Reactive)

Pathogenesis

FeatureDetails
PrecursorSerum Amyloid A (SAA) — Acute Phase Reactant (IL-6 Driven)
TriggerChronic Inflammation → Sustained High SAA → Fibril Formation
Associated ConditionsRA, JIA, AS, PsA, IBD, FMF, TB, Bronchiectasis, Chronic Osteomyelitis, Castleman Disease

Clinical Manifestations

OrganFeatures
RenalNephrotic Syndrome, CKD (Most Common Presentation)
HepaticHepatomegaly, Splenomegaly
CardiacRare (Unlike AL)
NeurologicalRare

Management

StrategyDetails
PrimaryTreat Underlying Inflammation (TNF Inhibitors, IL-1/6 Blockers, DMARDs)
FMFColchicine (Prophylaxis + Treatment)
SupportiveDiuretics, ACEi/ARB (Careful), Renal Replacement if ESRD
PrognosisBetter than AL if Inflammation Controlled

2. ATTR Amyloidosis (Transthyretin)

ATTRv (Hereditary / Variant)

FeatureDetails
Genetics>130 TTR Mutations (V30M Most Common in Portugal/Japan; T60A in UK/Ireland)
InheritanceAutosomal Dominant (Penetrance Variable)
PhenotypesFAP (Neuropathy + Autonomic), Cardiomyopathy, Mixed

ATTRwt (Wild-Type / Senile Systemic)

FeatureDetails
DemographicsElderly Males (>70 Years)
PresentationCardiomyopathy (HFpEF, Conduction Disease), Carpal Tunnel (Precedes by Years)
GeneticsWild-Type TTR (No Mutation)

Diagnosis

TestFinding
Tissue Biopsy + Congo RedApple-Green Birefringence
Mass Spec / IHCATTR (Transthyretin)
PYP/DPD ScintigraphyGrade 1-3 Cardiac Uptake (Non-Invasive Diagnosis for ATTR)
Genetic TestingTTR Mutation (ATTRv); Wild-Type (ATTRwt)
Cardiac MRI / EchoLate Gadolinium Enhancement, Granular Sparkling, Apical Sparing

Management

TypeTherapy
ATTRv / ATTRwt (Cardiac)Tafamidis 61mg OD (1st Line; TTR Stabiliser — ATTR-ACT Trial), Diflunisal (Neuropathy; Off-Label)
ATTRv (Neuropathy)Gene Silencers: Patisiran (siRNA IV q3wk), Inotersen (ASO SC Weekly), Vutrisiran (siRNA SC q3mo)
ATTRvLiver Transplant (Curative for Variant Production) + Cardiac Tx if Needed
SupportiveHeart Failure Rx (Diuretics, Avoid β-Blockers Initially in ATTR), Pacemaker/ICD, Autonomic Neuropathy Rx

2. Other Rare Types

TypeKey Features
ALECT2Renal Amyloidosis (Hispanic/Asian); No Systemic Involvement
ApoAI/IIRenal, Hepatic, Neuropathy; Autosomal Dominant
FibrinogenRenal (Hereditary Renal Amyloidosis); Autosomal Dominant
LysozymeRenal, GI, Hepatic; Autosomal Dominant

3. Diagnostic Pathway

SUSPECTED AMYLOIDOSIS (Organ Dysfunction + Proteinuria/Cardiomyopathy/Neuropathy)
         │
         ▼
TISSUE BIOPSY + CONGO RED STAIN
         │
         ├── **APPLE-GREEN BIREFRINGENCE** → **AMYLOID CONFIRMED**
         │       │
         │       ▼
         │   TYPING (Mass Spectrometry / IHC)
         │       │
         │       ├── **AL (κ/λ)** → Serum FLC, Bone Marrow, Plasma Cell Disorder Workup
         │       ├── **AA** → Inflammatory Workup (ESR/CRP, Autoimmune Screen, Infection Screen)
         │       ├── **ATTR** → PYP Scan, Genetic Testing (TTR), Family History
         │       └── **OTHER** → Genetic Testing (ALECT2, ApoAI, Fibrinogen, Lysozyme)
         │
         └── **NEGATIVE** → Consider Other Diagnoses

3. Organ-Specific Manifestations (All Types)

OrganALAAATTR
Renal+++ (Nephrotic)+++ (Nephrotic)+ (Later)
Cardiac+++ (Restrictive CM)++++ (ATTRwt/ATTRv)
Neurological++ (Peripheral/Autonomic)Rare+++ (ATTRv/FAP)
Hepatic++ (Hepatomegaly)+++
GI++ (Macroglossia, Bleeding)++
Soft Tissue++ (Purpura, Shoulder Pad)Rare++ (Carpal Tunnel — ATTR)
Skin++ (Purpura)RareRare

3. Treatment Summary by Type

TypeFirst-LineSecond-Line / Advanced
ALBorotetomib-Based (CyBorD/Dara-CyBorD) → Auto-SCT (If Eligible)Daratumumab, CAR-T, Clinical Trials
AATreat Underlying Inflammation (TNF/IL-1/6 Inhibitors, Colchicine for FMF)—
ATTRv (Neuro)Patisiran / Inotersen / Vutrisiran (Gene Silencers)Liver Transplant (+ Cardiac)
ATTR (Cardiac)Tafamidis 61mg OD (1st Line)Diflunisal, Gene Silencers, Heart Transplant
ATTRwtTafamidisGene Silencers, Heart Transplant
ALLSupportive: Diuretics, ACEi/ARB (Cautious), Compression, Anticoagulation (Factor X), Palliative Care

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Amyloidosis DefinitionExtracellular Fibrillar Protein Deposition (β-Pleated Sheets) → Organ Dysfunction
ClassificationAL (Light Chain), AA (SAA), ATTR (Transthyretin) + Rare Types
AL AmyloidosisLight Chain (κ/λ); Plasma Cell Dyscrasia; 10-15% Myeloma
AA AmyloidosisSAA (Acute Phase); Chronic Inflammation (RA, FMF, TB, IBD)
ATTRvTTR Mutation (V30M, T60A); AD; FAP + Cardiomyopathy
ATTRwtWild-Type TTR; Elderly Males; Cardiomyopathy + Carpal Tunnel
Diagnosis Gold StandardTissue Biopsy + Congo Red → Apple-Green Birefringence + Typing (Mass Spec/IHC)
AL DiagnosisSerum FLC Ratio Abnormal; Bone Marrow Plasma Cells; Congo Red + IHC/Mass Spec
ATTR Cardiac DiagnosisPYP/DPD Scintigraphy (Grade 1-3 Uptake) → Non-Invasive Diagnosis
AL TreatmentBorotetomib-Based (CyBorD/Dara-CyBorD) → Auto-SCT (If Eligible)
AA TreatmentTreat Underlying Inflammation (TNF/IL-1/6 Blockers; Colchicine for FMF)
ATTRv NeuropathyGene Silencers: Patisiran (siRNA), Inotersen (ASO), Vutrisiran (siRNA)
ATTR CardiacTafamidis 61mg OD (1st Line); Diflunisal, Gene Silencers, Heart Transplant
PYP ScanATTR Cardiac: Grade 1-3 Uptake (Non-Invasive Diagnosis)
AL PrognosisStage I >10yr; Stage II ~5yr; Stage III ~2yr; Stage IV <1yr (Cardiac Biomarkers)
AA PrognosisBetter if Inflammation Controlled
AL CardiacRestrictive CM, Low Voltage ECG, Apical Sparing on MRI, Factor X Deficiency
AL RenalNephrotic Syndrome, Proteinuria >3.5g/d
ATTRwtElderly Males, Cardiomyopathy + Carpal Tunnel (Years Before)
TypingMass Spectrometry / IHC on Biopsy (Not Serum)
Congo RedApple-Green Birefringence = Amyloid
AL Factor X DeficiencyAdsorption to Amyloid → Bleeding Risk

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
AL vs AAAL = Light Chain (Plasma Cell); AA = SAA (Inflammation)
ATTRv vs ATTRwtATTRv = Genetic (TTR Mutation); ATTRwt = Age-Related (Wild-Type)
AL vs ATTR CardiacAL = Restrictive CM + Low Voltage ECG + Factor X Deficiency; ATTR = Thick Walls + Apical Sparing + Carpal Tunnel
TypingMass Spec / IHC on Biopsy (Not Serum); AL = κ/λ; AA = SAA; ATTR = TTR
PYP ScanATTR Cardiac = Grade 1-3; AL = Grade 0
AL vs AA RenalBoth = Nephrotic; AL = FLC Ratio Abnormal; AA = High CRP/ESR + Chronic Inflammation
ATTRv vs ATTRwt Carpal TunnelATTRv = Earlier/Younger; ATTRwt = Elderly Males, Years Before Cardiac
TafamidisTTR Stabiliser (1st Line ATTR Cardiac); Not for AL/AA
Gene SilencersPatisiran/Inotersen/Vutrisiran = ATTRv Neuropathy (Not Cardiac 1st Line)
Liver TransplantCurative for ATTRv (Stops Variant TTR Production)
Congo RedApple-Green Birefringence = Amyloid (Gold Standard)
Free Light ChainsAL = Abnormal κ/λ Ratio; Total FLC May Be Normal
AL Factor X DeficiencyAdsorption to Amyloid → Bleeding Risk
AA TriggerChronic Inflammation (RA, FMF, TB, IBD, Bronchiectasis)

A. Light chain deposition

B. AA deposition

C. TTR deposition

D. Abeta deposition

Answer: A

A. Chronic inflammation

B. Plasma cell dyscrasia (MGUS, MM)

C. Familial

D. Aging

Answer: B

  1. AA amyloidosis causes:

A. MGUS

B. Chronic inflammation (RA, IBD, TB)

C. Familial TTR

D. Dialysis

Answer: B

  1. ATTR amyloidosis:

A. AL

B. AA

C. Hereditary TTR

D. All

Answer: C

  1. Diagnosis gold standard:

A. Serum amyloid A

B. Congo red staining (apple-green birefringence)

C. Genetic testing

D. Imaging

Answer: B

  1. Typing of amyloid:

A. Congo red

B. Mass spectrometry/Immunohistochemistry

C. Serum

D. Imaging

Answer: B

  1. Cardiac involvement:

A. AL > ATTR

B. ATTR > AL

C. Both equal

D. Neither

Answer: A

  1. AL amyloidosis treatment:

A. Anti-plasma cell (chemo/ASCT)

B. Anti-TNF

C. Tafamidis

D. Supportive only

Answer: A

  1. ATTR-CM treatment:

A. Tafamidis

B. Doxycycline

C. Patisiran

D. All depending on type

Answer: D

  1. Renal amyloidosis:

A. Proteinuria/nephrotic syndrome

B. AKI

C. RPGN

D. UTI

Answer: A

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.1.2 Haemochromatosis
[!info]
Hereditary Haemochromatosis = Autosomal Recessive Iron Overload Disorder. HFE C282Y Homozygosity = 90% of Cases. Secondary Iron Overload (Transfusional, Ineffective Erythropoiesis). Venesection (Phlebotomy) = Gold Standard Treatment. Triad: Cirrhosis, Diabetes, Skin Pigmentation.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Diagnose HFE haemochromatosis using TSAT, Ferritin, and Genetic Testing
  • [ ] Differentiate primary (HFE) from secondary iron overload
  • [ ] Apply venesection protocol (induction → maintenance)
  • [ ] Recognise organ complications: cirrhosis, diabetes, cardiomyopathy, hypogonadism, arthropathy
  • [ ] Apply screening and surveillance for family members

2. Classification

TypeGeneFrequencyFeatures
Type 1 (HFE)HFE (C282Y Homozygous 90%; H63D Compound Het)90%Adult-Onset; Northern European Ancestry
Type 2A (Juvenile)HJV (Hepcidin Antimicrobial Peptide)RareSevere, Early-Onset (20); Cardiac/Endocrine
Type 2B (Juvenile)HAMP (Hepcidin)RareSimilar to Type 2A
Type 3TFR2 (Transferrin Receptor 2)RareIntermediate Severity
Type 4 (Ferroportin Disease)SLC40A1 (Ferroportin)RareAutosomal Dominant; Macrophage Iron Retention (High Ferritin, Normal/High TSAT)
SecondaryTransfusional, Ineffective Erythropoiesis (Thalassaemia, Sideroblastic)CommonAcquired; No Genetic Defect

2. Pathophysiology

StepMechanism
1. HFE Mutation (C282Y)↓ HFE-αβ2M Interaction → ↓ Hepcidin Expression
2. Low Hepcidin↓ Hepcidin → ↑ Ferroportin Activity (Enterocytes, Macrophages)
3. Increased Iron Absorption↑ Dietary Iron Absorption (No Feedback Inhibition)
4. Iron OverloadProgressive Deposition: Liver → Pancreas → Heart → Joints → Skin → Pituitary → Gonads
5. Organ DamageOxidative Stress (Fenton Reaction) → Fibrosis, Cell Death, Dysfunction

Hepcidin-Ferroportin Axis

ComponentNormal FunctionHaemochromatosis
HepcidinHormone from Liver → Binds Ferroportin → DegradationLow (HFE Mutation → ↓ Hepcidin Transcription)
FerroportinIron Exporter (Enterocytes, Macrophages, Hepatocytes)Unregulated (No Hepcidin → Ferroportin Stable on Membrane)
ResultIron Excretion = AbsorptionPositive Iron Balance → Accumulation

2. Clinical Presentation

Classic Triad (Late Presentation)

OrganManifestation
LiverCirrhosis (Most Common), Hepatomegaly, HCC (20-30% with Cirrhosis)
PancreasDiabetes Mellitus ("Bronze Diabetes") — 30-60%
SkinBronze/Grey Pigmentation (Melanin + Iron), Slate-Grey Colour

Systemic Manifestations

SystemManifestations
CardiacCardiomyopathy (Dilated/Restrictive), Heart Failure, Arrhythmias, Conduction Defects
EndocrineHypogonadotrophic Hypogonadism (Impotence, Loss of Libido, Amenorrhoea), Thyroid Dysfunction
JointsArthropathy (2nd/3rd MCP Joints — "Iron Hand"), Chondrocalcinosis (Pseudogout)
LiverHepatomegaly, Cirrhosis (50-70%), HCC (20-30% if Cirrhosis)
SkinBronze/Grey Pigmentation (Face, Hands, Genitals)

Age of Onset

PresentationTypical Age
Biochemical Iron Overload20-30 Years
Symptomatic Disease40-60 Years (Male Earlier Than Female)
Cirrhosis/Diabetes50-70 Years

2. Diagnosis

Biochemical Screening

TestNormalHaemochromatosis
Transferrin Saturation (TSAT)<45%>45% (Early Marker); >55% Strongly Suggestive
Serum Ferritin30-300 µg/L (M) / 15-200 µg/L (F)>300 (M) / >200 (F) µg/L (Iron Overload)
Liver Function TestsNormal↑ ALT/AST (If Hepatitis/Cirrhosis)
GlucoseNormalImpaired Fasting Glucose / Diabetes
HormonesNormal↓ Testosterone/Oestradiol, ↑ LH/FSH (Hypogonadotrophic Hypogonadism)

Genetic Testing (Confirmatory)

GenotypeFrequencySignificance
C282Y Homozygous90% of Clinical HaemochromatosisDiagnostic (Penetrance ~50% Biochemical, ~10-30% Clinical)
C282Y/H63D Compound Heterozygous~5%Mild Iron Overload (Lower Penetrance)
H63D HomozygousRareUsually No Significant Iron Overload
Non-HFE (HJV, HAMP, TFR2, SLC40A1)RareJuvenile, TFR2, Ferroportin Disease

Liver Iron Quantification

MethodIndicationNormal / Thresholds
MRI Liver (FerriScan / R2*)Non-Invasive QuantificationHIC >1.9 mg/g (Mild), >3.8 (Moderate), >7.0 (Severe) mg/g DW
Liver BiopsyIf Non-HFE / Ferritin >1000 / Diagnostic UncertaintyHIC >1.9 (Mild), >3.8 (Moderate), >7.0 (Severe) mg/g DW Hepatic Iron Index (HII) = HIC / Age

3. Management — Venesection (Phlebotomy)

Induction Phase

ParameterProtocol
Volume400-500 mL Whole Blood (≈200-250 mg Iron per Unit)
FrequencyWeekly / Biweekly
TargetFerritin 50-100 µg/L; TSAT <50%
DurationInduction: 1-2 Years (Weekly → Biweekly → Monthly)

Maintenance Phase

ParameterProtocol
Volume400-500 mL
FrequencyEvery 3-4 Months (Lifelong)
TargetFerritin 50-100 µg/L; TSAT <50%
MonitoringFerritin, TSAT, Hb q3-4mo

Iron Removal Calculation

ParameterValue
Iron per Unit Blood200-250 mg (1 Unit = 450-500mL; Hb ~14g/dL → 200-250 mg Fe)
Total Body Iron ExcessMen: 5-10g; Women: 3-5g
Time to De-Iron1-2 Years Weekly Phlebotomy

3. Contraindications / Alternatives to Venesection

ContraindicationAlternative
Anaemia (Hb <11 g/dL)Chelation (Deferasirox / Deferiprone / Deferoxamine)
Cardiac Failure (Low Output)Chelation
Poor Venous AccessChelation
Patient RefusalChelation

Chelation Therapy (Second-Line)

AgentDoseMonitoring
Deferasirox10-20 mg/kg/day ODRenal Function, LFTs, GI SE, Auditory/Ophthalmic
Deferiprone75 mg/kg/day TDSAgranulocytosis (Weekly FBC), Arthralgia, Zinc Deficiency
Deferoxamine30-50 mg/kg/day SC/IV (8-12h)Infusion Site Reactions, Ocular/Auditory Toxicity

3. Organ Complication Management

ComplicationManagement
CirrhosisStandard Care; HCC Surveillance (US q6mo if Cirrhosis)
DiabetesInsulin (Often Required); Standard DM Management
CardiomyopathyStandard HF Rx (ACEi, β-Blocker, MRA, SGLT2i, Loop Diuretic)
HypogonadismTestosterone / Oestrogen Replacement (If Symptomatic)
ArthropathyNSAIDs, Joint Replacement (If Severe)
HCCUS q6mo (If Cirrhosis); AFP Monitoring

3. Screening & Surveillance

Cascade Screening (Family Members)

RelativeTesting
1st-Degree (Siblings, Parents, Children)HFE Genotyping + TSAT + Ferritin
If C282Y HomozygousTSAT >45% + Ferritin >300 (M)/200 (F) = Biochemical Iron Overload
ChildrenTest at Age 18 (Unless Symptomatic Earlier)

Surveillance (Post-Diagnosis)

ParameterFrequency
Ferritin / TSATq3-4mo (Maintenance)
Liver Functionq6-12mo
Glucose / HbA1cq6-12mo
EchocardiogramAnnual (If Cardiomyopathy Suspected)
HCC SurveillanceUS q6mo (If Cirrhosis) + AFP q6mo
Bone DensityDEXA q2-3yr (Osteoporosis Risk)
EndocrineAnnual (Testosterone/Oestradiol, TSH, Prolactin)

3. Special Populations

Pregnancy

AspectManagement
VenesectionContinue if Ferritin >50 (Target 50-100 µg/L); Avoid if Anaemic
Iron SupplementationContraindicated (Excess Iron Harmful)
MonitoringFerritin, Hb, TSAT qTrimester
Genetic CounsellingOffer to Partner; Foetal Risk if Both Parents Carriers

Neonatal/Childhood

AspectManagement
ScreeningNot Routine (Adult-Onset); Test at 18 If Family History
Juvenile HaemochromatosisHJV/HAMP Mutations (Types 2A/2B); Severe, Early-Onset; Cardio/Endocrine Dominant

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Haemochromatosis GeneHFE C282Y Homozygous (90%); H63D Compound Het (5%)
TSAT>45% = Early Marker; >55% = Strongly Suggestive
Ferritin>300 (M) / >200 (F) µg/L = Iron Overload (Also Acute Phase Reactant)
GeneticsHFE C282Y Homozygous = 90%; Penetrance ~50% Biochemical, ~10-30% Clinical
Venesection400-500mL Weekly/Biweekly → Target Ferritin 50-100, TSAT <50%
Maintenance Venesection400-500mL q3-4mo (Lifelong); Target Ferritin 50-100, TSAT <50%
Iron per Unit200-250 mg Fe (1 Unit = 450-500mL)
C282Y Homozygous90% of Clinical HH; Penetrance ~50% Biochemical, ~10-30% Clinical
Type 4 (Ferroportin)AD; High Ferritin, Normal/High TSAT; Macrophage Iron Retention
Secondary Iron OverloadTransfusional (Thalassaemia, Sickle Cell); Ineffective Erythropoiesis
MRI Liver (FerriScan)HIC >1.9 (Mild), >3.8 (Mod), >7.0 (Severe) mg/g DW
HCC SurveillanceUS q6mo + AFP (If Cirrhosis)
CardiomyopathyDilated/Restrictive; Standard HF Rx (ACEi, β-Blocker, MRA, SGLT2i)
HypogonadismHypogonadotrophic; Testosterone/HRT Replacement
Arthropathy2nd/3rd MCP Joints ("Iron Hand"); Chondrocalcinosis (Pseudogout)
SkinBronze/Grey Pigmentation (Melanin + Iron Deposition)
Cardiac IronMRI T2 (Cardiac Iron); Chelation if T2 <20ms
Liver IronMRI R2* (FerriScan) / Biopsy HIC
Genetic TestingC282Y Homozygous = Diagnostic; H63D Compound Het = Mild

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Ferritin vs TSATTSAT = Early Marker (Rises First); Ferritin = Storage (Also Acute Phase Reactant)
HFE C282Y vs H63DC282Y Homozygous = 90% Clinical HH; H63D Compound Het = Mild, Low Penetrance
Ferritin in InflammationFerritin = Acute Phase Reactant (↑ in Infection, Liver Disease, Malignancy) → TSAT More Specific
Type 4 (Ferroportin)AD Inheritance; High Ferritin, Normal/High TSAT; Macrophage Iron Retention
Secondary Iron OverloadTransfusional (Thalassaemia, SCD), Ineffective Erythropoiesis (Sideroblastic)
Venesection TargetFerritin 50-100 µg/L; TSAT <50%
Iron per Unit200-250 mg Fe (1 Unit = 450-500mL Whole Blood)
Cardiac IronMRI T2 (Cardiac Iron); Chelation if T2 <20ms
Liver IronMRI R2* (FerriScan) or Biopsy HIC
Type 4 FerroportinAD; High Ferritin, Normal/High TSAT; Macrophage Iron Retention
Secondary Iron OverloadTransfusion, Ineffective Erythropoiesis
Venesection ContraindicatedAnaemia, Cardiac Failure, Poor Access → Chelation
C282Y Penetrance~50% Biochemical; ~10-30% Clinical Disease
Homozygous C282Y90% of HH; Test Family Members (Siblings 25% Risk)
MRI Liver IronFerriScan (R2*); HIC >1.9 Mild, >3.8 Mod, >7.0 Severe mg/g DW

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.1.3 Lipid Disorders
[!info]
Dyslipidaemia = Abnormal Lipid Profile → Atherosclerotic Cardiovascular Disease (ASCVD) Risk. ESC/EAS 2019 / NICE Guidelines Guide Targets. Statin 1st Line; Ezetimibe/PCSK9i Add-On. Familial Hypercholesterolaemia (FH) = Autosomal Dominant LDLR/APOB/PCSK9 Mutations.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Classify dyslipidaemia (Fredrickson/WHO) and interpret lipid profile
  • [ ] Apply ESC/EAS 2019 LDL-C targets by cardiovascular risk category
  • [ ] Prescribe statin therapy (intensity selection, monitoring, adverse effects)
  • [ ] Apply add-on therapy: Ezetimibe → PCSK9 inhibitors → Bempedoic Acid
  • [ ] Diagnose and manage Familial Hypercholesterolaemia (FH)
  • [ ] Manage severe hypertriglyceridaemia and pancreatitis prevention

2. Classification & Lipid Profile Interpretation

Fredrickson/WHO Classification

TypeLipid AbnormalityTypical Pattern
Type IIaIsolated ↑ LDL-CFamilial Hypercholesterolaemia (FH)
Type IIb↑ LDL-C + ↑ TGCombined Hyperlipidaemia
Type III↑ IDL (β-VLDL)Dysbetalipoproteinaemia (ApoE2/E2)
Type IV↑ TG (VLDL), Normal LDL, ↓ HDLMetabolic Syndrome, Obesity, T2DM
Type V↑↑ TG (Chylomicrons + VLDL)Severe Hypertriglyceridaemia (Pancreatitis Risk)

Standard Lipid Profile (Fasting 8-12h)

ParameterOptimal / TargetHigh Risk / Action
Total Cholesterol<5.0 mmol/L>5.0
LDL-C<1.8 (Very High Risk) / <2.6 (High Risk) / <3.0 (Moderate)Per Risk Category
HDL-C>1.0 (M) / >1.2 (F)<1.0 (M) / <1.2 (F)
Triglycerides<1.7 mmol/L1.7-2.3 (Borderline); >2.3 (High)
Non-HDL-C<2.6 (Very High Risk) / <3.4 (High Risk)Secondary Target
ApoB<80 mg/dL (Very High Risk)Alternative to LDL-C
TC/HDL Ratio<4.0>5.0 (High Risk)

2. Cardiovascular Risk Categories & LDL-C Targets (ESC/EAS 2019)

Risk CategoryCriteriaLDL-C TargetLDL-C Reduction
Very High RiskEstablished ASCVD, Diabetes + Target Organ Damage, CKD eGFR<30, FH<1.4 mmol/L (55 mg/dL)≥50% Reduction
High RiskDiabetes (no target organ), CKD eGFR 30-59, 10yr CVD Risk ≥10%, Markedly Elevated Single Risk Factor<1.8 mmol/L (70 mg/dL)≥50% Reduction
Moderate Risk10yr CVD Risk 5-10%<2.6 mmol/L (100 mg/dL)—
Low Risk10yr CVD Risk <5%<3.0 mmol/L (115 mg/dL)—
Non-HDL-C Target = LDL-C Target + 0.8 mmol/L (30 mg/dL)

2. Statin Therapy — Intensity & Selection

IntensityStatins & DosesExpected LDL-C ReductionIndication
High-IntensityAtorvastatin 40-80mg / Rosuvastatin 20-40mg≥50%Very High / High Risk (1st Line)
Moderate-IntensityAtorvastatin 10-20mg / Rosuvastatin 5-10mg / Simvastatin 20-40mg30-49%Moderate Risk / Intolerance to High-Intensity
Low-IntensitySimvastatin 10mg / Pravastatin 10-20mg / Fluvastatin 20-40mg<30%Low Risk / Elderly / Drug Interactions

Statin Choice by Clinical Scenario

ScenarioPreferred Statin
High CVD Risk / FHAtorvastatin 40-80mg / Rosuvastatin 20-40mg
CKD (eGFR <30)Atorvastatin (No Dose Adjustment) / Rosuvastatin (Max 10mg)
Statin IntoleranceTry Alternative Statin → Ezetimibe → PCSK9i → Bempedoic Acid
Drug Interactions (CYP3A4 Inhibitors)Rosuvastatin / Pravastatin (Minimal CYP3A4)
Asian EthnicityRosuvastatin (Lower Dose 5-10mg Often Sufficient)
Check Baseline: LFTs, CK (If >5x ULN → Do Not Start), Renal Function.

2. Add-On Therapy (If Target Not Met on Max Tolerated Statin)

Add-On AgentDoseLDL-C ReductionIndication
Ezetimibe10mg OD15-20%1st Add-On (If Statin Max Tolerated / Intolerant)
PCSK9 InhibitorEvolocumab 140mg SC q2wk / Alirocumab 75-150mg SC q2wk50-60%2nd Add-On (Very High Risk, FH, Statin Intolerant)
Bempedoic Acid180mg OD15-25%Statin Intolerant (No Myopathy Risk)
Fibrates (Fenofibrate 145mg)145mg ODTG ↓30-50%, HDL ↑10-15%If TG >2.3 mmol/L (Combined with Statin)
Omega-3 Fatty Acids2-4g/day (EPA/DHA)TG ↓20-30%Adjunct for Severe HyperTG

Treatment Algorithm (ESC/EAS)

MAX TOLERATED STATIN
         │
         ├── LDL-C AT TARGET → CONTINUE
         │
         └── LDL-C ABOVE TARGET
                 │
                 ├── ADD EZETIMIBE 10mg OD
                 │       ├── AT TARGET → CONTINUE
                 │       └── NOT AT TARGET (Very High Risk / FH)
                 │               → ADD PCSK9 INHIBITOR
                 │                       (Evolocumab / Alirocumab)
                 │
                 ├── IF STATIN INTOLERANT
                 │       → EZETIMIBE 1st → BEMPEODOIC ACID → PCSK9 INHIBITOR
                 │
                 └── TG >2.3 mmol/L (Despite Statin ± Ezetimibe)
                         → ADD FENOFIBRATE 145mg OD / OMEGA-3 2-4g/d

3. Familial Hypercholesterolaemia (FH)

Genetics & Classification

TypeGeneticsFrequencyLDL-C LevelClinical Features
Heterozygous FH (HeFH)LDLR (85-90%), APOB, PCSK91:250>4.9 mmol/L (Adults), >4.0 (Children)Tendon Xanthomas, Corneal Arcus, Premature CVD
Homozygous FH (HoFH)2 Mutant Alleles (LDLR/APOB/PCSK9)1:300,000>13 mmol/LPlanar Xanthomas, Aortic Valve Disease, Childhood CVD

Diagnostic Criteria

SystemCriteria
Dutch Lipid Clinic Network (DLCN)Points-Based: Family History, Personal History, LDL-C, Tendon Xanthomas, Corneal Arcus, DNA Testing. ≥8 = Definite FH; 6-8 = Probable; 3-5 = Possible
Simon BroomeDefinite FH: LDL-C >4.9 (Adult) + Tendon Xanthomas OR DNA Mutation; Possible FH: LDL-C >4.9 + Family/Personal History

Management of FH

ScenarioManagement
HeFHHigh-Intensity Statin + Ezetimibe → PCSK9 Inhibitor (If Target Not Met)
HoFHStatin + Ezetimibe + PCSK9i → Lipid Apheresis (Regular, Lifelong) → Liver Transplant (Rare)
Cascade Screening1st-Degree Relatives → LDL-C + Genetic Testing (If Mutation Known)
ChildrenStatin from Age 8-10 (If LDL-C >4.0); PCSK9i from Age 12 (If Needed)

3. Severe Hypertriglyceridaemia (TG >10 mmol/L / 880 mg/dL)

SeverityTG LevelRiskManagement
Moderate2.3-10 mmol/LCVD RiskFibrates, Omega-3, Optimise Statin, Treat Secondary Causes
Severe>10 mmol/LAcute PancreatitisEmergency: Insulin Infusion, Heparin, Plasmapheresis, Fibrates, Omega-3

Aetiology of Severe HyperTG

Primary (Genetic)Secondary (Acquired)
Familial Chylomicronaemia (LPL, ApoC-II, ApoA-V, GPIHBP1)Uncontrolled Diabetes
Familial Combined HyperlipidaemiaAlcohol Excess
Obesity / Metabolic Syndrome
Hypothyroidism
Drugs (Oestrogen, Tamoxifen, Retinoids, Protease Inhibitors, Beta-Blockers, Thiazides)
Nephrotic Syndrome
Pregnancy

Emergency Management (TG >10 mmol/L / Pancreatitis)

StepAction
1. IV InsulinInsulin Infusion 0.1U/kg/h + D5W (Promotes LPL Activity)
2. Heparin50-100U/kg IV Bolus → 10-20U/kg/h (Releases LPL)
3. PlasmapheresisIf TG >20 mmol/L or Refractory Pancreatitis
4. FibratesFenofibrate 145mg OD (After Acute Phase)
5. Omega-32-4g/day EPA/DHA (Adjunct)
6. Treat UnderlyingGlycaemic Control, Alcohol Cessation, Drug Review

3. Statin Adverse Effects & Monitoring

Adverse EffectIncidenceManagement
Myopathy (CK >5x ULN + Symptoms)<0.1% (Rhabdo <0.01%)Stop Statin; Check CK; Rechallenge Lower Dose/Alternative
Asymptomatic CK Rise0.5-2% (CK 5-10x ULN)Continue if <5x ULN; Reduce Dose if 5-10x; Stop if >10x
New-Onset DiabetesSlight ↑ Risk (High-Dose)Monitor HbA1c; Benefit >> Risk in High CVD Risk
HepatotoxicityALT/AST >3x ULNReduce/Stop if >3x ULN Persistent
Drug InteractionsCYP3A4 Inhibitors (Clarithromycin, Azoles, Grapefruit)Avoid Simvastatin/Lovastatin >20mg; Use Rosuvastatin/Pravastatin

3. Monitoring Schedule

ParameterBaseline3 Months12 MonthsOngoing
Lipid Profile✅✅ (Check Target)✅Annual
LFTs✅✅ (If ↑ Baseline)✅Annual
CKIf SymptomaticIf SymptomaticIf SymptomaticIf Myalgia
HbA1c✅—✅Annual (Statin → Slight ↑ Diabetes Risk)
Renal Function✅—✅Annual

Statin IntoleranceTry Alternate Statin → Ezetimibe → PCSK9i → Bempedoic Acid
CK Monitoring>5x ULN → Stop; 5-10x → Reduce Dose; >10x → Stop

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Primary vs Secondary Prevention TargetsVery High Risk (ASCVD) = <1.4; High Risk = <1.8; Moderate = <2.6
Statin IntoleranceTry 3 Different Statins → Ezetimibe → PCSK9i → Bempedoic Acid
PCSK9i vs EzetimibePCSK9i = -50-60% LDL (Injectable); Ezetimibe = -15-20% (Oral, 1st Add-On)
Fibrate + StatinOnly if TG >2.3; Fenofibrate Preferred (Less CYP Interaction)
Bempedoic AcidATP-Citrate Lyase Inhibitor; No Myopathy Risk; Statin-Intolerant
HoFHLDL >13; Planar Xanthomas; Lipid Apheresis + PCSK9i + Liver Transplant
FH DiagnosisDLCN ≥8 = Definite; Simon Broome: LDL >4.9 + Tendon Xanthoma
TG >10 mmol/LEmergency: Insulin Infusion + Heparin + Plasmapheresis
Statin + FibrateOnly If TG >2.3; Fenofibrate Preferred (Less Interaction)
Bempedoic AcidATP-Citrate Lyase Inhibitor; No Myopathy; Statin-Intolerant
Rosuvastatin in CKDeGFR <30 → Max 10mg; Atorvastatin Preferred (No Dose Adjust)
FH DiagnosisDLCN ≥8 Definite; DNA Confirmation if Available
Statin-Induced DiabetesSmall ↑ Risk (High Dose); Benefit >> Risk in High CVD Risk
PCSK9i DoseEvolocumab 140mg q2wk; Alirocumab 75-150mg q2wk

9. Mind Map

Lipid Disorders
Classification
Type IIa: ↑LDL (FH)
Type IIb: ↑LDL + ↑TG
Type III: ↑IDL (Dysbetalipoproteinaemia)
Type IV: ↑TG, ↓HDL (Metabolic Syndrome)
Type V: ↑↑TG (Chylomicrons)
Targets (ESC 2019)
Very High Risk: LDL <1.4 (50%↓)
High Risk: LDL <1.8 (50%↓)
Moderate: LDL <2.6
Low: LDL <3.0
Statin Intensity
High: Atorva 40-80 / Rosuva 20-40 (1st Line High Risk)
Moderate: Atorva 10-20 / Rosuva 5-10
Low: Simva 10 / Pravastatin 10-20
Add-On
1st: Ezetimibe 10mg (15-20%↓)
2nd: PCSK9i (Evolocumab/Alirocumab) 50-60%↓
Adjunct: Bempedoic Acid (Statin-Intolerant)
Fibrates: TG>2.3 (Fenofibrate); Omega-3
FH
HeFH 1:250 (LDLR/APOB/PCSK9)
HoFH: 1:300k; LDL>13; Apheresis
DLCN ≥8 = Definite
Cascade Screening
Severe HyperTG
>10 mmol/L → Pancreatitis Risk

TopicKey Point

Rosuvastatin in CKDeGFR<30 → Max 10mg; Atorvastatin No Adjust

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.1.4 Obesity And Metabolic Syndrome
[!info]
Obesity = Chronic Relapsing Disease with Excess Adiposity → Metabolic Dysfunction. Metabolic Syndrome = Cluster of Cardiometabolic Risk Factors (Central Obesity + ≥2 of: TG↑, HDL↓, BP↑, Glucose↑). BMI ≥30 = Obesity; BMI ≥25 = Overweight.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Diagnose obesity (BMI, waist circumference) and metabolic syndrome (IDF/ATP III criteria)
  • [ ] Apply management pyramid: Lifestyle → Pharmacotherapy → Bariatric Surgery
  • [ ] Prescribe anti-obesity medications (GLP-1 RA, Orlistat, Naltrexone/Bupropion, Phentermine/Topiramate)
  • [ ] Apply bariatric surgery criteria and post-op monitoring
  • [ ] Manage cardiometabolic risk factors in metabolic syndrome

2. Definitions & Classification

BMI Classification (WHO)

CategoryBMI (kg/m²)Risk of Comorbidities
Underweight<18.5Low (but ↑ other risks)
Normal18.5-24.9Average
Overweight25.0-29.9Increased
Obese Class I30.0-34.9Moderate
Obese Class II35.0-39.9Severe
Obese Class III≥40.0Very Severe

Waist Circumference (Central Obesity)

PopulationMaleFemale
Europid≥102 cm≥88 cm
South Asian / Asian≥90 cm≥80 cm
Japanese≥85 cm≥90 cm

2. Metabolic Syndrome — Diagnostic Criteria

IDF Criteria (2005) — Central Obesity + ≥2 of 4

ComponentThreshold
Central ObesityWaist ≥94 cm (M) / ≥80 cm (F) (Europid)
Triglycerides≥1.7 mmol/L (150 mg/dL) or on Rx
HDL-Cholesterol<1.03 mmol/L (M) / <1.29 mmol/L (F) or on Rx
Blood Pressure≥130/85 mmHg or on Rx
Fasting Glucose≥5.6 mmol/L (100 mg/dL) or on Rx

ATP III / NCEP Criteria (2001) — ≥3 of 5

ComponentThreshold
Waist>102 cm (M) / >88 cm (F)
Triglycerides≥1.7 mmol/L
HDL-C<1.03 mmol/L (M) / <1.29 mmol/L (F)
BP≥130/85 mmHg
Fasting Glucose≥5.6 mmol/L
Central Obesity is Mandatory in IDF; Not Mandatory but Counted in ATP III.

2. Aetiology & Pathophysiology

FactorMechanism
Positive Energy BalanceCaloric Intake > Expenditure → Adipocyte Hypertrophy/Hyperplasia
Insulin ResistanceVisceral Adipose → ↑ FFA → Hepatic IR → Hyperinsulinaemia → Lipogenesis
Adipokine Dysregulation↓ Adiponectin, ↑ Leptin (Resistance), ↑ TNF-α, ↑ IL-6 → Inflammation
Sympathetic OveractivityHyperinsulinaemia → SNS Activation → Hypertension
GeneticsPolygenic (FTO, MC4R, etc.); Monogenic (Leptin/Leptin Receptor Deficiency)
EnvironmentSedentary Lifestyle, Ultra-Processed Foods, Sleep Deprivation, Stress

2. Clinical Complications

SystemComplications
CardiovascularCoronary Artery Disease, Heart Failure (HFpEF), Atrial Fibrillation, Stroke, PAD
MetabolicType 2 Diabetes, Dyslipidaemia, NAFLD/NASH, Gout, PCOS
RespiratoryObstructive Sleep Apnoea, Obesity Hypoventilation Syndrome, Asthma
MusculoskeletalOsteoarthritis (Knee, Hip), Low Back Pain, Gout
GI/HepaticNAFLD/NASH, Gallstones, GERD, Reflux, Pancreatitis
ReproductivePCOS, Infertility, Menstrual Irregularity, Erectile Dysfunction
OncologicalEndometrial, Breast, Colorectal, Oesophageal, Renal, Pancreatic, HCC
PsychosocialDepression, Anxiety, Stigma, Poor Quality of Life
OtherDyslipidaemia, Hypertension, T2DM, CKD, Venous Thromboembolism

2. Management Algorithm — Pyramid Approach

OBESITY / METABOLIC SYNDROME DIAGNOSED
         │
         └──► LIFESTYLE INTERVENTION (Foundation — All Patients)
                   │
                   ├── Diet: 600 kcal/d Deficit (Low Fat/Cal, Mediterranean, Low GI)
                   ├── Exercise: 150-300 min/wk Moderate + Resistance 2x/wk
                   ├── Behavioural: CBT, Self-Monitoring, Goal Setting
                   └── Target: **5-10% Weight Loss at 6mo** (Improves Metabolic Parameters)
         │
         ├── PHARMACOTHERAPY (BMI ≥30 or ≥27 + Comorbidity)
         │   ├── **GLP-1 RA** (1st Line Pharmacotherapy)
         │   │       ├── **Semaglutide 2.4mg SC Weekly** (>15% wt loss)
         │   │       ├── **Liraglutide 3.0mg SC Daily** (~8% wt loss)
         │   │       └── **Dulaglutide 1.5-4.5mg Weekly** (Lower Doses Approved)
         │   │
         │   ├── **SGLT2i + GLP-1 RA** (Tirzepatide — Dual GIP/GLP-1)
         │   │       └── **Tirzepatide 15mg SC Weekly** (>20% wt loss)
         │   │
         │   ├── ORAL AGENTS (If GLP-1 Contraindicated/Intolerant)
         │   │       ├── **Orlistat 120mg TDS** (Lipase Inhibitor; GI SE)
         │   │       ├── **Naltrexone/Bupropion** 32/360mg BD (Craving ↓; Nausea, Seizure Risk)
         │   │       └── **Phentermine/Topiramate** (Appetite Suppression; Tachycardia, Teratogenic)
         │   │
         │   └── MONITOR: Weight q4wk; 5% wt loss at 3mo → Continue; <5% → Switch/Stop
         │
         └── BARIATRIC SURGERY (BMI ≥40 or ≥35 + Comorbidity)
                 ├── **Sleeve Gastrectomy** (Most Common; Restrictive)
                 ├── **RYGB** (Roux-en-Y; Restrictive + Malabsorptive)
                 ├── **OAGB** (One-Anastomosis Gastric Bypass)
                 └── POST-OP: Nutritional Monitoring (Fe, B12, D, Ca), 25-OH D, PTH, LFTs

3. Pharmacotherapy — Detailed

GLP-1 Receptor Agonists (1st Line)

AgentDoseWeight LossKey Adverse Effects
Semaglutide 2.4mg0.25mg → 0.5 → 1.0 → 1.7 → 2.4mg SC Weekly (Escalate q4wk)15-17%Nausea, Vomiting, Diarrhoea, Pancreatitis Risk
Liraglutide 3.0mg0.6mg → 1.2 → 1.8 → 2.4 → 3.0mg SC Daily8-10%Nausea, Pancreatitis Risk, Thyroid C-Cell Tumours (Rodent)
Dulaglutide0.75-4.5mg SC Weekly~5-10% (Dose-Dependent)Similar GI Profile

Dual GIP/GLP-1 RA

AgentDoseWeight LossStatus
Tirzepatide2.5 → 5 → 7.5 → 10 → 15mg SC Weekly>20%Approved (Mounjaro®)

Other Oral Agents (If GLP-1 Contraindicated)

AgentDoseMechanismWeight LossKey SE
Orlistat120mg TDS with MealsLipase Inhibitor3-5%Steatorrhoea, Fat-Soluble Vitamin Deficiency
Naltrexone/Bupropion32/360mg BD (Titrate)Opioid Antagonist + NDRI5-8%Nausea, Seizure Risk, BP ↑
Phentermine/Topiramate3.75/23 → 15/92mg ODAppetite Suppression10-12%Tachycardia, Teratogenic, Depression
SetmelanotideMC4R AgonistRare Monogenic Obesity (POMC, LEPR, PCSK1)—Injection Site, Skin Hyperpigmentation

3. Bariatric Surgery

ProcedureMechanismWeight LossRemission T2DM
Sleeve GastrectomyRestrictive (80% Stomach Removed)60-70% EWL60-80%
RYGB (Roux-en-Y)Restrictive + Malabsorptive70-80% EWL80-90%
OAGB (One-Anastomosis)Restrictive + MalabsorptiveSimilar to RYGBSimilar
Adjustable Gastric BandRestrictive (Adjustable)40-50% EWLLower; Declining Use

Surgical Criteria (NICE / IFSO)

BMIComorbidityEligibility
≥40NoneEligible
35-39.9≥1 Obesity-Related Comorbidity (T2DM, HTN, OSA, etc.)Eligible
30-34.9T2DM (Recent Onset)Consider (NICE: BMI 30-35 + T2DM)

3. Post-Operative Monitoring

ParameterFrequency
Weight / BMIMonthly ×6mo, Then q3-6mo
Nutritional Labsq3mo ×1yr, Then q6-12mo: Fe, Ferritin, B12, Folate, Vit D, Ca, PTH, Albumin, LFTs
Bone DensityDEXA at 1yr, Then q2-3yr
Glucose/HbA1cq3mo (T2DM Remission Monitoring)
Medication ReviewDe-escalate DM/HTN/Lipid Rx as Weight Loss Occurs

3. Metabolic Syndrome Management

ComponentTarget
Weight Loss5-10% (Improves All Components)
Blood Pressure<130/80 (ACEi/ARB 1st Line)
LipidsStatin if CVD Risk >10%; Fenofibrate if TG >2.3
GlucoseMetformin if Pre-DM/T2DM; GLP-1/SGLT2i if T2DM
LifestyleMediterranean Diet, 150min/wk Exercise, Smoking Cessation

TopicKey Point
Obesity BMI≥30 kg/m² (Class I 30-34.9, II 35-39.9, III ≥40)
Waist CircumferenceMale ≥102cm / Female ≥88cm (Europid); Lower for Asian
Metabolic Syndrome (IDF)Central Obesity + ≥2 of 4: TG↑, HDL↓, BP↑, Glucose↑
Metabolic Syndrome (ATP III)≥3 of 5: Waist, TG↑, HDL↓, BP↑, Glucose↑
1st Line PharmacotherapyGLP-1 RA (Semaglutide 2.4mg / Liraglutide 3.0mg)
Semaglutide Dose0.25 → 0.5 → 1.0 → 1.7 → 2.4mg SC Weekly (Escalate q4wk)
TirzepatideDual GIP/GLP-1; 15mg Weekly → >20% Weight Loss
Orlistat120mg TDS (Lipase Inhibitor); Steatorrhoea SE
Naltrexone/Bupropion32/360mg BD; Nausea, Seizure Risk
Phentermine/TopiramateAppetite Suppression; Teratogenic (Contraception Mandatory)
Bariatric SurgeryBMI ≥40 or ≥35 + Comorbidity; Sleeve Gastrectomy Most Common
T2DM Remission Post-SurgerySleeve 60-80%; RYGB 80-90%
Post-Op MonitoringFe, B12, D, Ca, PTH q3mo ×1yr; DEXA at 1yr
Metabolic Syndrome RxWeight Loss 5-10% → Improves All Components
GLP-1 RA SENausea, Vomiting, Pancreatitis, Thyroid C-Cell Tumours (Rodent)
BMI ClassificationOverweight 25-29.9; Obese I 30-34.9; II 35-39.9; III ≥40

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
IDF vs ATP III MetSynIDF: Central Obesity Mandatory; ATP III: ≥3 of 5 (No Mandatory)
MetSyn vs ObesityMetSyn = Cluster of Risk Factors; Obesity = BMI ≥30 (Can Coexist)
GLP-1 RA vs SGLT2i for WeightGLP-1 RA > SGLT2i for Weight Loss; Tirzepatide > Semaglutide
Tirzepatide vs SemaglutideTirzepatide = Dual GIP/GLP-1 → >20% vs ~15%
Orlistat vs GLP-1Orlistat = Lipase Inhibitor (Less Effective, GI SE); GLP-1 = Hormonal (More Effective)
Bariatric CriteriaBMI ≥40 or ≥35 + Comorbidity; NICE: BMI 30-35 + T2DM
BMI vs WCBMI = General Adiposity; WC = Central/Visceral Adiposity (Better CV Predictor)
Weight Loss Target5-10% at 6mo (Clinically Meaningful)
T2DM RemissionRYGB > Sleeve > Band; Remission >80% in RYGB
GLP-1 RA ContraindicationsPersonal/Family MTC, MEN2, Pregnancy, Severe GI Disease

9. Mind Map

Obesity & Metabolic Syndrome
Definitions
BMI ≥30 = Obesity; 25-29.9 = Overweight
WC: M≥102/F≥88 (Europid)
MetSyn: IDF (Central Obesity + ≥2) / ATP III (≥3 of 5)
Aetiology
Energy Imbalance + Insulin Resistance + Adipokine Dysregulation
Genetics (FTO, MC4R) + Environment
Complications
CV: CAD, HF, AF, Stroke
Metabolic: T2DM, NAFLD, Dyslipidaemia
Resp: OSA, OHS, Asthma
MSK: OA, Gout
Cancer: Endometrial, Breast, Colorectal
Psych: Depression, Stigma
Management Pyramid
1. Lifestyle (Diet 600kcal def, Exercise 150min, Behavioural)
2. Pharmacotherapy (BMI≥30 or ≥27+Comorb)
– GLP-1 RA: Semaglutide 2.4mg (1st), Liraglutide 3.0mg
– Dual GIP/GLP-1: Tirzepatide 15mg (>20% wt loss)
– Oral: Orlistat, Naltrexone/Bupropion, Phentermine/Topiramate
3. Bariatric Surgery (BMI≥40 or ≥35+Comorbidity)
– Sleeve > RYGB > OAGB
Metabolic Syndrome
IDF: Central Obesity + ≥2 (TG↑, HDL↓, BP↑, Gluc↑)
ATP III: ≥3/5 (Waist, TG, HDL, BP, Gluc)
Rx: Wt Loss 5-10% → Improves All Components
Surgery
Sleeve (Most Common, Restrictive)
RYGB (Restrictive+Malabsorptive, Best T2DM Remission)
Post-Op: Nutritional Monitoring (Fe, B12, D, Ca, PTH)
Monitoring
Weight q4wk; 5% at 3mo → Continue
Post-Bariatric: Fe, B12, D, Ca, PTH q3mo; DEXA 1yr

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.1.5 Porphyria
[!info]
Porphyrias = Group of Rare Metabolic Disorders due to Enzyme Defects in Haem Biosynthesis. Acute Hepatic Porphyrias (Neurovisceral Attacks) vs Cutaneous Porphyrias (Photoactive). PBG/ALA = Diagnostic Hallmark in Acute Attack.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Classify porphyrias into acute hepatic vs cutaneous
  • [ ] Recognise acute porphyria attack: abdominal pain, neuropathy, psychiatric, hyponatraemia
  • [ ] Apply diagnostic criteria: PBG/ALA elevation (Gold Standard)
  • [ ] Manage acute attack: Haemarginate, IV Glucose, Avoid Precipitants
  • [ ] Recognise cutaneous porphyrias: PCT, EPP, CEP, XLEPP
  • [ ] Apply drug precautions (Safe vs Unsafe drugs)

2. Classification

Acute Hepatic Porphyrias (Neurovisceral)

TypeEnzyme DefectGeneInheritanceKey Features
AIP (Acute Intermittent Porphyria)HMBS (Hydroxymethylbilane Synthase)HMBSADMost Common Acute; Neurovisceral (No Skin)
VP (Variegate Porphyria)PPOX (Protoporphyrinogen Oxidase)PPOXADAcute + Cutaneous (Photosensitivity)
HCP (Hereditary Coproporphyria)CPOX (Coproporphyrinogen Oxidase)CPOXADAcute + Cutaneous (Milder)
ADP (ALAD Deficiency Porphyria)ALAD (ALA Dehydratase)ALADARUltra-Rare; Severe Infantile Onset

Cutaneous Porphyrias (Photoactive)

TypeEnzyme DefectGeneInheritanceKey Features
PCT (Porphyria Cutanea Tarda)UROD (Uroporphyrinogen Decarboxylase)URODAD (80%) / Sporadic (20%)Most Common Cutaneous; Blisters, Scarring, Hypertrichosis
EPP (Erythropoietic Protoporphyria)FECH (Ferrochelatase)FECHARPainful Photosensitivity (Immediate Burning); Liver Risk
CEP (Congenital Erythropoietic Porphyria)UROS (Uroporphyrinogen III Synthase)UROSARSevere Photosensitivity (Infancy); Red Urine, Deformities
XLEPP (X-Linked EPP)ALAS2ALAS2XLSimilar to EPP; Higher Liver Risk

2. Haem Biosynthesis Pathway & Enzyme Defects

Glycine + Succinyl-CoA
      │
      ▼
ALA Synthase (ALAS) ← **Rate-Limiting** (Repressed by Haem)
      │
      ▼
δ-Aminolaevulinic Acid (ALA)
      │
      ▼
**ALA Dehydratase (ALAD)** → **ADP** (AR)
      │
      ▼
Porphobilinogen (PBG)
      │
      ▼
**PBG Deaminase (HMBS)** → **AIP** (AD)
      │
      ▼
Hydroxymethylbilane
      │
      ▼
Uroporphyrinogen III Synthase (UROS) → **CEP** (AR)
      │
      ▼
Uroporphyrinogen III
      │
      ▼
**Uroporphyrinogen Decarboxylase (UROD)** → **PCT** (AD/Sporadic)
      │
      ▼
Coproporphyrinogen III
      │
      ▼
**Coproporphyrinogen Oxidase (CPOX)** → **HCP** (AD)
      │
      ▼
Protoporphyrinogen IX
      │
      ▼
**Protoporphyrinogen Oxidase (PPOX)** → **VP** (AD)
      │
      ▼
Protoporphyrin IX
      │
      ▼
**Ferrochelatase (FECH)** → **EPP/XLEPP** (AR/XL)
      │
      ▼
**HAEM** (Inserted into Globin / Cytochromes)

2. Acute Porphyria Attack — Clinical Features

SystemFeatures
AbdominalSevere Colicky Pain (Most Common), Nausea, Vomiting, Constipation, Ileus
NeurologicalPeripheral Neuropathy (Motor > Sensory), Quadriparesis, Areflexia, Cranial Nerve Palsies
PsychiatricAnxiety, Agitation, Confusion, Hallucinations, Depression, Seizures
AutonomicTachycardia, Hypertension, Flushing, Sweating, Postural Hypotension
ElectrolytesHyponatraemia (SIADH), Hypokalaemia, Hypomagnesaemia
SkinAbsent in AIP/ADP; Present in VP/HCP (Photosensitivity, Blisters)

Acute Attack Precipitants (Avoid in All Porphyrias!)

Drug ClassExamples
Barbiturates (Thiopental, Phenobarbital)Strong Inducers (↑ ALAS1)
SulfonamidesCo-trimoxazole, Sulfasalazine
RifampicinPotent Inducer
AntiepilepticsPhenytoin, Carbamazepine, Valproate, Phenobarbital, Ethosuximide
HormonalOestrogen (OCP), Progesterone, Androgens, Corticosteroids
AnaestheticsThiopental, Enflurane (Some); Safe: Propofol, Etomidate, Ketamine, Sevoflurane
OtherAlcohol (Acute), Fasting/Starvation, Infection, Surgery, Stress

2. Diagnosis — Biochemical (Gold Standard)

Acute Attack

TestFindingSignificance
Urine PBG (Quantitative)↑↑↑ (Acute Attack)Gold Standard Screening
Urine ALA↑↑Supports Diagnosis
Urine Total Porphyrins↑ (Coproporphyrin, Uroporphyrin)Supports Diagnosis
Faecal Porphyrins↑ Copro / Uro (VP/HCP Differentiation)Type Differentiation
Plasma FluorescencePeak ~625nm (VP/HCP)Cutaneous Porphyrias
Enzyme AssayHMBS (AIP), PPOX (VP), CPOX (HCP), ALAD (ADP)Confirmatory
Genetic TestingMutation IDConfirmatory; Family Screening

Biochemical Profile by Type

TypeUrine PBGUrine ALAUrine PorphyrinsFaecal PorphyrinsSkin
AIP↑↑↑↑↑↑ Uro/CoproNormalNone
VP↑↑↑↑↑ Uro/Copro↑ Proto + CoproPhotosensitivity
HCP↑↑↑↑↑ Copro > Uro↑ Copro IIIPhotosensitivity (Milder)
ADPNormal/↑↑↑↑↑ ALANormalNone
PCTNormalNormal↑ Uro (Carboxylic)↑ Iso-CoproBlisters, Fragility
EPPNormalNormalNormal↑ ProtoImmediate Burning Pain

2. Acute Attack Management

1. IMMEDIATE: STOP PRECIPITATING DRUGS

Drug Classes to STOPExamples
BarbituratesThiopental, Phenobarbital
SulfonamidesCo-trimoxazole, Sulfasalazine
Rifampicin
AntiepilepticsPhenytoin, Carbamazepine, Valproate, Phenobarbital
HormonesOCP, Progesterone, Androgens
Certain AnaestheticsThiopental, Enflurane

2. SPECIFIC THERAPY

AgentDoseMechanism
Haemarginate3-4 mg/kg IV Daily × 4 DaysReplenishes Haem Pool → Represses ALAS1 (Rate-Limiting Enzyme)
IV Glucose300-400g/day (5-10% Dextrose)Represses ALAS1 (Insulin-Mediated)
IV HaeminAlternative to Haemarginate (3-4 mg/kg)Same as Haemarginate

3. SUPPORTIVE CARE

IssueManagement
PainOpioids (Morphine, Fentanyl — Safe); Avoid NSAIDs (Renal), Pethidine (Seizure Risk)
Nausea/VomitingOndansetron, Metoclopramide (Safe)
SeizuresLevetiracetam (Safe); Avoid Phenytoin, Valproate, Carbamazepine
HyponatraemiaFluid Restriction (SIADH); Hypertonic Saline if Severe
Hypokalaemia/HypomagnesaemiaReplace Aggressively
Autonomic Instabilityβ-Blocker (Propranolol) for Tachycardia/Hypertension

4. DRUGS TO AVOID (Red List) vs SAFE (Green List)

AVOID (Red)SAFE (Green)
Barbiturates, Sulfonamides, RifampicinParacetamol, NSAIDs (Short-Term)
Phenytoin, Carbamazepine, Valproate, PhenobarbitalLevetiracetam, Gabapentin, Lamotrigine
Oestrogen/Progesterone (OCP)Progestogen-Only (Mini-Pill / Implant)
Rifampicin, GriseofulvinMost Antibiotics (Penicillins, Cephalosporins, Macrolides)
Alcohol (Acute), FastingNormal Diet, Glucose Infusion
Thiopental, EnfluranePropofol, Etomidate, Ketamine, Sevoflurane

3. Cutaneous Porphyrias — Management

Porphyria Cutanea Tarda (PCT) — Most Common

FeatureDetails
AetiologyUROD Deficiency (Sporadic 80% — Hepatic Iron Overload; Familial 20% — UROD Mutation)
TriggersAlcohol, Oestrogen, Hepatitis C, HIV, Iron Overload, Smoking
ClinicalPhotosensitivity (Hands/Face), Blisters/Fragility, Hypertrichosis, Scarring, Milia
DiagnosisUrine Uroporphyrin ↑ (Carboxylic), Plasma Fluorescence Peak 625nm, ↑ Faecal Iso-Coproporphyrin

| Management | 1. Phlebotomy 400-500mL q2wk → Target Ferritin 20-50 µg/L (1st Line)

2. Low-Dose Chloroquine/Hydroxychloroquine 125mg 2x/week (Mobilises Hepatic Porphyrins)

3. Avoid Triggers: Alcohol, Oestrogen, Iron Supplements

4. Treat HCV/HIV (If Co-Infection) |

Erythropoietic Protoporphyria (EPP) / XLEPP

FeatureDetails
SymptomsAcute Burning Pain on Sun Exposure (Immediate, No Blisters), Oedema, Erythema
DiagnosisErythrocyte Protoporphyrin ↑↑ (Total + Free); Plasma Fluorescence; FECH Gene

| Management | Photoprotection (UV-Blocking Clothing, Sunscreens, Window Films)

Beta-Carotene 120-180mg/day (Mild Benefit)

Afamelanotide (Scenesse®) — SC Implant q2mo (Approved)

Liver Transplant (End-Stage Liver Disease) |

Congenital Erythropoietic Porphyria (CEP) — Ultra-Rare

FeatureManagement
Severe Photosensitivity (Infancy), Red Urine, Deformities, Haemolytic AnaemiaSplenectomy (Reduces Haemolysis), Bone Marrow Transplant (Curative), Photoprotection

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Acute Porphyria HallmarkUrine PBG ↑↑↑ (Gold Standard)
AIP vs VP vs HCPAIP: No Skin; VP/HCP: Skin + Acute; VP = Faecal Proto > Copro; HCP = Faecal Copro > Proto
Acute AttackSevere Abdo Pain + Neuropathy + Psychiatric + Hyponatraemia
PrecipitantsBarbiturates, Sulfonamides, Rifampicin, Antiepileptics, Oestrogen, Alcohol, Fasting
Acute Attack RxHaemarginate 3-4mg/kg IV × 4 Days + IV Glucose 300-400g/d
Safe DrugsLevetiracetam, Gabapentin, Penicillins, Propofol, Progestogen-Only Pill
Unsafe DrugsBarbiturates, Phenytoin, Valproate, Rifampicin, Oestrogen, Sulfonamides, Alcohol
PCTMost Common Cutaneous; Phlebotomy 1st Line; Chloroquine 125mg 2x/wk; HCV/HIV Screen
EPPImmediate Burning Pain on Sun; Erythrocyte Protoporphyrin ↑↑; Afamelanotide
CEPInfantile; Severe Photosensitivity + Deformities; Splenectomy / BMT
XLEPPALAS2 Mutation (XL); Higher Liver Risk than EPP
Acute Attack RxHaemarginate 3-4mg/kg IV × 4 Days + IV Glucose 300-400g/d
Safe AntiepilepticLevetiracetam (First Choice); Avoid Phenytoin/Valproate/Carbamazepine
Safe AnaestheticPropofol, Etomidate, Ketamine, Sevoflurane
PCT ManagementPhlebotomy 1st Line; Low-Dose Chloroquine; Avoid Alcohol/Fe/Estrogen
VP vs HCPVP: Faecal Proto > Copro; HCP: Faecal Copro > Proto
PrecipitantsBarbiturates, Rifampicin, Phenytoin, Valproate, Oestrogen, Alcohol, Fasting
Glucose in Acute Attack300-400g/d 5-10% Dextrose (Represses ALAS1)

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
AIP vs VP vs HCPAIP = No Skin; VP = Proto > Copro in Faeces; HCP = Copro > Proto
Acute vs CutaneousAcute = Neurovisceral (AIP/ADP); Cutaneous = Photosensitivity (PCT/EPP/CEP); VP/HCP = Both
PCT vs EPPPCT = Blisters/Fragility (Delayed); EPP = Immediate Burning Pain (No Blisters)
PCT vs VPPCT = Uro Porphyrin ↑ (Urine); VP = Proto > Copro in Faeces
PCT ManagementPhlebotomy 1st Line (Target Ferritin 20-50); Low-Dose Chloroquine 2nd Line
EPP vs CEPEPP = Immediate Burning, No Blisters; CEP = Severe Infantile + Deformities
Safe AntiepilepticLevetiracetam (Only Safe One); Avoid Phenytoin/Valproate/Carbamazepine
Safe AnaestheticPropofol, Etomidate, Ketamine, Sevoflurane
PCT PrecipitantsAlcohol, Oestrogen, HCV, Iron, Smoking
Glucose in Acute Attack300-400g/d 5-10% Dextrose (Represses ALAS1)
Haemarginate Dose3-4mg/kg IV Daily × 4 Days
VP vs HCP DifferentiationVP: Faecal Proto > Copro; HCP: Faecal Copro > Proto
EPP vs XLEPPEPP = FECH (AR); XLEPP = ALAS2 (XL); XLEPP Higher Liver Risk
PCT Phlebotomy TargetFerritin 20-50 µg/L
CEPSplenectomy / Bone Marrow Transplant (Curative)
GeneticsAIP/VP/HCP = AD; ADP = AR; PCT = AD/Sporadic; EPP = AR; CEP = AR; XLEPP = XL

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.1.6 Wilson Disease
[!info]
Wilson Disease = Autosomal Recessive Disorder of Copper Metabolism due to ATP7B Mutation (Chromosome 13). Impaired Biliary Copper Excretion → Copper Accumulation in Liver, Brain (Basal Ganglia), Cornea (Kayser-Fleischer Rings), Kidney. Treatable if Diagnosed Early.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Recognise hepatic, neurological, and psychiatric presentations
  • [ ] Apply diagnostic criteria (Leipzig Score, ceruloplasmin, urinary copper, KF rings, liver copper)
  • [ ] Prescribe lifelong chelation therapy (penicillamine, trientine, zinc)
  • [ ] Recognise indications for liver transplantation
  • [ ] Counsel on family screening and genetic testing

2. Genetics & Pathophysiology

FeatureDetails
GeneATP7B (Chromosome 13q14.3) — Copper-Transporting ATPase
FunctionIntra-Golgi Copper Transport → Copper Incorporation into Ceruloplasmin + Biliary Excretion
Mutation EffectLoss-of-Function → ↓ Ceruloplasmin Incorporation + ↓ Biliary Excretion → Copper Accumulation
InheritanceAutosomal Recessive (Carrier Frequency ~1:100)
Allelic Heterogeneity>800 Mutations (H1069Q Most Common in Europeans)
Copper AccumulationLiver → Brain (Basal Ganglia, Putamen) → Cornea (KF Rings) → Kidney, Heart, Pancreas

2. Clinical Presentation

Hepatic Presentation (Childhood/Young Adult)

PresentationFrequency
AsymptomaticIncidental LFT Abnormality
Acute HepatitisJaundice, Nausea, Fatigue, Hepatomegaly
Chronic HepatitisPersistent LFT Elevation, Progressive Fibrosis
CirrhosisPortal Hypertension, Ascites, Varices, Splenomegaly
Acute Liver Failure (Fulminant)Coombs-Negative Haemolytic Anaemia, ALF (High Mortality Without Transplant)

Neuropsychiatric Presentation (Young Adult, 20-40yr)

SystemFeatures
MotorTremor (Wing-Beating, Rest/Action), Dystonia, Rigidity, Bradykinesia, Chorea
SpeechDysarthria (Scanning, Monotone), Drooling
PsychiatricDepression, Bipolar, Psychosis, Personality Change, Cognitive Decline
OcularKayser-Fleischer Rings (Pathognomonic; 95% Neuro, 50% Hepatic), Sunflower Cataract
OtherDysphagia, Gait Disturbance, Salivation

Other System Involvement

SystemFeatures
RenalFanconi Syndrome (Aminoaciduria, Phosphaturia, Glycosuria, RTA), Nephrolithiasis
CardiacCardiomyopathy, Arrhythmias
SkeletalJoint Pain, Osteoporosis, Premature Osteoarthritis
EndocrineHypogonadism, Menstrual Irregularity, Infertility
HaematologicalCoombs-Negative Haemolytic Anaemia (Acute Liver Failure), Thrombocytopenia

2. Diagnostic Criteria — Leipzig Scoring System

ParameterScore
Kayser-Fleischer Rings2 (Present) / 0 (Absent)
Ceruloplasmin2 (<0.1 g/L), 1 (0.1-0.2), 0 (>0.2)
24h Urinary Copper2 (>1.6 µmol/24h / >100 µg/24h), 1 (0.8-1.6 µmol), 0 (Normal)
Liver Copper (Dry Weight)2 (>4.0 µg/g / >250 µg/g), 1 (1-4 / 50-250), 0 (<1 / <50)
Genetic Testing (ATP7B)4 (2 Mutations), 1 (1 Mutation), 0 (None)
Neurological Symptoms2 (Severe), 1 (Mild), 0 (None)
Coombs-Negative Haemolytic Anaemia1 (Present)
Total ScoreInterpretation
≥4Wilson Disease Diagnosed
3Possible (Further Testing)
<3Unlikely

2. Key Diagnostic Investigations

TestWilson Disease FindingNotes
Ceruloplasmin<0.2 g/L (Low)Acute Phase Reactant → Can Be Normal in Acute Inflammation
24h Urinary Copper>100 µg/24h (1.6 µmol/24h)↑↑ (Free Copper)
Kayser-Fleischer RingsPresent in 95% Neuro / 50% HepaticSlit-Lamp Exam Required; Pathognomonic
Liver Copper (Biopsy)>250 µg/g Dry Weight (Severe)Gold Standard; >4.0 µmol/g = Diagnostic
Free Serum Copper>15-20 µg/dL (Calculated: Total Cu - 3×Ceruloplasmin)>1.6 µmol/L
Genetic Testing (ATP7B)Biallelic Pathogenic VariantsConfirmatory; Family Screening
Brain MRI"Face of the Giant Panda" Sign (Midbrain T2 Hyperintensity), Basal Ganglia T2 HyperintensitySupportive

3. Lens Signs

Kayser-Fleischer Rings

FeatureDetails
LocationDescemet's Membrane (Corneal Periphery)
AppearanceGolden-Brown / Greenish Ring at Limbus
DetectionSlit-Lamp Examination (Essential)
Prevalence95% Neurological Wilson; 50% Hepatic Wilson; <1% Other Liver Disease

Sunflower Cataract

FeatureDetails
AppearanceRadial, Petal-Like Opacities in Anterior/Posterior Lens Capsule
SignificancePathognomonic for Wilson Disease (Rare but Specific)

3. Management

Chelation Therapy (Lifelong Unless Transplanted)

AgentDoseIndicationKey Adverse Effects
Penicillamine500-1500mg/day (Divided Doses)1st Line (If Tolerated)Proteinuria, Neutropenia, Lupus-like Syndrome, Skin Changes, Taste Disturbance
Trientine600-1200mg/day (Divided Doses)2nd Line (If Penicillamine Intolerant)Fewer SE; No Cross-Reaction with Penicillamine
Zinc Acetate50mg TDS (Elemental Zn 25mg/TDS)Maintenance (After Initial Chelation) / Initial if Mild/HepaticGastric Irritation; Cu Deficiency if Overdosed

Initiation & Monitoring

PhaseMonitoring
Initial (Months 1-3)24h Urine Cu q2-4wk (Target 200-500 µg/24h on Chelation), Ceruloplasmin, LFTs, FBC, U&Es q2-4wk, Free Cu <1.6 µmol/L
Maintenance24h Urine Cu q3-6mo, Ceruloplasmin, LFTs, FBC, U&Es q3-6mo, Free Cu <1.6 µmol/L
Zinc TherapySerum Zinc, Urine Cu, FBC, LFTs q3-6mo

Pregnancy

AspectManagement
PenicillamineContinue (Reduce Dose 250-500mg/day); Pyridoxine 25mg OD
TrientineContinue (Safe in Pregnancy)
ZincContinue (Safe)
MonitoringMonthly Urine Cu, LFTs, FBC; Target Free Cu <1.6 µmol/L

3. Liver Transplantation

Indications

IndicationCriteria
Acute Liver FailureWilsonian ALF (High Mortality Without Transplant)
Decompensated CirrhosisRefractory Ascites, Variceal Bleeding, Hepatic Encephalopathy
Refractory NeuropsychiatricProgressive Despite Optimal Chelation
Fulminant Wilson DiseaseCoombs-Negative Haemolytic Anaemia + ALF

Outcomes

OutcomePost-Transplant
Survival1yr >85%, 5yr >80%
Neurological RecoveryOften Incomplete (Residual Dystonia/Tremor)
Copper MetabolismNormalised (Donor Liver Provides Functional ATP7B)

3. Family Screening & Genetic Counselling

AspectRecommendation
1st-Degree RelativesGenetic Testing (ATP7B) + Biochemical (Ceruloplasmin, Urine Cu)
Siblings25% Risk (Both Parents Carriers); Screen Immediately
Offspring50% Carrier Risk; Screen if Partner Carrier
Prenatal DiagnosisCVS/Amniocentesis (If Familial Mutations Known)
Genetic CounsellingAutosomal Recessive → 25% Affected, 50% Carrier, 25% Normal

4. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Wilson DiseaseATP7B Mutation (Chr 13) → Impaired Cu Excretion → Accumulation in Liver/Brain/Cornea
Kayser-Fleischer RingsPathognomonic (Slit-Lamp); 95% Neurological, 50% Hepatic
Ceruloplasmin<0.2 g/L (Low); Can Be Normal in Acute Inflammation (Acute Phase Reactant)
24h Urinary Copper>100 µg/24h (Normal <40)
Liver Copper>250 µg/g Dry Weight (Diagnostic)
Leipzig Score≥4 = Diagnosis; 3 = Possible; <3 = Unlikely
ATP7B MutationH1069Q (Most Common European); >800 Mutations Known
Penicillamine500-1500mg/d (1st Line); SE: Proteinuria, Neutropenia, Lupus, Skin
Trientine600-1200mg/d (2nd Line); Fewer SE; No Cross-Reactivity with Penicillamine
Zinc Acetate50mg TDS (Maintenance); Blocks Intestinal Cu Absorption
Free CopperTotal Cu - (3 × Ceruloplasmin) → Target <1.6 µmol/L
Liver TransplantIndicated for ALF, Decompensated Cirrhosis, Refractory Neuro; Neuro Recovery Incomplete
Fulminant WilsonCoombs-Negative Haemolytic Anaemia + ALF → Urgent Transplant
Neurological WilsonTremor (Wing-Beating), Dystonia, Dysarthria, KF Rings, "Face of Giant Panda" MRI
Hepatic WilsonAcute Hepatitis, Chronic Hepatitis, Cirrhosis, ALF
Penicillamine SEProteinuria, Neutropenia, Lupus-like, Skin Changes, Taste Disturbance
Trientine600-1200mg/d (Better Tolerated); No Cross-Reactivity
Zinc Acetate50mg TDS (Blocks Intestinal Cu Absorption); Maintenance Therapy
Free CopperTotal Cu - (3×Ceruloplasmin) → Target <1.6 µmol/L on Therapy
Neurological Recovery Post-TxOften Incomplete (Residual Dystonia/Tremor)
PregnancyContinue Penicillamine (Reduce Dose) / Trientine / Zinc; Pyridoxine 25mg OD

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Ceruloplasmin Low ≠ WilsonCan Be Low in Malnutrition, Nephrotic Syndrome, Protein-Losing Enteropathy; Confirm with Urine Cu / KF Rings / Genetics
Ceruloplasmin Normal in WilsonPossible (Acute Phase Reactant in Inflammation/Infection)
KF Rings AbsentOcular Wilson (Hepatic Only) — KF Rings Absent in ~50% Hepatic Presentation
Penicillamine vs TrientinePenicillamine = 1st Line (More SE); Trientine = 2nd Line (Better Tolerated, No Cross-Reactivity)
Zinc vs PenicillamineZinc = Blocks Absorption (Maintenance); Penicillamine = Chelation (Initial)
Free Copper FormulaTotal Cu - (3 × Ceruloplasmin) = Free Copper; Target <1.6 µmol/L on Therapy
Liver Cu QuantitationGold Standard (Biopsy); >250 µg/g DW = Diagnostic
Leipzig Score≥4 = Diagnosis; 3 = Possible; <3 = Unlikely
Neurological Recovery Post-TxIncomplete (Residual Dystonia/Tremor Common)
Acute Liver Failure WilsonCoombs-Negative Haemolytic Anaemia + ALF → Urgent Transplant
Penicillamine in PregnancyContinue (Dose Reduce 250-500mg/d); Pyridoxine 25mg OD
TrientineBetter Tolerated; No Cross-Reactivity with Penicillamine Allergy
Free Copper Target<1.6 µmol/L on Chelation

9. Mind Map

Wilson Disease
Genetics
ATP7B (Chr 13), AR, H1069Q Common
Cu Transport → Biliary Excretion + Ceruloplasmin Incorporation
Pathophysiology
Cu Accumulation: Liver → Brain (Basal Ganglia) → Cornea (KF Rings) → Kidney/Heart/Pancreas
↓ Ceruloplasmin, ↓ Biliary Excretion
Clinical
Hepatic: Acute Hepatitis → Cirrhosis → ALF (Coombs-Neg Haemolytic)
Neuropsych: Tremor (Wing-Beating), Dystonia, Dysarthria, Psychiatric, KF Rings, Panda Sign
Diagnosis
Leipzig Score ≥4 = Dx
Ceruloplasmin <0.2, Urine Cu >100µg/24h, KF Rings, Liver Cu >250µg/g
Free Cu = Total Cu - 3×Cerulo <1.6µmol/L (Rx Target)
Genetic: ATP7B Biallelic Mutations
Treatment
Penicillamine (1st), Trientine (2nd), Zinc (Maintenance)
Free Cu Target <1.6 µmol/L
Lifelong Chelation (Unless Tx)
Transplant
ALF, Decompensated Cirrhosis, Refractory Neuro
Cu Metabolism Normalised Post-Tx
Genetics
AR, ATP7B (Chr13), H1069Q Common
Siblings 25% Risk; Cascade Screening
Prenatal/PGD Possible
Complications
Fulminant Hepatic Failure (Coombs-Neg HA)
Neuro: Dystonia, Tremor, Dysarthria
Renal: Fanconi, Stones
Cardiac: Cardiomyopathy
Haematological: Coombs-Neg HA

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.2 Sodium and Water Balance 4
▸ 19.2.1 Diabetes Insipidus
[!info]
Diabetes Insipidus (DI) = Polyuria + Polydipsia due to ADH Deficiency (Central) or Renal Resistance (Nephrogenic). Central DI = ADH Deficiency; Nephrogenic DI = Renal Resistance. Water Deprivation Test + Desmopressin Challenge = Gold Standard Diagnostic Test.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Differentiate Central DI, Nephrogenic DI, and Primary Polydipsia
  • [ ] Perform and interpret Water Deprivation Test + Desmopressin Challenge
  • [ ] Apply desmopressin therapy for Central DI
  • [ ] Manage Nephrogenic DI (Thiazides, Amiloride, Low Salt Diet)
  • [ ] Recognise Gestational DI and its management

2. Overview & Classification

TypePathophysiologyADH LevelUrine OsmolalityDesmopressin Response
Central DIADH Deficiency (Pituitary/Stalk/Hypothalamic Lesion)LowLow (Dilute)Responds ↑ Urine Osm >50%
Nephrogenic DIRenal Resistance to ADH (V2 Receptor/AQP2 Defect)High/NormalLow (Dilute)No Response
Primary PolydipsiaExcessive Water Intake (Psychogenic/Dipsogenic)SuppressedLow (Concentrates on Deprivation)Concentrates on Deprivation
Gestational DIPlacental Vasopressinase Degrades ADHLow/NormalDiluteResponds to Desmopressin

2. Aetiology

Central DI (CDI)

CauseFrequencyDetails
Idiopathic~30%Autoimmune (Lymphocytic Infundibuloneurohypophysitis)
Pituitary Surgery / Trauma~20%Post-TSS, Head Trauma, Basal Skull Fracture
Infiltration~15%Sarcoidosis, Langerhans Cell Histiocytosis, Metastases, Haemochromatosis
GeneticRareAVP Gene Mutations (Autosomal Dominant)
Pituitary Surgery/Apoplexy~10%Post-TSS, Pituitary Apoplexy
Craniopharyngioma~5%Suprasellar Tumor Compressing Stalk

Nephrogenic DI (NDI)

CauseMechanismKey Features
LithiumMost Common Acquired↓ AQP2 Expression, ↓ cAMP; Dose/Duration Dependent
DrugsDemeclocycline, Amphotericin B, Foscarnet, Ofloxacin, IfosfamideV2 Receptor / AQP2 Inhibition
ElectrolytesHypercalcaemia, HypokalaemiaTubular Damage
Obstructive UropathyTubulointerstitial Damage
GeneticAVPR2 (X-Linked Recessive), AQP2 (AR)Congenital NDI

Primary Polydipsia (Psychogenic)

FeatureDetails
AetiologyPsychogenic (Schizophrenia), Habitual, Dipsogenic
MechanismExcess Water Intake → Suppresses ADH → Dilute Urine
Key FeatureUrine Concentrates During Deprivation (Unlike DI)

Gestational DI

FeatureDetails
CausePlacental Vasopressinase Degrades ADH
Onset2nd/3rd Trimester
ResolutionPostpartum (4-6 Weeks)
TreatmentDesmopressin (Safe in Pregnancy); Monitor Fluid Balance
RecurrenceHigh in Subsequent Pregnancies

2. Clinical Presentation

FeatureCentral DINephrogenic DIPrimary Polydipsia
Polyuria>3-4 L/day>3-4 L/day>3-4 L/day
PolydipsiaProfound Thirst, NocturiaProfound Thirst, NocturiaCompulsive Drinking
Urine OsmolalityLow (<300 mOsm/kg)Low (<300 mOsm/kg)Low/Variable (Concentrates on Deprivation)
Serum OsmolalityHigh (>295 mOsm/kg)HighNormal/ Low
Serum SodiumHigh (>145 mmol/L)HighNormal/Low
ADH LevelLow/UndetectableHighSuppressed

3. Diagnostic Algorithm — Water Deprivation Test (WDT)

Protocol

PhaseProcedureStop Criteria
1. Fluid DeprivationNPO + Fluid Restriction; Weight, Serum/Urine Osmolality q1-2hWeight Loss >5%; Urine Osm > Plasma Osm; Haemodynamic Instability
2. Desmopressin ChallengeDDAVP 2µg SC/IV (or 10-40µg Intranasal)Measure Urine Osm at 60min

Interpretation Matrix

ResultCentral DINephrogenic DIPrimary Polydipsia
Baseline Urine OsmLow (<300)Low (<300)Low/Variable
After DeprivationLow (<300)Low (<300)Concentrates (>600)
Post-DDAVP (60min)↑ >50%No Response (<10%)N/A (Already Concentrated)
Plasma ADHLowHighLow (Suppressed)

Stop Criteria (Safety)

CriterionAction
Weight Loss >5%STOP
Urine Osm > Plasma OsmSTOP
Haemodynamic Instability (SBP<90, HR>120)STOP
Time >8 HoursSTOP

3. Desmopressin (DDAVP) Therapy

Central DI

RouteDoseFrequency
Intranasal10-40µgq12-24h
Oral (Tablet)0.1-0.4mgq12-24h
Subcutaneous / IV2-4µgq12-24h
Dose TitrationTarget: Urine Output 1.5-2.5L/day, No Nocturia, Normal Na⁺

Nephrogenic DI

TreatmentDoseMechanism
Low Salt / Low Protein Diet—Reduces Solute Load
Thiazide DiureticHydrochlorothiazide 25-50mg BDInduces Mild Volume Depletion → ↑ Proximal Reabsorption
Amiloride5-10mg BDENaC Blocker; K⁺-Sparing
NSAIDs (Indomethacin)25-50mg TDS↑ Prostaglandin Inhibition → ↓ PGE2 → ↑ ADH Sensitivity
DesmopressinPartial Response (If Partial NDI)Limited Role

3. Gestational DI

FeatureDetails
CausePlacental Vasopressinase Degrades ADH
Onset2nd/3rd Trimester
ResolutionPostpartum (4-6 Weeks)
TreatmentDesmopressin (Safe in Pregnancy); Monitor Fluid Balance
RecurrenceHigh in Subsequent Pregnancies

4. Differential Diagnosis

FeatureCentral DINephrogenic DIPrimary Polydipsia
Serum Osmolality>295 mOsm/kg>295 mOsm/kgNormal/Low
Urine Osmolality<300 mOsm/kg<300 mOsm/kgConcentrates on Deprivation
Urine Osm Post-DDAVP↑ >50%No ChangeN/A
Plasma ADHLowHighSuppressed
Desmopressin TestPositive ResponseNo ResponseConcentrates on Deprivation

4. Management

Central DI

AspectDetails
Desmopressin (DDAVP)Intranasal 10-40µg q12-24h; Oral 0.1-0.4mg q12-24h; SC/IV 2-4µg q24h
Dose TitrationStart Low; Titrate to Urine Output 1.5-2.5L/day; Nocturia ≤1
Fluid IntakeNo Restriction (Ad Libitum)
Adverse EffectsHyponatraemia (Water Retention) — Monitor Na⁺

Nephrogenic DI

TherapyDoseRole
DietLow Salt, Low ProteinReduce Solute Load
ThiazideHCTZ 25-50mg BDInduces Mild Volume Depletion → ↑ Proximal Reabsorption
Amiloride5-10mg BDENaC Blocker; K⁺-Sparing
NSAIDsIndomethacin 25-50mg TDS↓ Prostaglandin → ↑ ADH Sensitivity
DesmopressinPartial Response OnlyIf Partial NDI

4. Complications & Monitoring

ComplicationMonitoring
HyponatraemiaSerum Na⁺ q6-12h (If on Desmopressin)
Water IntoxicationFluid Restriction if Severe; Stop Desmopressin
HypernatraemiaIf Desmopressin Missed/Dose Inadequate
Breakthrough PolyuriaDose Escalation / Split Dosing

5. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
DI vs SIADHDI = Polyuria + Dilute Urine + High Serum Osm; SIADH = Hyponatraemia + Concentrated Urine
Central vs Nephrogenic DICentral: ADH Low, Responds to DDAVP; Nephrogenic: ADH High, No DDAVP Response
WDT Stop CriteriaWeight Loss >5% OR Urine Osm > Plasma Osm OR Haemodynamic Instability
Central DI TreatmentDesmopressin (DDAVP) — Intranasal/Oral/SC/IV
Nephrogenic DI TreatmentThiazide + Amiloride + Low Salt Diet (Desmopressine Ineffective)
LithiumMost Common Cause of Acquired NDI (↓ AQP2, ↓ cAMP)
Primary PolydipsiaUrine Concentrates on Deprivation; DDAVP Not Needed
Gestational DIPlacental Vasopressinase; Desmopressin Safe; Resolves Postpartum
WDT Stop CriteriaWeight Loss >5%, Urine Osm > Plasma Osm, Haemodynamic Instability
Desmopressin HyponatraemiaMonitor Na⁺; Limit Fluids if on DDAVP
Lithium NDI↓ AQP2 Expression → Stop Lithium if Possible
Central vs Nephrogenic DIDDAVP Response: Central = ↑ Urine Osm >50%; Nephrogenic = No Response

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Central vs Nephrogenic DICentral = ADH Deficiency; Nephrogenic = Renal Resistance to ADH
DDAVP ResponseCentral = Works; Nephrogenic = Fails
Primary Polydipsia vs DIPolydipsia: Urine Concentrates on Deprivation; DI = Fails to Concentrate
Gestational DIPlacental Vasopressinase → ADH Degradation; Resolves Postpartum
Lithium NDI↓ AQP2 Expression; ↓ cAMP; Most Common Acquired NDI
Desmopressin vs VasopressinDDAVP = Pure V2 Agonist (No Pressor Effect); Vasopressin = V1+V2
Desmopressin in EnuresisIntranasal/Oral at Bedtime; No Fluid Restriction Needed
WDT StopWeight Loss >5% OR Urine Osm > Plasma Osm

9. Mind Map

Diabetes Insipidus
Types
Central DI (ADH Deficiency)
– Pituitary Surgery/Trauma
– Infiltration (Sarcoid, LCH, Mets)
– Genetic (AVP Mutation)
Nephrogenic DI (Renal Resistance)
– Lithium (Most Common Acquired)
– Drugs (Demeclocycline, Amphotericin)
– Genetic (AVPR2, AQP2)
– Electrolytes (HyperCa, HypoK)
Primary Polydipsia
– Psychogenic / Habitual
– Urine Concentrates on Deprivation
Gestational DI
– Placental Vasopressinase
– Desmopressin Safe
Diagnosis
Water Deprivation Test (Gold Standard)
Deprivation → DDAVP Challenge
Central: Urine Osm ↑ >50% post DDAVP
Nephrogenic: No Response
Polydipsia: Concentrates on Deprivation
Treatment
Central: Desmopressin (DDAVP)
Nephrogenic: Thiazide + Amiloride + Low Salt
Gestational: DDAVP (Safe)
WDT Protocol
Deprivation until >5% weight loss or Uosm > Posm
DDAVP 2µg SC/IV → Urine Osm at 60min
Central: ↑>50%; Nephrogenic: No Response

9. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Central vs Nephrogenic DICentral: ADH Low → DDAVP Response; Nephrogenic: ADH High → DDAVP No Response
WDT Gold StandardDeprivation → DDAVP Challenge
Central DIDDAVP → Urine Osm ↑ >50%
Nephrogenic DIDDAVP → No Response
Primary PolydipsiaUrine Concentrates on Deprivation (No DDAVP Needed)
Gestational DIPlacental Vasopressinase → ADH Degradation → Desmopressin Safe
Lithium NDIMost Common Acquired NDI (↓ AQP2, ↓ cAMP)
DDAVP in Central DIIntranasal/Oral/SC/IV; Monitor Na+ (Hyponatraemia Risk)
NDI ManagementThiazide + Amiloride + Low Salt Diet; Desmopressine Not Effective
WDT Stop CriteriaWeight Loss >5% OR Urine Osm > Plasma Osm

▸ 19.2.2 Hypernatraemia
[!info]
Hypernatraemia = Serum Na⁺ >145 mmol/L. Represents Free Water Deficit relative to Sodium. Indicates Impaired Thirst or Access to Water, or Excessive Water Loss. Mortality Up to 50% if Severe (>160) or Rapid Correction.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Define hypernatraemia and classify by volume status
  • [ ] Calculate free water deficit and plan correction
  • [ ] Apply water deprivation test and desmopressin challenge for diabetes insipidus
  • [ ] Differentiate central vs nephrogenic diabetes insipidus
  • [ ] Apply safe correction rate limits to prevent cerebral oedema

2. Aetiology & Classification by Volume Status

Hypovolaemic Hypernatraemia (Na⁺ & Water Loss, Water > Na⁺)

CauseMechanism
GI Losses (Diarrhoea, Vomiting, High-Output Stoma)Water Loss > Na⁺ Loss
Renal Losses (Diuretics, Osmotic Diuresis, Diabetes Insipidus, Salt-Wasting Nephropathy)Impaired Water Reabsorption
Cutaneous Losses (Burns, Sweating, Fever)Insensible + Sensible Water Loss
Respiratory Losses (Hyperventilation, Tracheostomy)Increased Respiratory Water Loss

Euvolaemic Hypernatraemia (Water Deficit Only)

CauseMechanism
Water Deprivation (Impaired Thirst, Impaired Access, Neurogenic)Inadequate Intake
Diabetes Insipidus (Central/Nephrogenic)Impaired ADH Action → Massive Dilute Urine
Lactation / Hypermetabolic StatesIncreased Water Requirement
HyperventilationRespiratory Water Loss

Hypervolaemic Hypernatraemia (Sodium Gain > Water Gain)

CauseMechanism
Iatrogenic (Hypertonic Saline, Sodium Bicarbonate, Blood Transfusion)Exogenous Sodium Load
Hypertonic Feeds / TPNSodium Gain > Water
Salt Poisoning (Salt Ingestion, Seawater Ingestion)
Mineralocorticoid Excess (Conn's Syndrome)Na⁺ Retention > K⁺/H⁺ Loss

2. Diabetes Insipidus (Central & Nephrogenic)

Pathophysiology

TypeMechanismADH Level
Central DIADH Deficiency (Pituitary/Stalk/Hypothalamic Lesion)Low / Undetectable
Nephrogenic DIRenal Resistance to ADH (V2 Receptor/AQP2 Defect)High / Normal
Gestational DIPlacental Vasopressinase Degrades ADHLow/Normal
Primary PolydipsiaExcessive Intake → ADH SuppressionSuppressed

Water Deprivation Test + Desmopressin Challenge (Gold Standard)

StepProcedure
BaselineSerum Osmo, Urine Osmo, Serum Na⁺, Weight, Vitals
Fluid DeprivationNPO + No IV Fluids; Monitor Weight, Serum/Urine Osmo q1-2h
Stop CriteriaWeight Loss >3-5% OR Urine Osmo > Plasma Osmo OR Haemodynamic Instability
Desmopressin ChallengeDDAVP 2µg IV/SC (or 10-40µg Intranasal); Measure Urine Osmo at 60 min

Interpretation Matrix

FindingCentral DINephrogenic DIPrimary Polydipsia
Urine Osmo (Baseline)Low (<300)Low (<300)Low/Variable
After DeprivationLow (Fails to Concentrate)Low (Fails to Concentrate)Concentrates (>600)
Post-DDAVP (60min)↑ >50% (Urine Osmo > Plasma)No Response (<10% Rise)N/A (Already Concentrated)
Plasma ADHLowHighSuppressed

3. Central vs Nephrogenic Diabetes Insipidus

FeatureCentral DINephrogenic DI
ADHLow / UndetectableHigh / Normal
DDAVP ResponsePositive (Urine Osmo ↑ >50%)Negative (<10% Rise)
Common CausesSurgery (TSS, Craniotomy), Trauma, Infiltration (Sarcoid, LCH, Mets), Genetic (AVP Mutation)Lithium (Most Common), Drugs (Demeclocycline, Amphotericin), Electrolytes (Hypercalcaemia, Hypokalaemia), Genetic (AVPR2, AQP2)
TreatmentDesmopressin (DDAVP)Thiazides + Amiloride + Low Salt Diet

3. Water Deprivation Test Protocol

PhaseAction
1. Preparation08:00 Start; NPO; Empty Bladder; Weight, Serum/Ur Osmo, Serum Na⁺, Vitals
2. DeprivationNPO; Monitor: Weight q1h, Serum/Ur Osmo q1-2h, Vitals q1h
3. Stop CriteriaWeight Loss >3-5% OR Urine Osmo > Plasma Osmo OR Haemodynamic Instability OR Time >8h
4. DDAVP Challenge2µg IV/SC (or 10-40µg Intranasal)
5. Post-DDAVPUrine Osmo at 60 min

Interpretation

ResultDiagnosis
Urine Concentrates on Deprivation → Primary Polydipsia
Fails to Concentrate + ↑ >50% Post-DDAVP → Central DI
Fails to Concentrate + No DDAVP Response → Nephrogenic DI

3. Free Water Deficit & Correction

Free Water Deficit (FWD) Formula

FWD = TBW × (Current Na⁺/140 - 1)
- TBW = 0.6 × Weight (kg) Men; 0.5 × Weight Women
- Target Na⁺ = 140 mmol/L (or 12 mmol/L Reduction from Current)

Correction Plan

ParameterTarget
Max Correction Rate10-12 mmol/L/24h (Avoid Cerebral Oedema)
If Acute (<24h)Can Correct Faster (Up to 15 mmol/L/24h)
Fluid Choice5% Dextrose (D5W) or 0.45% NaCl (Hypotonic)
If Hypovolaemic0.9% NaCl First (Restore Volume) → Then D5W
Correction Rate0.5 mmol/L/hr (12 mmol/L/24h)

Example Calculation

70kg Man, Na⁺ 160 mmol/L
- TBW = 0.6 × 70 = 42 L
- FWD = 42 × (160/140 - 1) = 42 × 0.143 = 6 L
- Replace over 24-48h with D5W (Avoid Rapid Correction)

3. Central Diabetes Insipidus Management

AgentDoseRouteFrequency
Desmopressin (DDAVP)10-40 µgIntranasalq12-24h
Desmopressin (Tablet)0.1-0.4 mgOralq12-24h
Desmopressin (IV/SC)2-4 µgIV/SCq12-24h

Titration

StepAction
Start Low10 µg Intranasal q12h or 0.1 mg PO q12h
TitrateIncrease by 10 µg / 0.1 mg every 3-7 Days
TargetUrine Output 1.5-2.5 L/day; Nocturia ≤1; Normal Na⁺

3. Nephrogenic Diabetes Insipidus Management

TreatmentDoseMechanism
Low Salt / Low Protein Diet—Reduces Solute Load
Thiazide DiureticHydrochlorothiazide 25-50mg BDInduces Mild Volume Depletion → ↑ Proximal Reabsorption
Amiloride5-10 mg BDENaC Blocker; K⁺-Sparing
NSAIDs (Indomethacin)25-50mg TDS↓ Prostaglandin → ↑ ADH Sensitivity
DesmopressinPartial Response OnlyIf Partial NDI

3. Acute Hypernatraemia Management

ScenarioManagement
Hypovolaemic0.9% NaCl 1-2L Bolus → Then D5W / 0.45% NaCl (Restore Volume First)
EuvolaemicD5W or 0.45% NaCl (Free Water Replacement)
HypervolaemicSodium Restriction + Loop Diuretic + D5W

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Hypernatraemia DefinitionNa⁺ >145 mmol/L (Free Water Deficit)
Free Water Deficit FormulaTBW × (Current Na⁺/140 - 1)
TBW0.6 × Weight (Men); 0.5 × Weight (Women)
Max Correction Rate10-12 mmol/L/24h (Avoid Cerebral Oedema)
Acute CorrectionUp to 15 mmol/L/24h if Onset <24h
Fluid ChoiceD5W (Free Water); 0.45% NaCl Alternative
Water Deprivation TestGold Standard for DI (Deprivation → DDAVP Challenge)
Central DI DDAVP ResponseUrine Osmo ↑ >50%
Nephrogenic DI DDAVP ResponseNo Response (<10% Rise)
LithiumMost Common Cause of Acquired Nephrogenic DI
Central DI TreatmentDesmopressin (DDAVP) Intranasal/PO/IV/SC
Nephrogenic DI TreatmentThiazide + Amiloride + Low Salt Diet (DDAVP Ineffective)
Gestational DIPlacental Vasopressinase → Resolves Postpartum
Primary PolydipsiaUrine Concentrates on Deprivation; DDAVP Not Needed
Correction Rate Limit10-12 mmol/L/24h (Cerebral Oedema Risk)
Cerebral OedemaRisk if Correction >12 mmol/L/24h; Monitor Neurological Status

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Central vs Nephrogenic DICentral = ADH Deficiency → DDAVP Works; Nephrogenic = Renal Resistance → DDAVP Fails
DI vs SIADHDI = Na⁺ High + Dilute Urine; SIADH = Na⁺ Low + Concentrated Urine
Central vs Nephrogenic DDAVPCentral = Responds (Urine Osmo ↑ >50%); Nephrogenic = Fails
Water Deprivation TestConcentrates → Polydipsia; Fails + DDAVP Response → Central DI; Fails + No DDAVP → Nephrogenic
Free Water DeficitTBW × (Current Na⁺/140 - 1); Replace with D5W
Correction Rate10-12 mmol/L/24h Max (Cerebral Oedema Risk)
Fluid for HypernatraemiaD5W (Free Water); NOT 0.9% NaCl (Unless Hypovolaemic)
Central DI CausesSurgery (TSS), Trauma, Infiltration (Sarcoid, LCH, Mets)
Nephrogenic DI CausesLithium (Most Common), Drugs, Electrolytes, Genetic
Water Deprivation StopWeight Loss >3-5% OR Urine Osmo > Plasma Osmo OR Haemodynamic Instability
