▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.4 Potassium Disorders 2
▸ 19.4.1 Hyperkalaemia
[!info]
Hyperkalaemia = Serum K⁺ >5.5 mmol/L. Life-Threatening Emergency if >6.5 or ECG Changes. Immediate Membrane Stabilisation (Calcium Gluconate) → Shift K⁺ Into Cells (Insulin/Dextrose) → Enhanced Excretion (Dialysis/Resonium). ECG Progression: Peaked T Waves → PR Prolongation/QRS Widening → Sine Wave → VF/Asystole.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Recognise ECG progression of hyperkalaemia and initiate immediate stabilisation
  • [ ] Apply the 4-step emergency management: Calcium → Insulin/Dextrose → Salbutamol → Resonium/Dialysis
  • [ ] Differentiate true hyperkalaemia from pseudohyperkalaemia
  • [ ] Identify causes: Renal Failure, Drugs (ACEi, K-sparing), Acidosis, Adrenal Insufficiency, Tumour Lysis
  • [ ] Apply dialysis indications and monitoring

2. Definitions & Severity

SeveritySerum K⁺ (mmol/L)ECG FindingsClinical Urgency
Mild5.5-6.0Peaked T Waves (Often Only Finding)Urgent (Monitor & Treat)
Moderate6.0-6.5Peaked T, PR Prolongation, QRS WideningEmergent (Immediate Stabilisation)
Severe>6.5QRS >120ms, Sine Wave, Loss of P Waves → VF/AsystoleCRITICAL (ICU, Immediate Dialysis)

2. Aetiology & Classification

Impaired Excretion (Renal)

CauseMechanism
Acute Kidney Injury (AKI)↓ GFR → ↓ K⁺ Excretion
Chronic Kidney Disease (CKD)↓ Nephron Mass → ↓ K⁺ Excretion
DrugsACEi, ARB, K⁺-Sparing Diuretics (Spironolactone, Amiloride, Triamterene), NSAIDs, Heparin, Trimethoprim, Beta-Blockers, Calcineurin Inhibitors
Obstructive UropathyPost-renal AKI
Hypoaldosteronism (Type 4 RTA, Diabetes, HIV, ACEi)↓ Aldosterone → ↓ K⁺ Excretion

Transcellular Shift (K⁺ Moves Out of Cells)

CauseMechanism
Metabolic AcidosisH⁺ Enters Cells → K⁺ Moves Out (0.6 mmol/L K⁺ ↑ per 0.1 pH ↓)
Respiratory AcidosisSimilar (Less Pronounced)
Insulin Deficiency (DKA, HHS)↓ Insulin → ↓ Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase → K⁺ Shift Out
Tumour Lysis SyndromeMassive Cell Lysis → K⁺/Phosphate/Uric Acid Release
RhabdomyolysisMuscle Cell Lysis → K⁺/Phosphate/CK/Myoglobin Release
HaemolysisRBC Lysis → K⁺ Release (In Vitro / In Vivo)
Beta-Blockers↓ β₂-Mediated K⁺ Uptake
SuccinylcholineMassive Depolarisation → K⁺ Release (Burns, Trauma, Denervation)

Impaired Excretion + Shift

CauseFeatures
Tumour Lysis SyndromeAKI + Cell Lysis + Hyperphosphataemia + Hyperuricaemia
RhabdomyolysisAKI + Myoglobinuria + Hyperkalaemia + Hyperphosphataemia
Adrenal Insufficiency (Addison's)Hypoaldosteronism + Hyponatraemia + Hyperkalaemia + Hypotension

2. Pseudohyperkalaemia (Spurious)

CauseMechanism
Haemolysis (During Phlebotomy)RBC K⁺ Release → Falsely High Serum K⁺
Thrombocytosis (>1000×10⁹/L)Platelet K⁺ Release During Clotting
Leucocytosis (>100×10⁹/L)WBC K⁺ Release During Clotting
Fist Clenching / TourniquetLocal Muscle Contraction → Local K⁺ Release
Delayed ProcessingK⁺ Leaks from Cells Over Time

Detection

TestPseudohyperkalaemiaTrue Hyperkalaemia
Repeat Sample (No Tourniquet, Free Flow)NormalisesRemains High
Plasma K⁺ (EDTA)Normal (No Clotting)High
Platelet Count>1000 ×10⁹/LNormal
WBC Count>100 ×10⁹/LNormal
Clinical ContextNo ECG ChangesECG Changes Match K⁺

3. ECG Progression (Critical for Viva)

Serum K⁺ECG ChangesClinical Significance
5.5-6.0Peaked T Waves (Tall, Narrow, Tent-Shaped)Early Sign; Monitor Closely
6.0-6.5PR Prolongation, QRS Widening (>100ms), Flattened P WavesEmergent — Immediate Stabilisation
6.5-7.0QRS >120ms, Sine Wave (QRS-T Fusion), P Waves AbsentCRITICAL — Imminent VF/Asystole
>7.0Sine Wave, Asystole/VFCARDIAC ARREST IMMINENT
Key: ECG Changes Do NOT Always Correlate Perfectly with K⁺ Level — Treat Patient, Not Number. Peaked T Waves = Often First Sign.

3. Emergency Management Algorithm (4-Step)

HYPERAKALAEMIA (K⁺ >6.5 OR ECG CHANGES)
         │
         ▼
STEP 1: **MEMBRANE STABILISATION** (INSTANT)
         │
         ├── **Calcium Gluconate 10% 10mL IV** (Over 5-10 Min)
         │       **Mechanism**: Antagonises K⁺ Effect on Cardiac Membrane
         │       **Onset**: Immediate; **Duration**: 30-60 Min
         │       **Repeat**: If ECG Changes Persist / Recur
         │
         │       ⚠️ **CAUTION**: In Digoxin Toxicity → Calcium Can Worsen Arrhythmias
         │       ⚠️ CaCl₂ 10% 5-10mL Alternative (Central Line Only; Irritant)
         │
         ▼
STEP 2: **SHIFT K⁺ INTO CELLS** (RAPID, TEMPORARY)
         │
         ├── **Insulin 10U Actrapid + 50mL 50% Dextrose IV**
         │       **Mechanism**: Insulin → ↑ Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase → K⁺ Shift Into Cells
         │       **Onset**: 15-30 Min; **Peak**: 30-60 Min; **Duration**: 2-4 Hours
         │       **Effect**: ↓ K⁺ by 0.5-1.0 mmol/L (Transient)
         │       **Monitor**: CBG q30min (Risk of Hypoglycaemia)
         │
         ├── **Salbutamol 5mg Nebulised** (Adjunct)
         │       **Mechanism**: β₂-Agonist → ↑ cAMP → ↑ Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase
         │       **Onset**: 15 Min; **Effect**: ↓ K⁺ 0.5-1.0 mmol/L
         │
         └── **Sodium Bicarbonate** (If Metabolic Acidosis)
                 8.4% NaHCO₃ 50-100mL IV (Corrects Acidosis → ↓ K⁺ Shift)
         │
         ▼
STEP 3: **ENHANCE EXCRETION** (DEFINITIVE)
         │
         ├── **Calcium Resonium (Sodium Polystyrene Sulfonate) 15g PO/PR**
         │       **Mechanism**: Gut K⁺ Binding (Na⁺/K⁺ Exchange)
         │       **Onset**: 2-4 Hours; **Duration**: 6-8 Hours
         │       **Caution**: Constipation, Colonic Necrosis (Rare)
         │
         ├── **Loop Diuretic** (Furosemide 40-80mg IV)
         │       **Only if Volume Overload / Not Oliguric**
         │       **Effect**: ↑ K⁺ Excretion (If Urine Output Adequate)
         │
         └── **DIALYSIS** (DEFINITIVE TREATMENT)
                 **Indications**: K⁺ >6.5 + ECG / Refractory / AKI / Oliguria / Tumour Lysis
                 **Modalities**: IHD (Preferred), SLED, CVVHDF
                 **Effect**: Rapid K⁺ Removal (3-5 mmol/L per Session)
         │
         ▼
STEP 4: **IDENTIFY & TREAT CAUSE**
         │
         ├── Review Drugs (ACEi, ARB, K-Sparing, NSAIDs, Heparin, Beta-Blockers, Trimethoprim)
         ├── AKI / CKD → Renal Support
         ├── DKA → Insulin + Fluids
         ├── Tumour Lysis → Allopurinol/Rasburicase + Hydration + Dialysis
         ├── Rhabdomyolysis → Hydration + Alkalisation
         ├── Adrenal Insufficiency → Hydrocortisone 100mg IV q6h
         └── Stop/Adjust Offending Drugs (ACEi/ARB/K-Sparing/NSAIDs/Heparin)

3. Dialysis Indications (Absolute)

IndicationDetails
K⁺ >6.5 mmol/L with ECG ChangesAbsolute
K⁺ >7.0 mmol/L (Any ECG)Absolute
Refractory to Medical Management>6.5 Despite Calcium + Insulin + Resonium
Oliguric AKI / CKD Stage 5Unable to Excrete K⁺
Tumour Lysis SyndromeMassive K⁺/Phosphate/Uric Acid Load
RhabdomyolysisMassive K⁺ Release + AKI

3. Monitoring During Treatment

ParameterFrequencyTarget
Serum K⁺q30-60 min (Acute); q4-6h (Stable)<5.5 mmol/L
ECGContinuous (Acute); Serial q1-2hResolution of Peaked T/QRS Widening
Blood Glucoseq30-60 min (During Insulin)4-10 mmol/L
Serum Ca²⁺q1-2h (If Calcium Given)Normal
Urine OutputHourly>0.5 mL/kg/h
Magnesiumq6-12hNormalise if Low

3. Pseudohyperkalaemia — Quick Detection

ClueAction
No ECG Changes Despite High K⁺Suspect Pseudohyperkalaemia
Platelets >1000 or WBC >100Collect EDTA Plasma Sample
Haemolysed SampleRepeat with Free Flow, Large Bore Needle
Fist ClenchingRepeat Without Tourniquet/Clenching

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Hyperkalaemia Emergency ThresholdK⁺ >6.5 OR ECG Changes → Immediate Stabilisation
ECG ProgressionPeaked T → PR Prolongation/QRS Widening → Sine Wave → VF/Asystole
Step 1 (Immediate)Calcium Gluconate 10% 10mL IV (Membrane Stabilisation)
Step 2 (Shift)Insulin 10U + 50mL 50% Dextrose (Onset 15-30 min)
Calcium Gluconate Dose10mL 10% IV over 5-10 min (Repeat if ECG Persists)
Insulin/Dextrose Dose10U Actrapid + 50mL 50% Dextrose IV
Salbutamol Nebuliser5mg (Adjunct; β₂-Agonist)
Resonium15g PO/PR (Onset 2-4h; Gut K⁺ Binding)
Dialysis IndicationK⁺ >6.5 + ECG / Refractory / AKI / Tumour Lysis
Calcium Gluconate CautionDigoxin Toxicity → Calcium Can Worsen Arrhythmias
PseudohyperkalaemiaNo ECG Changes; Thrombocytosis/Leucocytosis/Haemolysis → Repeat EDTA Plasma
Insulin/Dextrose MonitoringCBG q30min (Hypoglycaemia Risk)
Acidosis → Hyperkalaemia0.6 mmol/L K⁺ Rise per 0.1 pH Drop
Tumour Lysis & RhabdoDialysis Often Needed (Massive K⁺ Release + AKI)
Adrenal InsufficiencyHyperkalaemia + Hyponatraemia + Hypotension → Hydrocortisone 100mg IV

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
True vs Pseudo HyperkalaemiaPseudo: No ECG Changes; EDTA Plasma Normal; Thrombocytosis/Leucocytosis
Calcium Gluconate vs Calcium ChlorideGluconate 10% 10mL (Peripheral OK); Chloride 10% 5-10mL (Central Only)
Calcium in Digoxin ToxicityContraindicated (Worsens Arrhythmias)
Insulin vs Dextrose OrderInsulin AFTER Dextrose (Or Mixed) — Avoid Hypoglycaemia
Resonium TimingOnset 2-4h (Not for Acute Stabilisation)
Dialysis CriteriaK⁺ >6.5 + ECG / Refractory / AKI / Tumour Lysis
Calcium EffectMembrane Stabilisation ONLY (Does NOT Lower K⁺)
Acidosis Contribution0.6 mmol/L K⁺ Rise per 0.1 pH Drop
Peaked T WavesFirst ECG Sign (Often Only Finding at K⁺ 5.5-6.0)
Sine WaveQRS-T Fusion; Pre-Terminal; Imminent VF/Asystole

9. Mind Map

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.4.2 Hypokalaemia
[!info]
Hypokalaemia = Serum K⁺ <3.5 mmol/L. Common Electrolyte Disorder. Life-Threatening Arrhythmia Risk (Especially with Digoxin). Always Check Mg²⁺ (Hypomagnesaemia Causes Refractory Hypokalaemia). ECG Changes: U Waves, ST Depression, QT Prolongation.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Recognise ECG changes of hypokalaemia and arrhythmia risk
  • [ ] Differentiate renal vs extrarenal causes using urine K⁺
  • [ ] Apply oral and IV potassium replacement protocols
  • [ ] Recognise and treat hypomagnesaemia as cause of refractory hypokalaemia
  • [ ] Manage hypokalaemia in special contexts (DKA, Digoxin Toxicity, Refeeding)

2. Definitions & Severity

SeveritySerum K⁺ (mmol/L)ECG ChangesClinical Risk
Mild3.0-3.5None / Subtle U WavesLow
Moderate2.5-3.0U Waves Prominent, ST Depression, T Wave FlatteningArrhythmia Risk ↑ (With Digoxin)
Severe<2.5Prominent U Waves, ST Depression, QT Prolongation, Flattened T WavesLife-Threatening Arrhythmias (VT/VF, Digoxin Toxicity)

2. Aetiology — Renal vs Extrarenal (Urine K⁺ Key Discriminator)

Renal Losses (Urine K⁺ >20 mmol/24h or Urine K⁺/Creatinine >13 mmol/mmol)

CauseMechanism
Diuretics (Loop, Thiazide)↑ Distal Na⁺ Delivery → ↑ K⁺ Secretion
Mineralocorticoid Excess (Primary Hyperaldosteronism, Cushing's, Liquorice, Carbenoxolone)ENaC Activation → ↑ K⁺ Secretion
Renal Tubular Acidosis (RTA)Distal Acidification Defect → ↑ K⁺ Wasting
Magnesium DeficiencyImpairs Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase & ROMK → Renal K⁺ Wasting
Renal Tubular Disorders (Bartter, Gitelman, Fanconi)Genetic Tubular Transport Defects
Diabetic Ketoacidosis (Post-Treatment)Insulin + K⁺ Shift In + Osmotic Diuresis
Hyperglycaemia / Osmotic Diuresis↑ Distal Flow → ↑ K⁺ Secretion

Extrarenal Losses (Urine K⁺ <20 mmol/24h)

CauseMechanism
GI Losses (Vomiting, Diarrhoea, Laxative Abuse, High-Output Stoma/Fistula)Direct K⁺ Loss + Volume Depletion → 2° Aldosterone ↑
Insulin / Alkalosis (Transcellular Shift)K⁺ Moves Into Cells (Not True Loss)
Inadequate IntakeMalnutrition, Anorexia, TPN without K⁺
SweatingMinor K⁺ Loss (Usually Not Sole Cause)

Transcellular Shift (Pseudohypokalaemia)

CauseMechanism
Insulin↑ Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase → K⁺ Shift Into Cells
AlkalosisH⁺ Moves Out of Cells → K⁺ Moves In
β₂-Agonists (Salbutamol, Isoprenaline)↑ cAMP → ↑ Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase
Hypothermia↓ Cellular Metabolism
Barium PoisoningBlocks K⁺ Channels

2. Clinical Presentation & ECG

SeverityK⁺ (mmol/L)ECG FindingsClinical Features
Mild3.0-3.5Subtle U WavesAsymptomatic or Mild Fatigue
Moderate2.5-3.0Prominent U Waves, ST Depression, T Wave FlatteningMuscle Weakness, Cramps, Polyuria, Constipation
Severe<2.5Prominent U Waves, ST Depression, QT Prolongation, Flattened T, ArrhythmiasParalysis, Ileus, Rhabdomyolysis, VT/VF, Torsades

ECG Hallmarks

ECG ChangeSignificance
U WavesMost Specific (Best Seen in V2-V3)
ST DepressionCommon (ST Segment Sagging)
T Wave Flattening/InversionOften Coexists with U Waves
QT ProlongationDue to Prominent U Waves Merging with T
ArrhythmiasEctopy, VT/VF, Torsades de Pointes (Especially with Digoxin)

3. Assessment Algorithm

HYPOKALAEMIA (K⁺ <3.5)
         │
         ▼
ECG IMMEDIATELY (Check for U Waves, QT Prolongation, Arrhythmias)
         │
         ▼
CHECK MAGNESIUM (Hypomagnesaemia → Refractory Hypokalaemia)
         │
         ▼
URINE K⁺ (24h or Spot K⁺/Creatinine Ratio)
         │
         ├── URINE K⁺ >20 mmol/24h (or K⁺/Cr >13) → **RENAL LOSSES**
         │       ├── Diuretics (Loop/Thiazide) → Reduce/Stop; K⁺ Sparing Diuretic
         │       ├── Mineralocorticoid Excess (Conn's, Cushing's, Liquorice) → Treat Cause
         │       ├── RTA (Distal) → Alkali Therapy + K⁺ Supplement
         │       ├── Bartter/Gitelman → K⁺ Supplement + NSAIDs (Bartter) / K⁺ Sparing
         │       ├── Mg²⁺ Deficiency → **Correct Mg²⁺ First** (Refractory Hypokalaemia)
         │       └── Post-DKA / Osmotic Diuresis → Monitor & Replace
         │
         └── URINE K⁺ <20 mmol/24h → **EXTRAreNAL / SHIFT**
                 ├── GI Losses (Vomiting, Diarrhoea, Laxatives) → Replace K⁺ + Fluid
                 ├── Transcellular Shift (Insulin, Alkalosis, β₂-Agonists) → Correct Cause
                 └── Inadequate Intake → Dietary K⁺ + Supplement

3. Management

Oral Replacement (Preferred for Asymptomatic/Moderate)

PreparationElemental K⁺Typical Dose
KCl Liquid20 mmol/15mL20-40 mmol TDS (60-120 mmol/d)
KCl Tablets (Slow-K)8 mmol (600mg)1-2 Tablets TDS (24-48 mmol/d)
KCl Effervescent (Sando-K)12 mmol/Tablet1-2 Tablets TDS (36-72 mmol/d)
Potassium Citrate12 mmol/Sachet1-2 Sachets TDS
Take with Food/Water to Reduce GI Irritation.

IV Replacement (Severe / Symptomatic / Unable Oral)

ParameterProtocol
IV Fluid0.9% NaCl or D5W (NOT 0.45% NaCl — Rapid K⁺ Shift)
ConcentrationMax 40 mmol/L (Peripheral); Up to 80 mmol/L (Central, Monitored)
RatePeripheral: 10 mmol/h Max; Central: 20-40 mmol/h (Cardiac Monitor)
Total Daily Dose40-80 mmol/day (Up to 120-160 mmol in Severe)
MonitoringSerum K⁺ q2-4h; ECG Continuous; Urine Output >0.5 mL/kg/h

Severe Hypokalaemia (K⁺ <2.5 / ECG Changes / Symptoms)

StepAction
1. Cardiac MonitorContinuous ECG
2. IV KCl20 mmol in 100mL 0.9% NaCl over 1h (Central: 20mmol in 50mL)
3. RepeatRecheck K⁺ q1-2h; Repeat Bolus Until K⁺ >3.0
4. Mg²⁺IV MgSO₄ 2-4g if Hypomagnesaemia
5. DigoxinStop/Reduce if Toxicity Suspected

3. Hypomagnesaemia & Refractory Hypokalaemia

FeatureDetails
MechanismMg²⁺ Required for Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase & ROMK Channel Function
Urine K⁺Inappropriately High Despite Hypokalaemia
ClinicalTetany, Seizures, Arrhythmias, Refractory Hypokalaemia
DiagnosisSerum Mg²⁺ <0.7 mmol/L
TreatmentIV MgSO₄ 2-4g (8-16 mmol) over 20-30 min; Then 1g/h Infusion
Key PrincipleCorrect Mg²⁺ FIRST — K⁺ Will Not Normalise Until Mg²⁺ Repleted

3. Special Contexts

ContextSpecific Considerations
Digoxin ToxicityHypokalaemia ↑ Digoxin Binding → Toxicity; Stop Digoxin; Correct K⁺ Urgently
DKA Post-TreatmentInsulin Drives K⁺ Into Cells; Monitor q1-2h; Replace Proactively
Refeeding SyndromeInsulin Surge → K⁺/PO₄/Mg²⁺ Shift In; Monitor q6h; Slow Calorie Introduction
Diuretic-InducedAdd K⁺-Sparing (Spironolactone 25-50mg / Amiloride 5-10mg)
Conn's SyndromePrimary Hyperaldosteronism → Hypokalaemia + HTN; CT Adrenals / AVS
Bartter/GitelmanGenetic; Hypokalaemia, Metabolic Alkalosis, Normal/ Low BP

3. Monitoring & Targets

ParameterTargetFrequency
Serum K⁺>4.0 mmol/Lq2-4h (IV); Daily (PO)
ECGResolution of U Waves, QT NormalisationContinuous (IV); Daily (PO)
Magnesium>0.7 mmol/Lq6-12h (IV); Daily (PO)
Urine Output>0.5 mL/kg/hHourly (IV)
Digoxin Level0.8-2.0 ng/mL (If on Digoxin)q24-48h

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Hypokalaemia DefinitionK⁺ <3.5 mmol/L (Moderate 2.5-3.0; Severe <2.5)
ECG HallmarksU Waves (Most Specific), ST Depression, QT Prolongation, T Wave Flattening
Urine K⁺ Cut-off>20 mmol/24h = Renal Loss; <20 = Extrarenal / Shift
Mg²⁺ DeficiencyCorrect Mg FIRST (Refractory Hypokalaemia; Mg Needed for K⁺ Retention)

IV KCl ConcentrationMax 40 mmol/L Peripheral; 80 mmol/L Central
Severe HypokalaemiaK⁺ <2.5 → IV KCl 20 mmol in 100mL over 1h (Cardiac Monitor)
Digoxin ToxicityHypokalaemia ↑ Digoxin Binding → Stop Digoxin, Correct K⁺ Urgently

Mg²⁺ RepletionIV MgSO₄ 2-4g over 20-30 min; Then 1g/h Infusion
Bartter/GitelmanHypokalaemia + Metabolic Alkalosis + Normal/Low BP; Genetic

K⁺ Replacement (Oral)40-80 mmol/day (Divided Doses with Food)
Severe Hypokalaemia ECGProminent U Waves, ST Depression, QT Prolongation → VT/VF Risk
Digoxin + HypokalaemiaStop Digoxin, Correct K⁺ Urgently (↑ Toxicity Risk)

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Renal vs ExtrarenalUrine K⁺ >20 = Renal; <20 = Extrarenal/Shift
Mg²⁺ & K⁺Correct Mg FIRST (Mg Needed for Na⁺/K⁺-ATPase & ROMK)
ECG U WavesMost Specific Sign of Hypokalaemia (Best Seen V2-V3)
Digoxin + HypokalaemiaStop Digoxin (↑ Toxicity Risk)
IV KCl RatePeripheral 10 mmol/h; Central 20-40 mmol/h (Monitored)
IV KCl ConcentrationPeripheral Max 40 mmol/L; Central Max 80 mmol/L
QT ProlongationDue to Prominent U Waves Merging with T Wave
Refractory HypokalaemiaCheck Mg²⁺ (<0.7 → Correct First)
Urine K⁺/Cr Ratio>13 mmol/mmol = Renal Loss (Alternative to 24h Urine)
Alkalosis + HypokalaemiaH⁺ Out → K⁺ In (Transcellular Shift, Not True Loss)

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.5 Acid-Base Disorders 5
▸ 19.5.1 Metabolic Acidosis
[!info]
Metabolic Acidosis = Primary ↓ HCO₃⁻ (<22 mmol/L) with Compensatory ↓ pCO₂. Primary Distinction: High Anion Gap (AGMA) vs Normal Anion Gap (NAGMA). MUDPILES Mnemonic for AGMA Causes.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Calculate anion gap and corrected anion gap (for hypoalbuminaemia)
  • [ ] Differentiate high anion gap (AGMA) from normal anion gap (NAGMA) metabolic acidosis
  • [ ] Apply MUDPILES and HARDASS mnemonics for aetiology
  • [ ] Calculate delta ratio and delta-delta for mixed disorders
  • [ ] Apply Winter's formula for respiratory compensation
  • [ ] Apply bicarbonate therapy indications and dosing

2. Definitions & Diagnostic Criteria

ParameterNormal RangeMetabolic Acidosis
pH7.35-7.45<7.35
HCO₃⁻22-26 mmol/L<22 mmol/L
pCO₂4.5-6.0 kPa (35-45 mmHg)Compensatorily Low
Anion Gap (AG)8-12 mmol/LHigh (>12) = AGMA; Normal (8-12) = NAGMA
Anion Gap (AG) = Na⁺ - (Cl⁻ + HCO₃⁻) [Normal 8-12 mmol/L]
Corrected AG (Hypoalbuminaemia) = AG + 2.5 × (40 - Albumin g/L)

2. Aetiology — High Anion Gap Metabolic Acidosis (AGMA)

MUDPILES Mnemonic

LetterCauseMechanism
MMethanolFormic Acid Accumulation
UUraemia (CKD Stage 4-5)Retained Organic Acids
DDKA (Diabetic Ketoacidosis)β-Hydroxybutyrate, Acetoacetate
PParaldehyde / Propylene GlycolOrganic Acid Metabolites
IIron / IsoniazidLactic Acid / Pyruvic Acid Accumulation
LLactic Acidosis (Type A: Hypoperfusion; Type B: Metabolic)Anaerobic Glycolysis / Mitochondrial Dysfunction
EEthylene Glycol / EthanolGlycolic/Oxalic Acid / Lactic Acidosis
SSalicylates / SepsisUncouples Oxidative Phosphorylation / Lactic Acidosis

Additional High AG Causes

CauseTypical Context
Pyroglutamic Acidosis (5-Oxoproline)Chronic Paracetamol Use, Malnutrition, Sepsis, Renal Failure
β-Hydroxybutyrate (Ketotic)Starvation, Alcoholism, Low-Carb Diet, Pregnancy
D-Lactic AcidosisShort Bowel Syndrome, Jejunoileal Bypass

2. Aetiology — Normal Anion Gap Metabolic Acidosis (NAGMA)

HARDASS Mnemonic

LetterCauseMechanism
HHyperalimentation (TPN)Ammonium Chloride Byproduct
AAcetazolamide↓ Proximal HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption
RRenal Tubular Acidosis (RTA)Distal (Type 1), Proximal (Type 2), Type 4 (Hypoaldosteronism)
DDiarrhoeaHCO₃⁻ Loss (Voluminous Watery)
AAdrenal Insufficiency (Addison's)Hypoaldosteronism (Type 4 RTA)
SSaline Infusion (0.9% NaCl)Hyperchloraemic (Dilutional)
SSpironolactone / Ureteric DiversionRenal HCO₃⁻ Loss

3. Diagnostic Algorithm

METABOLIC ACIDOSIS (HCO₃⁻ <22, pH <7.35)
         │
         ▼
CALCULATE ANION GAP (AG = Na⁺ - Cl⁻ - HCO₃⁻)
         │
         ├── **HIGH AG (>12)** → **AGMA**
         │       ├── **MUDPILES**: Methanol, Uraemia, DKA, Paraldehyde, Iron/Isoniazid, Lactic, Ethylene Glycol/Ethanol, Salicylates
         │       │
         │       └── **CALCULATE DELTA RATIO** (ΔAG / ΔHCO₃⁻)
         │               ├── 1-2 → **Pure AGMA**
         │               ├── <0.4 → **AGMA + NAGMA**
         │               ├── 0.4-0.8 → AGMA + NAGMA (Mild)
         │               └── >2 → **AGMA + Metabolic Alkalosis**
         │
         └── **NORMAL AG (8-12)** → **NAGMA**
                 ├── **HARDASS**: Hyperalimentation, Acetazolamide, RTA, Diarrhoea, Adrenal Insufficiency, Saline, Spironolactone
                 └── **ALWAYS EXCLUDE**: Renal Failure (Uraemia Can Raise AG)

3. Delta Ratio & Delta-Delta (Mixed Disorders)

RatioInterpretation
ΔAG / ΔHCO₃⁻1-2 → Pure AGMA
<0.4AGMA + NAGMA (Mixed High & Normal AG)
0.4-0.8AGMA + NAGMA (Mild NAGMA Component)
>2AGMA + Metabolic Alkalosis (Concurrent Alkalosis)

Delta-Delta Formula

Corrected HCO₃⁻ = Measured HCO₃⁻ + ΔAG
- Corrected HCO₃⁻ >24 → Concurrent Metabolic Alkalosis
- Corrected HCO₃⁻ <24 → Concurrent NAGMA

3. Respiratory Compensation — Winter's Formula

DisorderExpected Compensation
Metabolic AcidosisExpected pCO₂ = 1.5 × HCO₃⁻ + 8 ± 2
AssessmentIf Actual pCO₂ > Expected → Concurrent Respiratory Acidosis
If Actual pCO₂ < Expected → Concurrent Respiratory Alkalosis

3. Bicarbonate Therapy Indications

IndicationDose & Administration
pH <7.1 (Severe Acidaemia)8.4% NaHCO₃ 50-100 mmol IV over 30-60 min
Severe AKI (Urine Output <0.5 mL/kg/h)Same as Above
Severe Sepsis (Lactic Acidosis, pH <7.2)Consider 50-100 mmol
Cardiac Arrest50-100 mmol IV Bolus (Per Protocol)
DKANOT Routine (Risk of Paradoxical CNS Acidosis, Hypokalaemia, Volume Overload)
ContraindicatedRespiratory Acidosis (↑ CO₂ Production), Volume Overload, Alkalosis

Bicarbonate Dosing

PreparationDoseTarget
8.4% NaHCO₃50-100 mmol (50-100 mL) over 30-60 minpH >7.20
1.26% NaHCO₃ (1.4%)500-1000 mLIV Infusion (Less Concentrated)
Goal: Raise pH >7.20, Not Normalise pH. Avoid Overcorrection (Post-Hypercapnic Alkalosis).

3. Specific Causes — Key Features

Lactic Acidosis

TypeCauseK⁺/Glucose
Type A (Hypoperfusion)Shock, Sepsis, cardiac Arrest, Mesenteric IschaemiaVariable
Type B (Metabolic/Toxin)Metformin, HAART, Propofol, Thiamine Deficiency, Alcoholic KetoacidosisOften Euglycaemic (Metformin)

DKA vs HHS

FeatureDKAHHS
Glucose>11.1 mmol/L>33.3 mmol/L
KetonesPositive (β-HB, Acetoacetate)Negative/Trace
pH<7.3 (Often <7.1)>7.3
Anion GapHighNormal/Mildly High
OsmolalityElevatedVery High (>320)

Renal Tubular Acidosis (RTA)

TypeDefectKey Features
Type 1 (Distal)↓ H⁺ Secretion in Collecting DuctHypokalaemia, Nephrocalcinosis, Stones
Type 2 (Proximal)↓ HCO₃⁻ ReabsorptionFanconi Syndrome, Rickets, Glycosuria
Type 4 (Hypoaldosteronism)↓ Aldosterone / Renal ResistanceHyperkalaemia, Mild Acidosis, Diabetes/CKD

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Metabolic Acidosis DefinitionpH <7.35 + HCO₃⁻ <22
Anion GapNa⁺ - (Cl⁻ + HCO₃⁻); Normal 8-12; Correct for Albumin
AGMA CausesMUDPILES: Methanol, Uraemia, DKA, Paraldehyde, Iron/Isoniazid, Lactic, Ethylene Glycol, Salicylates
NAGMA CausesHARDASS: Hyperalimentation, Acetazolamide, RTA, Diarrhoea, Adrenal Insufficiency, Saline, Spironolactone
Delta RatioΔAG/ΔHCO₃⁻: 1-2 = Pure AGMA; <0.4 = AGMA+NAGMA; >2 = AGMA+Met Alk
Winter's FormulaExpected pCO₂ = 1.5 × HCO₃⁻ + 8 ± 2
Bicarb IndicationspH <7.1, Severe AKI, Sepsis pH<7.2, Cardiac Arrest
DKA BicarbNOT Routine (Paradoxical CNS Acidosis, Hypokalaemia)
Metformin Lactic AcidosisType B Lactic Acidosis; Euglycaemic; Stop Metformin; Haemodialysis
RTA TypesType 1 (Distal): Hypokalaemia; Type 2 (Proximal): Fanconi; Type 4: Hyperkalaemia
Salicylate ToxicityRespiratory Alkalosis + Metabolic Acidosis (Mixed)
Ethylene Glycol/MethanolOsmolar Gap ↑; Treat with Fomepizole/Ethanol + Dialysis
Winter's FormulaExpected pCO₂ = 1.5 × HCO₃⁻ + 8 ± 2
Corrected AG for AlbuminAG + 2.5 × (40 - Albumin g/L)

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
AGMA vs NAGMAAGMA = Anion Gap >12; NAGMA = AG 8-12
Delta Ratio1-2 = Pure AGMA; <0.4 = AGMA+NAGMA; >2 = AGMA+Met Alkalosis
Winter's FormulaExpected pCO₂ = 1.5 × HCO₃⁻ + 8 ± 2 (Metabolic Acidosis)
Respiratory CompensationIf Actual pCO₂ > Expected → Respiratory Acidosis Too
Bicarb in DKANot Routine (Paradoxical CNS Acidosis, Hypokalaemia, Volume Overload)
SalicylateMixed Picture: Respiratory Alkalosis + Metabolic Acidosis
Ethylene Glycol/MethanolOsmolar Gap ↑; Fomepizole/Ethanol + Dialysis
Pyroglutamic AcidosisChronic Paracetamol + Malnutrition/Sepsis/Renal Failure
5-OxoprolineUrine Organic Acids; Treated by N-acetylcysteine
DKA vs HHSDKA: pH<7.3, Ketones+, AGMA; HHS: pH>7.3, Glucose>33, Normal AG

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.5.2 Metabolic Alkalosis
[!info]
Metabolic Alkalosis = Primary ↑ HCO₃⁻ (>26 mmol/L) with Compensatory ↑ pCO₂. Most Common Acid-Base Disorder in Hospitalised Patients. Key Differentiation: Chloride-Responsive (Urine Cl⁻ <20) vs Chloride-Resistant (Urine Cl⁻ >20).

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Apply urine chloride to differentiate chloride-responsive from chloride-resistant metabolic alkalosis
  • [ ] Identify maintenance factors: volume depletion, hypokalaemia, hypochloraemia
  • [ ] Apply management: NaCl + KCl for responsive; acetazolamide/amiloride/spironolactone for resistant
  • [ ] Recognise specific causes: vomiting, diuretics, hyperaldosteronism, Cushing's, Bartter/Gitelman

2. Definitions & Diagnostic Criteria

ParameterNormal RangeMetabolic Alkalosis
pH7.35-7.45>7.45
HCO₃⁻22-26 mmol/L>26 mmol/L
pCO₂4.5-6.0 kPa (35-45 mmHg)Compensatorily Elevated
Compensation: Expected pCO₂ = 0.7 × HCO₃⁻ + 20 ± 5 (Max ~55-60 mmHg)

2. Aetiology — Chloride-Responsive vs Chloride-Resistant

Chloride-Responsive (Urine Cl⁻ <20 mmol/L) — Volume Depleted

CauseMechanism
Vomiting / NG SuctionLoss of HCl → HCO₃⁻ Retention; Volume Depletion → ↑ Aldosterone
Diuretic Use (Post-Diuretic Phase)Loop/Thiazide → Na⁺/Cl⁻ Loss + Volume Depletion → ↑ Aldosterone
Post-Hypercapnic StateChronic Hypercapnia → Renal HCO₃⁻ Compensation; Rapid Ventilation → Alkalosis
Nasogastric AspirationSimilar to Vomiting

Chloride-Resistant (Urine Cl⁻ >20 mmol/L) — Volume Normal/Expanded

CauseMechanism
Primary Hyperaldosteronism (Conn's)Aldosterone → ↑ Na⁺ Reabsorption / H⁺ & K⁺ Excretion
Cushing's SyndromeCortisol → Mineralocorticoid Effect
Bartter Syndrome (NKCC2/ROMK/CLCNKB)Loop-Like Diuretic Effect → Salt Wasting, Hypokalaemia, Alkalosis
Gitelman Syndrome (NCCT)Thiazide-Like Effect → Hypomagnesaemia, Hypocalciuria
Liquorice / Carbenoxolone11β-HSD2 Inhibition → Cortisol → Mineralocorticoid Receptor
Severe HypokalaemiaMaintains Alkalosis (H⁺ Shift In / K⁺ Shift Out)
Liddle SyndromeENaC Gain-of-Function → Na⁺ Retention, K⁺/H⁺ Loss

2. Maintenance Factors (Why Alkalosis Persists)

FactorMechanism
Volume Depletion↑ Aldosterone → ↑ Na⁺ Reabsorption → ↑ H⁺ Secretion
HypokalaemiaH⁺ Shifts Into Cells / K⁺ Shifts Out → ↑ Renal HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption
Hypochloraemia↓ Cl⁻/HCO₃⁻ Exchange in Collecting Duct → ↓ HCO₃⁻ Excretion
Reduced GFR↓ Filtered HCO₃⁻ Load → ↓ Excretion
Reduced Renal Blood Flow↑ Proximal HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption

3. Diagnostic Algorithm

METABOLIC ALKALOSIS (HCO₃⁻ >26, pH >7.45)
         │
         ├── MEASURE URINE CHLORIDE
         │       ├── **Urine Cl⁻ <20 mmol/L** → **CHLORIDE-RESPONSIVE**
         │       │       ├── Vomiting / NG Suction
         │       │       ├── Post-Diuretic (Loop/Thiazide)
         │       │       ├── Post-Hypercapnic State
         │       │       └── **MANAGEMENT**: **0.9% NaCl + KCl** Replacement
         │       │
         │       └── **Urine Cl⁻ >20 mmol/L** → **CHLORIDE-RESISTANT**
         │               ├── Primary Hyperaldosteronism (Conn's)
         │               ├── Cushing's Syndrome
         │               ├── Bartter / Gitelman Syndrome
         │               ├── Liquorice / Carbenoxolone
         │               ├── Severe Hypokalaemia (<3.0)
         │               └── **MANAGEMENT**: **Treat Cause** + Acetazolamide / Amiloride / Spironolactone

3. Clinical Features

SystemFeatures
NeuromuscularTetany (Hypocalcaemia from Alkalosis), Weakness, Tetany, Seizures
CardiovascularHypertension (Aldosterone/Cushing's), Arrhythmias (Hypokalaemia)
RespiratoryHypoventilation (Compensatory ↑ pCO₂), Apnoeic Spells
GastrointestinalNausea, Vomiting (May Be Cause or Effect)
RenalHypokalaemia (K⁺ Wasting), Polyuria (Hypokalaemia Nephropathy)
NeurologicalConfusion, Tremor, Seizures (If Severe Hypokalaemia/Hypocalcaemia)

3. Investigation

TestExpected in Metabolic AlkalosisDifferentiation
Arterial Blood GaspH >7.45, HCO₃⁻ >26, pCO₂ ↑ (Compensated)Primary Disorder
Urine Chloride<20 = Chloride-Responsive; >20 = Chloride-ResistantKey Differentiator
Serum ElectrolytesHypokalaemia (Common), Hypochloraemia, Hypocalcaemia (Ionised)Maintenance Factors
Serum Mg²⁺Often Low (Associated)Maintenance Factor
Urine K⁺High (K⁺ Wasting)Especially with Aldosterone Excess
ABG + CompensationpCO₂ ↑ ~0.7×ΔHCO₃⁻ (Max ~55 mmHg)Assess Compensation

3. Management

Chloride-Responsive (Urine Cl⁻ <20)

StepAction
1. Volume Repletion0.9% NaCl 1-2L Bolus → Then 100-150 mL/hr (Replace Volume)
2. Potassium ReplacementKCl 40-80 mmol/day PO (If K⁺ <4.0); IV if <3.0 / ECG Changes
3. MonitorNa⁺, K⁺, Cl⁻, HCO₃⁻, pH q6-12h; Fluid Balance
4. Stop LossesNG Suction (If Applicable), Stop Diuretics (If Possible)

Chloride-Resistant (Urine Cl⁻ >20)

CauseSpecific Management
Primary HyperaldosteronismSpironolactone 25-100mg BD / Eplerenone; Surgery if Adenoma
Cushing's SyndromeTreat Cause (Surgery, Medical, Adrenalectomy)
Bartter / GitelmanNSAIDs (Indomethacin 50-100mg TDS) + K⁺/Mg²⁺ Supplement; Spironolactone/Eplerenone
Liquorice/CarbenoxoloneStop Ingestion
Severe HypokalaemiaCorrect K⁺ First (IV KCl); Acetazolamide 250-500mg BD (↑ HCO₃⁻ Excretion)
Liddle SyndromeAmiloride 5-10mg BD / Triamterene (ENaC Blockers)

Acetazolamide (For Chloride-Resistant)

DoseIndication
250-500mg BDChloride-Resistant Metabolic Alkalosis (Failed Volume Repletion)
MechanismCA Inhibitor → ↑ HCO₃⁻ Excretion → Corrects Alkalosis
CautionsHypokalaemia, Metabolic Acidosis, Renal Stones, Paresthesias

3. Maintenance Factors (Why Alkalosis Persists)

FactorMechanism
Volume Depletion↑ Aldosterone → ↑ Na⁺ Reabsorption → ↑ H⁺ Secretion → ↑ HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption
HypokalaemiaH⁺ Shifts Into Cells / K⁺ Shifts Out → ↑ Renal NH₄⁺ Production → ↑ HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption
Hypochloraemia↓ Cl⁻/HCO₃⁻ Exchange (Pendrin) in Collecting Duct → ↓ HCO₃⁻ Excretion
Reduced GFR↓ Filtered HCO₃⁻ Load → ↓ Excretion
Reduced Renal Blood Flow↑ Proximal HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption (Sympathetic)

4. Compensation

ParameterFormula
Expected pCO₂0.7 × HCO₃⁻ + 20 ± 5
Max pCO₂~55-60 mmHg (Physiological Limit)
If Actual pCO₂ > ExpectedConcurrent Respiratory Acidosis
If Actual pCO₂ < ExpectedConcurrent Respiratory Alkalosis

4. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Metabolic AlkalosispH >7.45 + HCO₃⁻ >26
Urine Cl⁻ <20Chloride-Responsive → Volume Depletion → 0.9% NaCl + KCl
Urine Cl⁻ >20Chloride-Resistant → Aldosterone Excess → Treat Cause
Chloride-Responsive CausesVomiting, NG Suction, Diuretics (Post-Diuretic), Post-Hypercapnic
Chloride-Resistant CausesConn's, Cushing's, Bartter, Gitelman, Liquorice, Severe Hypokalaemia
Expected pCO₂0.7 × HCO₃⁻ + 20 ± 5 (Max ~55-60 mmHg)
HypokalaemiaMaintenance Factor (H⁺ Shift In → Alkalosis Worsens)
Vomiting Management0.9% NaCl + KCl (Fluid + Electrolyte Replacement)
Conn's SyndromeHypertension + Hypokalaemia + Metabolic Alkalosis + Low Uric Acid
Bartter/GitelmanHypokalaemia + Metabolic Alkalosis + Normal/Low BP; Gitelman = Hypomagnesaemia + Hypocalciuria
Liquorice11β-HSD2 Inhibition → Cortisol Acts on MR → Alkalosis + Hypokalaemia
Acetazolamide250-500mg BD (Cl-Resistant); CA Inhibitor → ↑ HCO₃⁻ Excretion
HypochloraemiaMaintenance Factor (↓ Cl⁻/HCO₃⁻ Exchange)
Urine Cl⁻ Cut-off<20 = Chloride-Responsive; >20 = Chloride-Resistant
CompensationpCO₂ = 0.7 × HCO₃⁻ + 20 (Max 55-60 mmHg)

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Urine Cl⁻ in Alkalosis<20 = Volume Depleted (Responsive); >20 = Mineralocorticoid Excess (Resistant)
Cl-Responsive vs ResistantResponsive = Volume Depleted → Saline; Resistant = Mineralocorticoid Excess
Vomiting vs DiureticBoth Cl⁻-Responsive; Vomiting = Acute; Diuretic = Post-Diuretic Phase
Bartter vs GitelmanBartter = Loop-Like (Hypercalciuria); Gitelman = Thiazide-Like (Hypocalciuria, Hypomagnesaemia)
Hypokalaemia MaintenanceH⁺ Shift In → Renal NH₄⁺ Genes → HCO₃⁻ Reabsorption
Acetazolamide250-500mg BD; ↑ HCO₃⁻ Excretion; Monitor K⁺, Acidosis
Urine Cl⁻ Cut-off<20 = Responsive; >20 = Resistant
HypochloraemiaMaintenance Factor (↓ Cl⁻/HCO₃⁻ Exchange)
Compensation LimitpCO₂ Max ~55-60 mmHg
Liquorice11β-HSD2 Inhibitor → Cortisol on MR → Alkalosis

9. Mind Map

▸ 19.5.3 Mixed Acid Base Disorders
[!info]
Mixed Acid-Base Disorder = >1 Primary Acid-Base Disturbance Simultaneously. Common in ICU (30-50% of ABGs). Systematic Approach Required: Identify Primary → Assess Compensation → Calculate Anion Gap + Delta Ratio → Identify All Components.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Apply systematic 4-step approach to ABG interpretation
  • [ ] Calculate anion gap, corrected anion gap, delta ratio, and delta-delta
  • [ ] Identify mixed disorders using compensation rules and delta ratio
  • [ ] Recognise classic mixed patterns: Salicylate, DKA+Vomiting, COPD+Diuretics, Sepsis+Diarrhoea
  • [ ] Apply management priorities for life-threatening mixed disorders

2. Systematic 4-Step ABG Interpretation

ARTERIAL BLOOD GAS (ABG) — MIXED DISORDER APPROACH
         │
         ├── STEP 1: pH
         │       ├── Acidæmia (pH <7.35) → Primary: Metabolic Acidosis OR Respiratory Acidosis
         │       └── Alkalaemia (pH >7.45) → Primary: Metabolic Alkalosis OR Respiratory Alkalosis
         │
         ├── STEP 2: Identify Primary Disorder
         │       ├── Acidæmia:
         │       │       ├── pCO₂ ↑ → Respiratory Acidosis (Primary)
         │       │       └── HCO₃⁻ ↓ → Metabolic Acidosis (Primary)
         │       │
         │       └── Alkalaemia:
         │               ├── pCO₂ ↓ → Respiratory Alkalosis (Primary)
         │               └── HCO₃⁻ ↑ → Metabolic Alkalosis (Primary)
         │
         ├── STEP 3: Assess Compensation (Expected vs Actual)
         │       ├── Metabolic Acidosis → Winter's Formula: Expected pCO₂ = 1.5 × HCO₃⁻ + 8 ± 2
         │       ├── Metabolic Alkalosis → Expected pCO₂ = 0.7 × HCO₃⁻ + 20 ± 5 (Max ~55-60)
         │       ├── Respiratory Acidosis (Acute): HCO₃⁻ ↑ 1/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑
         │       ├── Respiratory Acidosis (Chronic): HCO₃⁻ ↑ 4/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑
         │       ├── Respiratory Alkalosis (Acute): HCO₃⁻ ↓ 2/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓
         │       └── Respiratory Alkalosis (Chronic): HCO₃⁻ ↓ 5/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓
         │       │
         │       └── **Mismatch Actual vs Expected → Mixed Disorder**
         │
         └── STEP 4: Anion Gap + Delta Ratio (If Metabolic Acidosis Present)
                 ├── Calculate AG = Na⁺ - (Cl⁻ + HCO₃⁻); Corrected AG = AG + 2.5 × (40 - Albumin)
                 ├── If AGMA Present → Delta Ratio = ΔAG / ΔHCO₃⁻
                 │       ├── 1-2 → Pure AGMA
                 │       ├── <0.4 → AGMA + NAGMA
                 │       ├── 0.4-0.8 → AGMA + NAGMA (Mild)
                 │       └── >2 → AGMA + Metabolic Alkalosis
                 │
                 └── Delta-Delta: Corrected HCO₃⁻ = Measured HCO₃⁻ + ΔAG
                         ├── Corrected HCO₃⁻ >24 → Concurrent Metabolic Alkalosis
                         └── Corrected HCO₃⁻ <24 → Concurrent NAGMA

2. Delta Ratio & Delta-Delta — Core Tools

Delta Ratio (For AGMA)

Delta RatioInterpretation
1-2Pure AGMA (No Concurrent Metabolic Disorder)
<0.4AGMA + NAGMA (Concurrent Non-Gap Acidosis)
0.4-0.8AGMA + NAGMA (Mild NAGMA Component)
>2AGMA + Metabolic Alkalosis (Concurrent Alkalosis)

Delta-Delta (Corrected HCO₃⁻)

FormulaInterpretation
Corrected HCO₃⁻ = Measured HCO₃⁻ + ΔAG
Corrected HCO₃⁻ >24Concurrent Metabolic Alkalosis
Corrected HCO₃⁻ <24Concurrent NAGMA (Non-Gap Metabolic Acidosis)

2. Compensation Rules Quick Reference

Primary DisorderExpected CompensationRed Flag for Mixed Disorder
Metabolic AcidosisWinter's: pCO₂ = 1.5 × HCO₃⁻ + 8 ± 2Actual pCO₂ > Expected → Resp Acidosis Too
Metabolic AlkalosispCO₂ = 0.7 × HCO₃⁻ + 20 ± 5 (Max 55)Actual pCO₂ > Expected → Resp Acidosis Too
Respiratory Acidosis (Acute)HCO₃⁻ ↑ 1/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑HCO₃⁻ > Expected → Met Alkalosis Too
Respiratory Acidosis (Chronic)HCO₃⁻ ↑ 4/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑HCO₃⁻ < Expected → Met Acidosis Too
Respiratory Alkalosis (Acute)HCO₃⁻ ↓ 2/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓HCO₃⁻ < Expected → Met Acidosis Too
Respiratory Alkalosis (Chronic)HCO₃⁻ ↓ 5/10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓HCO₃⁻ > Expected → Met Alkalosis Too

2. Classic Mixed Acid-Base Patterns

1. Salicylate Toxicity (Classic Mixed)

ABG PatternMechanism
Respiratory Alkalosis + Metabolic AcidosisDirect Respiratory Centre Stimulation → Hyperventilation (Resp Alk); Uncouples Oxidative Phosphorylation → Lactic Acidosis (Met Acidosis)
Key FeaturesTinnitus, Hyperventilation, Altered Mental Status, Osmolar Gap ↑ (Early)
ManagementIV NaHCO₃ (Alkalinisation → ↑ Renal Excretion), Haemodialysis (Level >700 mg/L, Altered Mental Status, Renal Failure)

2. DKA + Vomiting / NG Suction

ABG PatternMechanism
AGMA (DKA) + Metabolic Alkalosis (Vomiting)DKA → AGMA; Vomiting → H⁺/Cl⁻ Loss → Metabolic Alkalosis
CluesHigh AG + HCO₃⁻ "Higher Than Expected" for AGMA; Urine Cl⁻ <20 (Cl-Responsive)

3. DKA + Diarrhoea / Renal Failure

ABG PatternMechanism
AGMA (DKA) + NAGMA (Diarrhoea/Renal)DKA → AGMA; Diarrhoea/Renal → HCO₃⁻ Loss (NAGMA)
CluesDelta Ratio <0.4; Urine Cl⁻ >20 (Renal) / <20 (GI)

4. COPD + Diuretic Use

ABG PatternMechanism
Chronic Respiratory Acidosis + Metabolic AlkalosisCOPD → Chronic Resp Acidosis (Compensated); Diuretics → Volume Depletion → Cl⁻-Responsive Metabolic Alkalosis
CluesHigh pCO₂ + High HCO₃⁻ (Higher Than Expected for Chronic Resp Acidosis); Urine Cl⁻ <20

5. COPD + DKA / Sepsis

ABG PatternMechanism
Chronic Respiratory Acidosis + AGMACOPD Baseline + DKA/Lactic Acidosis → AGMA Superimposed
CluesHCO₃⁻ Lower Than Expected for Chronic Resp Acidosis Alone

6. Sepsis + Diarrhoea

ABG PatternMechanism
Hyperventilation (Resp Alkalosis) + Lactic Acidosis + NAGMASepsis → Hyperventilation (Resp Alk) + Lactic Acidosis (AGMA) + Diarrhoea/Renal (NAGMA)

7. Triple Disorders

ExampleComponents
COPD + Diuretics + DKAChronic Resp Acidosis + Metabolic Alkalosis + AGMA
CKD + DKA + VomitingNAGMA (CKD) + AGMA (DKA) + Metabolic Alkalosis (Vomiting)
Salicylate + VomitingResp Alk + AGMA (Salicylate) + Metabolic Alkalosis (Vomiting)

3. Stepwise Approach to Any ABG

ABG INTERPRETATION ALGORITHM
         │
         ├── 1. pH: Acidæmia (<7.35) or Alkalaemia (>7.45)?
         │
         ├── 2. PRIMARY DISORDER (First Derangement)
         │       ├── Acidæmia: pCO₂↑ → Resp Acidosis; HCO₃⁻↓ → Met Acidosis
         │       └── Alkalaemia: pCO₂↓ → Resp Alkalosis; HCO₃⁻↑ → Met Alkalosis
         │
         ├── 3. COMPENSATION: Expected vs Actual
         │       ├── Winter's (Met Acidosis): pCO₂ = 1.5×HCO₃⁻ + 8±2
         │       ├── Met Alkalosis: pCO₂ = 0.7×HCO₃⁻ + 20±5 (Max 55)
         │       ├── Resp Acidosis Acute: HCO₃⁻↑1/10pCO₂; Chronic: HCO₃⁻↑4/10pCO₂
         │       ├── Resp Alkalosis Acute: HCO₃⁻↓2/10pCO₂; Chronic: HCO₃⁻↓5/10pCO₂
         │       └── Mismatch = Mixed Disorder
         │
         ├── 4. ANION GAP (If Met Acidosis)
         │       AG = Na⁺ - (Cl⁻ + HCO₃⁻); Norm 8-12; Corrected = AG + 2.5×(40-Alb)
         │       High AG → AGMA; Normal AG → NAGMA
         │
         ├── 5. DELTA RATIO (If AGMA)
         │       ΔRatio = ΔAG / ΔHCO₃⁻
         │       1-2 = Pure AGMA; <0.4 = AGMA+NAGMA; >2 = AGMA+Met Alk
         │
         └── 6. DELTA-DELTA (If AGMA)
                 Corrected HCO₃ = Measured HCO₃ + ΔAG
                 >24 = Metabolic Alkalosis Present; <24 = NAGMA Present

3. Common Mixed Patterns — Quick Recognition

Clinical ScenarioExpected ABG PatternKey Clue
Salicylate OverdoseResp Alk + Met AcidosisTinnitus, Hyperventilation, Osmolar Gap
DKA + VomitingHigh AG + High HCO₃⁻ (Higher Than Expected)Urine Cl⁻ <20; History of Vomiting
DKA + Diarrhoea/RenalAGMA + Delta Ratio <0.4Urine Cl⁻ <20 (GI) or >20 (Renal)
COPD + DiureticsHigh pCO₂ + High HCO₃⁻ (Higher Than Expected)Cl⁻-Responsive (Urine Cl⁻ <20)
COPD + DKAHigh pCO₂ + Lower HCO₃⁻ Than Expected (Chronic Resp)Known COPD + Hyperglycaemia
SepsisResp Alk (Early) → AGMA (Lactic) + NAGMA (Diarrhoea/Renal)SOFA Score ↑, Lactate ↑
SalicylateResp Alk + AGMA (Classic)Tinnitus, Osmolar Gap, AMS
Pregnancy + DKACompensated Resp Alk + AGMAPregnancy + Hyperglycaemia
COPD + DKAChronic Resp Acidosis + AGMAHCO₃⁻ Lower Than Expected for Chronic

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.5.4 Respiratory Acidosis
[!info]
Respiratory Acidosis = Primary ↑ pCO₂ (>6.0 kPa / 45 mmHg) → pH <7.35. Failure of Ventilation → CO₂ Retention. Acute vs Chronic Differentiation is Critical (Compensation Differs). COPD Exacerbation = Most Common Cause.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Differentiate acute vs chronic respiratory acidosis using compensation rules
  • [ ] Identify causes: airway obstruction, hypoventilation, CNS depression, mechanical ventilation issues
  • [ ] Apply NIV as first-line for COPD exacerbation
  • [ ] Recognise intubation criteria (pH <7.25, GCS <8, exhaustion)
  • [ ] Manage acute exacerbation of COPD with respiratory acidosis

2. Definitions & Diagnostic Criteria

ParameterNormalRespiratory Acidosis
pH7.35-7.45<7.35
pCO₂4.5-6.0 kPa (35-45 mmHg)>6.0 kPa (45 mmHg)
HCO₃⁻22-26 mmol/LNormal (Acute) / Elevated (Chronic)
pH7.35-7.45<7.35

2. Acute vs Chronic — Critical Distinction

FeatureAcute Respiratory AcidosisChronic Respiratory Acidosis
OnsetMinutes-HoursDays-Weeks (Pre-existing Lung Disease)
CompensationHCO₃⁻ ↑ 1 mmol/L per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑HCO₃⁻ ↑ 4 mmol/L per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑
pH Change per 10 mmHg pCO₂↓ 0.08↓ 0.03
HCO₃⁻ at pCO₂ 80 mmHg~24-26 mmol/L~36-40 mmol/L
Clinical ContextAcute Opiate Overdose, Asthma Attack, Pulmonary Oedema, PneumoniaCOPD, Obesity Hypoventilation, Neuromuscular Disease
Renal CompensationNone (Takes 2-5 Days)Complete (Renal HCO₃⁻ Retention)

2. Aetiology

CategoryCauses
Airway ObstructionCOPD Exacerbation (Most Common), Asthma (Status Asthmaticus), Croup, Foreign Body, Laryngeal Oedema
Hypoventilation (Central)Opiate/Sedative Overdose, CNS Depression (Stroke, Tumour, Encephalitis), Obesity Hypoventilation Syndrome, Neuromuscular Disease (MND, Guillain-Barré, Myasthenia Gravis)
Mechanical VentilationInadequate Tidal Volume/Rate, Auto-PEEP, Circuit Disconnection
Chest Wall / PleuralFlail Chest, Pneumothorax, Pleural Effusion, Kyphoscoliosis, Ankylosing Spondylitis

2. Clinical Presentation

FeatureAcuteChronic
Mental StatusConfusion, Drowsiness, Coma (Rapid)Chronic Confusion, Morning Headaches, Daytime Somnolence
RespiratorySevere Dyspnoea, Tachypnoea, Accessory Muscle UseChronic Dyspnoea, Orthopnoea, Cor Pulmonale Signs
NeurologicalTremor, Asterixis (CO₂ Narcosis), SeizuresPapilloedema (Rare), Polycythemia
CardiovascularTachycardia, Hypertension, ArrhythmiasCor Pulmonale (RVH, Peripheral Oedema, JVP↑)

3. Diagnostic Criteria

TestFinding
ABGpH <7.35, pCO₂ >6.0 kPa (45 mmHg), HCO₃⁻ Normal (Acute) / ↑ (Chronic)
Compensation AssessmentAcute: HCO₃⁻ ↑ 1/10 mmHg pCO₂; Chronic: HCO₃⁻ ↑ 4/10 mmHg pCO₂
CXRCOPD Changes, Consolidation, Oedema, Pneumothorax
SpirometryObstructive Pattern (COPD/Asthma), Restrictive (Neuromuscular/Chest Wall)
CT HeadIf CNS Depression Suspected (Stroke, Tumour, Haemorrhage)
Drug ScreenOpiates, Benzodiazepines, Alcohol

3. Compensation Rules

TypeExpected HCO₃⁻ Change per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑Expected pH Change per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↑
Acute↑ 1 mmol/L↓ 0.08
Chronic↑ 4 mmol/L↓ 0.03

Quick Assessment

pCO₂ (mmHg)Expected HCO₃⁻ (Acute)Expected HCO₃⁻ (Chronic)
6024-2628-30
7025-2732-34
8026-2836-38
9027-2940-42
If Actual HCO₃⁻ > Expected for Acute → Concurrent Metabolic Alkalosis
If Actual HCO₃⁻ < Expected for Chronic → Concurrent Metabolic Acidosis

3. Management Algorithm

RESPIRATORY ACIDOSIS (pH <7.35, pCO₂ >6.0 kPa)
         │
         ▼
ASSESS SEVERITY & ACUITY
         │
         ├── ACUTE / SEVERE (pH <7.25, pCO₂ >8.0 kPa, GCS <8, Exhaustion)
         │       → **INTUBATION + INVASIVE MECHANICAL VENTILATION**
         │
         ├── COPD EXACERBATION (pH 7.25-7.35, pCO₂ 6.0-8.0, Conscious)
         │       → **NON-INVASIVE VENTILATION (NIV / BiPAP)** — **1st Line**
         │       │       → IPAP 10-15, EPAP 4-5 cmH₂O; Titrate to pH >7.35
         │       │       → Monitor: pH, pCO₂, SpO₂, GCS q1-2h
         │       │
         │       └── IF NIV FAILS (pH <7.25, Deteriorating GCS, Exhaustion)
         │               → **INTUBATION + IPPV**
         │
         ├── CHRONIC STABLE (Compensated, Asymptomatic)
         │       → **OPTIMISE MAINTENANCE** (Bronchodilators, Steroids, Long-Term O₂)
         │
         └── OTHER CAUSES
                 ├── OPIATE OVERDOSE → **Naloxone 0.4-2mg IV** (Repeat/Infusion)
                 ├── NEUROMUSCULAR → **NIV** (BiPAP) / Tracheostomy + Ventilator
                 ├── OBESITY HYPOVENTILATION → **NIV (BiPAP)** + Weight Loss
                 └── MECHANICAL VENTILATION ISSUE → Adjust Tidal Volume/Rate

3. NIV (BiPAP) for COPD Exacerbation

ParameterSetting
ModeBiPAP (S/T Mode) or CPAP + Pressure Support
IPAP10-15 cmH₂O (Titrate to Tidal Volume 6-8 mL/kg)
EPAP4-5 cmH₂O (Counteract Auto-PEEP)
FiO₂Target SpO₂ 88-92% (Avoid Hyperoxia)
RateBackup Rate 12-15/min (S/T Mode)
MonitoringABG q1-2h (First 4h), SpO₂ Continuous, GCS q1h

NIV Failure Criteria (→ Intubation)

CriterionThreshold
pH<7.25 (Despite Optimal NIV 1-2h)
GCS<8 / Deteriorating
Respiratory Rate>35/min (Worsening)
HaemodynamicsSBP <90, Unstable Arrhythmia
Inability to Protect AirwayExcessive Secretions, Impaired Cough

3. Intubation Criteria (Absolute)

CriterionThreshold
pH<7.25 (Despite Optimal NIV)
GCS<8 / Unable to Protect Airway
Respiratory FatigueExhaustion, Paradoxical Breathing, Accessory Muscle Exhaustion
Haemodynamic InstabilitySBP <90 mmHg on Vasopressors
Severe HypoxaemiaSpO₂ <85% on FiO₂ 1.0 + NIV
Life-Threatening ArrhythmiaVF/VT, Severe Bradycardia

3. Specific Causes Management

CauseSpecific Management
COPD ExacerbationNIV 1st Line (BiPAP); Steroids 40-50mg Prednisolone 5d; Antibiotics if Purulent Sputum; Bronchodilators (SABA + SAMA Nebulisers)
Opiate OverdoseNaloxone 0.4-2mg IV/IM (Repeat q2-3min or Infusion 0.4-2mg/h); Observe 4-6h Post-Reversal
Asthma (Status Asthmaticus)NIV Caution (High Intrinsic PEEP Risk); Prefer Intubation + Low Tidal Volume (6-8 mL/kg) + Permissive Hypercapnia
Obesity HypoventilationBiPAP (High EPAP 8-10 cmH₂O); Weight Loss; Screen for OSA
NeuromuscularBiPAP (S/T Mode, Backup Rate); Consider Tracheostomy + Home Ventilator if Chronic
Pneumothorax / Pleural EffusionChest Drain (Urgent)

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.5.5 Respiratory Alkalosis
[!info]
Respiratory Alkalosis = Primary ↓ pCO₂ (<4.5 kPa / 35 mmHg) → pH >7.45. Hyperventilation → CO₂ Washout. Acute vs Chronic Compensation Differs. Common in ICU (Sepsis, Pain, Anxiety, Mechanical Ventilation).

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Differentiate acute vs chronic respiratory alkalosis using compensation rules
  • [ ] Identify causes: anxiety, pain, sepsis, hepatic encephalopathy, salicylate, pregnancy, mechanical ventilation
  • [ ] Apply compensation rules to assess mixed disorders
  • [ ] Manage underlying cause (treat anxiety, sepsis, adjust ventilator)

2. Definitions & Diagnostic Criteria

ParameterNormalRespiratory Alkalosis
pH7.35-7.45>7.45
pCO₂4.5-6.0 kPa (35-45 mmHg)<4.5 kPa (35 mmHg)
HCO₃⁻22-26 mmol/LNormal (Acute) / Decreased (Chronic)
pH7.35-7.45>7.45

2. Acute vs Chronic — Compensation Rules

FeatureAcute Respiratory AlkalosisChronic Respiratory Alkalosis
OnsetMinutes-HoursDays-Weeks
CompensationHCO₃⁻ ↓ 2 mmol/L per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓HCO₃⁻ ↓ 5 mmol/L per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓
pH Change per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓↑ 0.08↑ 0.03
HCO₃⁻ at pCO₂ 20 mmHg20-22 mmol/L12-14 mmol/L
Clinical ContextAnxiety, Pain, Sepsis (Early), Salicylates, Mechanical VentilationPregnancy, High Altitude, Chronic Liver Disease, Chronic Hypoxia

2. Aetiology

CategoryCauses
Psychogenic / BehaviouralAnxiety, Panic Disorder, Hysteria, Hyperventilation Syndrome
Pain / TraumaSevere Pain, Post-Operative, Fractures
CNSStroke (Brainstem), Meningitis, Encephalitis, Tumour, Subarachnoid Haemorrhage
PulmonaryPE (Early), Pneumonia, Interstitial Lung Disease, Pneumothorax, Asthma
Sepsis / SIRSEarly Sepsis (Cytokine-Mediated Hyperventilation), ARDS (Early)
HepaticHepatic Encephalopathy (Portosystemic Shunting → Ammonia → Respiratory Centre Stimulation)
Drugs / ToxinsSalicylates (Aspirin Overdose — Mixed: Resp Alk + Met Acidosis), Progesterone, Caffeine, Theophylline, Naloxone
PregnancyProgesterone → ↑ Respiratory Drive (Normal in 2nd/3rd Trimester)
Mechanical VentilationExcessive Rate/Tidal Volume, Inappropriate Settings
EndocrineThyrotoxicosis, Diabetic Ketoacidosis (Early)

2. Acute vs Chronic — Compensation Rules

Chronic↓ 5 mmol/L↑ 0.03

3. Clinical Presentation

FeatureAcuteChronic
SymptomsPerioral Paraesthesia, Carpopedal Spasm (Tetany), Dizziness, Palpitations, AnxietyOften Asymptomatic (Compensated); Chronic Dyspnoea (If Hepatic/Pulmonary)
SignsTrousseau's/Chvostek's Signs (Hypocalcaemia from Alkalosis), TetanyOften Subtle (Adapted); Underlying Disease Signs
ABGpH >7.45, pCO₂ <4.5 kPa (35 mmHg), HCO₃⁻ Normal/Slightly ↓pH >7.45, pCO₂ <4.5 kPa, HCO₃⁻ Decreased
NeurologicalConfusion, Lightheadedness, Syncope (Cerebral Vasoconstriction)Subtle Cognitive Changes (If Hepatic Encephalopathy)

3. Differential Diagnosis of Hypocapnia

ConditionpCO₂HCO₃⁻Key Differentiator
Acute Respiratory Alkalosis<4.5 kPaNormal/Slightly ↓Anxiety, Pain, Sepsis, Salicylates
Chronic Respiratory Alkalosis<4.5 kPaMarkedly DecreasedPregnancy, Liver Disease, High Altitude
Compensated Metabolic Acidosis<4.5 kPaLow (Primary ↓ HCO₃⁻)Primary Low HCO₃⁻ (Winter's Formula)
Mixed: Resp Alk + Met Acidosis<4.5 kPaLowSalicylates, Sepsis, PE
Mixed: Resp Alk + Met Alkalosis<4.5 kPaHighRare (e.g., Vomiting + Hyperventilation)

3. Key Causes — Clinical Pearls

Salicylate Toxicity (Classic Mixed Disorder)

FeatureDetails
PatternRespiratory Alkalosis + Metabolic Acidosis (Mixed)
MechanismDirect Respiratory Centre Stimulation + Uncouples Oxidative Phosphorylation → Lactic Acidosis
DiagnosisSerum Salicylate Level; ABG: Mixed Resp Alk + Met Acidosis; Ferric Chloride Test (Urine)
ManagementIV Fluids, Alkalinisation (NaHCO₃ → ↑ Renal Excretion), Dialysis (Severe >700 mg/L, Altered Mental Status, Renal Failure)

Hepatic Encephalopathy

FeatureDetails
MechanismAmmonia → Cerebral Oedema → Respiratory Centre Stimulation
ABGChronic Respiratory Alkalosis (Low pCO₂, Low HCO₃⁻)
Other FeaturesAsterixis, Confusion, Fetor Hepaticus, Ascites

Pregnancy

FeatureDetails
MechanismProgesterone → ↑ Respiratory Drive
ABGCompensated Chronic Respiratory Alkalosis (pH ~7.45-7.50, pCO₂ ~27-32 mmHg, HCO₃⁻ ~18-22)
Normal in 2nd/3rd TrimesterNot Pathological

Mechanical Ventilation

ScenarioManagement
IatrogenicReduce Respiratory Rate / Tidal Volume / Minute Ventilation
Permissive HypercapniaTarget pH >7.20 (ARDS) / Accept pCO₂ 50-60 mmHg

3. Management

Primary Principle

StepAction
1. Treat Underlying CauseAnxiety (Rebreathing/Anxiolytics), Pain (Analgesia), Sepsis (Antibiotics), Salicylates (Alkalinisation/Haemodialysis), Hepatic Encephalopathy (Lactulose/Rifaximin), Adjust Ventilator
2. Symptomatic ReliefRebreathing (Paper Bag) for Anxiety-Induced; Calcium Gluconate for Tetany
3. Correct HypocalcaemiaIV Calcium Gluconate 10% 10mL if Tetany/Seizures (Alkalosis → ↓ Ionised Ca²⁺)
4. Ventilator AdjustmentReduce Rate / Tidal Volume / Minute Volume; Allow Permissive Hypercapnia if Tolerated

3. Complications & Monitoring

ComplicationMechanismMonitoring
Cerebral VasoconstrictionHypocapnia → ↓ CBF → Dizziness, Syncope, SeizuresNeurological Assessment, Continuous EEG if Seizures
HypocalcaemiaAlkalosis → ↑ Protein Binding → ↓ Ionised Ca²⁺ → TetanyIonised Ca²⁺ q4-6h; Replace if Symptomatic
HypokalaemiaAlkalosis → K⁺ Shift Into CellsK⁺ q4-6h; Replace if <3.0
Left Shift ODCAlkalosis → ↑ Hb-O₂ Affinity → ↓ Tissue O₂ DeliveryMonitor Tissue Perfusion, Lactate
Paradoxical CNS AcidosisRapid Correction of Chronic Alk → CSF pCO₂ ↑ Faster Than BloodSlow Weaning of Ventilator

9. Mind Map

Respiratory Alkalosis
Definition
pH >7.45, pCO₂ <4.5 kPa (35 mmHg)
Acute vs Chronic
Acute: HCO3 ↓2/10mmHg, pH↑0.08
Chronic: HCO3 ↓5/10mmHg, pH↑0.03
Pregnancy: Chronic, Compensated
Causes
Psychogenic: Anxiety, Panic
Pain, Trauma, Post-Op
CNS: Stroke, Meningitis, SAH
Sepsis (Early)
Pulmonary: PE, Pneumonia
Salicylate Toxicity
Hepatic Encephalopathy
Pregnancy (Progesterone)
Mechanical Ventilation
Compensation
Acute: HCO3 ↓2/10mmHg pCO2
Chronic: HCO3 ↓5/10mmHg pCO2
Mixed Disorders
Salicylate: Resp Alk + Met Acidosis
Sepsis: Resp Alk + Met Acidosis (Lactic)
Pregnancy: Pure Chronic Resp Alk
Management
Treat Cause
Rebreathing (Paper Bag) for Anxiety
Calcium Gluconate for Tetany
Ventilator Adjust (Reduce Rate/Vt)
Salicylate
Resp Alk + Met Acidosis (Mixed)
Alkalinisation (NaHCO3) + Dialysis (Severe)

9. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Respiratory AlkalosispH >7.45 + pCO₂ <4.5 kPa (35 mmHg)
Acute CompensationHCO₃⁻ ↓2 mmol/L per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓
Chronic CompensationHCO₃⁻ ↓5 mmol/L per 10 mmHg pCO₂ ↓
Salicylate ToxicityMixed: Respiratory Alkalosis + Metabolic Acidosis
Hepatic EncephalopathyChronic Respiratory Alkalosis (Ammonia)
PregnancyProgesterone → Compensated Chronic Respiratory Alkalosis
Pregnancy ABGpH ~7.45-7.50, pCO₂ ~27-32 mmHg, HCO₃⁻ ~18-22
Mechanical VentilationReduce Rate/Tidal Volume; Permissive Hypercapnia
Salicylate ToxicityMixed: Resp Alk + Met Acidosis; Alkalinisation + Dialysis
Cerebral VasoconstrictionHypocapnia → ↓ CBF → Syncope, Seizures
Hypocalcaemia in AlkalosisAlkalosis → ↑ Protein Binding → ↓ Ionised Ca²⁺ → Tetany
IV Calcium Gluconate10% 10mL IV for Tetany/Seizures
RebreathingPaper Bag for Anxiety Hyperventilation
Pregnancy ABGCompensated Chronic Resp Alkalosis (Normal)
Mixed Disorder: SalicylateResp Alkalosis + Met Acidosis (Unique Pattern)

▸ 19.6 Metabolic Bone Disease 4
▸ 19.6.1 Osteomalacia
[!info]
Osteomalacia / Rickets = Defective Mineralisation of Osteoid (Vitamin D / Calcium / Phosphate Deficiency). Adults = Osteomalacia; Children = Rickets (Growth Plate Involvement). Biochemical Hallmark: ↑ ALP, ↓ Phosphate, ↓ 25-OH Vit D, ↑ PTH (2° HPT).

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Differentiate osteomalacia (adult) from rickets (child) and osteoporosis
  • [ ] Identify causes: Vitamin D deficiency, calcium/phosphate deficiency, renal disease, drug-induced
  • [ ] Recognise clinical features: bone pain, proximal myopathy, fractures, deformities (rickets)
  • [ ] Apply biochemical diagnosis: ↓ PO₄, ↑ ALP, ↓ 25-OH D, ↑ PTH
  • [ ] Apply management: Vitamin D replacement (loading + maintenance), calcium, phosphate if needed

2. Pathophysiology

FeatureDetails
Core DefectDefective Mineralisation of Osteoid (Unmineralised Osteoid Accumulates)
AdultsOsteomalacia (Closed Growth Plates)
ChildrenRickets (Open Growth Plates → Deformities)
Key MediatorVitamin D (↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D → ↓ Intestinal Ca²⁺/PO₄ Absorption) → ↓ Ca²⁺×PO₄ Product

2. Aetiology — Causes of Osteomalacia / Rickets

Vitamin D Deficiency (Most Common)

CauseMechanism
Low Sunlight ExposureHousebound, Institutionalised, Dark Skin, High Latitude, Veiled Clothing
MalabsorptionCoeliac, Crohn's, Cystic Fibrosis, Bariatric Surgery, Short Bowel, Cholestatic Liver Disease
Renal DiseaseCKD → ↓ 1α-Hydroxylase → ↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D
Hepatic Failure↓ 25-Hydroxylation
Drug-InducedEnzyme Inducers: Phenytoin, Carbamazepine, Rifampicin, Isoniazid, Antiretrovirals (EFV, NVP)

Calcium / Phosphate Deficiency

DeficiencyMechanism
Calcium DeficiencyLow Intake, Malabsorption, Hypoparathyroidism
Phosphate DeficiencyFanconi Syndrome, X-Linked Hypophosphataemic Rickets (XLH), Oncogenic Osteomalacia, Tumour Lysis, Refeeding Syndrome

Renal Disease

TypeMechanism
CKD↓ 1α-Hydroxylase → ↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D; Hyperphosphataemia; ↓ Ca²⁺ Absorption
Renal Tubular DisordersFanconi Syndrome (Proximal Tubular Dysfunction → PO₄ Wasting), XLH (PHEX Mutation → ↑ FGF23), Oncogenic Osteomalacia (FGF23-Secreting Tumour)

2. Clinical Features

Adults — Osteomalacia

FeatureDetails
Bone PainProximal Myopathy (Thighs, Shoulders), Diffuse Bone Pain (Ribs, Spine, Pelvis)
FracturesLooser's Zones (Pseudofractures), Pathological Fractures
MuscularProximal Myopathy (Waddling Gait, Difficulty Rising), Muscle Weakness
BiochemicalLow Ca²⁺/Normal, ↓ Phosphate, ↑ ALP, ↓ 25-OH D, ↑ PTH

Children — Rickets

FeatureDetails
SkeletalCraniotabes (Soft Skull), Harrison's Groove (Costochondral Junction), Rachitic Rosary, Wrist/Ankle Widening, Bow Legs (Genu Varum), Knock Knees (Genu Valgum)
GrowthFailure to Thrive, Delayed Walking, Stunted Growth
MuscularHypotonia, Proximal Myopathy, Delayed Motor Milestones
DentalDelayed Eruption, Enamel Hypoplasia, Caries
BiochemicalLow Ca²⁺, ↓ Phosphate, ↑ ALP, ↓ 25-OH D, ↑ PTH

2. Biochemical Diagnosis

TestNormalOsteomalacia / Rickets
Serum Calcium (Corrected)2.15-2.55 mmol/LLow / Normal
Ionised Calcium1.15-1.30 mmol/LLow / Normal
Serum Phosphate0.8-1.5 mmol/LLow (<0.8)
ALP30-130 U/LMarkedly Elevated (Disproportionate to Other LFTs)
PTH1.6-6.9 pmol/LElevated (2° HPT)
25-OH Vitamin D>50 nmol/L (20 ng/mL)Low (<25 nmol/L = Deficiency)
1,25-(OH)₂D75-220 pmol/LLow / Normal
FGF23<100 RU/mLHigh (If XLH/Oncogenic)
ALP IsoenzymesLiver/BoneBone ALP ↑

2. Differential Diagnosis

ConditionCa²⁺PO₄ALPPTH25-OH DKey Differentiator
OsteomalaciaLow/NormalLowHighHighLow↓ 25-OH D, ↑ PTH
OsteoporosisNormalNormalNormal/↑NormalNormalT-Score ≤-2.5, Normal PO₄/ALP
Renal OsteodystrophyLow/NormalHighHigh/↑Very HighLow/NormalHigh Creatinine, ↑ FGF23
Hypophosphataemic Rickets (XLH)NormalLowHighNormalNormalFGF23 ↑, Genetic (PHEX)
Oncogenic OsteomalaciaNormalLowHighNormalNormalFGF23 ↑, Tumour (Mesenchymal)
Hypophosphataemia (Other)NormalLowNormal/↑Normal/↑NormalCause-Specific (Fanconi, Antacids, Refeeding)

3. Management

Vitamin D Replacement (Core Therapy)

RegimenDoseDuration
Loading (Severe Deficiency <12 ng/mL)Cholecalciferol 50,000 IU Weekly × 6-8 WeeksUntil 25-OH D >30 ng/mL
Loading (Moderate Deficiency 12-20 ng/mL)50,000 IU Weekly × 4-6 WeeksUntil 25-OH D >30 ng/mL
MaintenanceCholecalciferol 800-2000 IU/day (or 50,000 IU Monthly)Lifelong if Risk Factors Persist

Calcium Supplementation

PreparationElemental Ca²⁺Dose
Calcium Carbonate40% (400mg/tablet)1-2g TDS with Meals
Calcium Citrate21%1-2g TDS (Better if Achlorhydria)
Target1.5-2g/day ElementalDivided Doses

Phosphate Replacement (If Hypophosphataemic)

PreparationDose
Phosphate Sandoz1-2 Tablets TDS (~16 mmol PO₄ each)
Neutraphos1-2 Packets QID (~8 mmol PO₄ each)
IV Phosphate (Severe <0.3)15-30 mmol over 6-12h (Monitor Ca²⁺)

Paediatric Dosing (Rickets)

AgeDeficiency TreatmentMaintenance
0-1 Year2,000 IU/day × 6 Weeks → 400-1,000 IU/day400-1,000 IU/day
1-18 Years50,000 IU Weekly × 6 Weeks → 600-1,000 IU/day600-1,000 IU/day

3. X-Ray Findings (Rickets / Osteomalacia)

FindingDescription
Looser's Zones (Pseudofractures)Transverse Lucent Lines Perpendicular to Cortex (Ribs, Femoral Neck, Pubic Rami)
Rachitic RosaryCostochondral Junction Widening (Costal Cartilage Hypertrophy)
Harrison's GrooveCostal Margin Indrawing at Diaphragm Attachment
Wrist/Ankle WideningMetaphyseal Cupping, Fraying, Widening
Bow Legs / Knock KneesGenu Varum / Valgum (Weight-Bearing Deformities)
CraniotabesSoftening of Skull Bones (Ping-Pong Ball Feel)

3. Special Causes & Management

Oncogenic Osteomalacia (Tumour-Induced)

FeatureDetails
MechanismFGF23-Secreting Tumour → Renal Phosphate Wasting + ↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D
Tumour TypeMesenchymal (Haemangiopericytoma, Fibrous Tumours, Osteoblastoma)
Biochemical↓ PO₄, ↑ FGF23, FEP >5%, Normal PTH, Low 1,25-(OH)₂D
ManagementTumour Resection (Curative); Pre-Op Phosphate + Calcitriol

X-Linked Hypophosphataemic Rickets (XLH)

FeatureDetails
GenePHEX (X-Linked Dominant)
Mechanism↓ PHEX → ↑ FGF23 → Renal Phosphate Wasting + ↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D
ClinicalRickets (Childhood), Osteomalacia (Adult), Short Stature, Dental Abscesses
ManagementBurosumab (Anti-FGF23 mAb) 0.8mg/kg SC q2wk (Child) / 1mg/kg q4wk (Adult); Phosphate + Calcitriol (Traditional)

Renal Osteodystrophy (See Separate Note)

Key PointSee Renal Osteodystrophy Note for Full Details

3. Monitoring & Follow-Up

ParameterFrequencyTarget
25-OH Vitamin D3-4 Months Post-Loading → Then q6-12mo>50 nmol/L (20 ng/mL)
Serum Calciumq3-6mo2.15-2.55 mmol/L
Serum Phosphateq3-6mo>0.8 mmol/L
ALPq3-6moNormalisation (Marker of Healing)
PTHq6-12moNormalisation
Bone DensityDEXA q2-3yr (Adults)T-Score Improvement

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Osteomalacia vs RicketsAdults = Osteomalacia; Children = Rickets (Open Growth Plates)
Biochemical HallmarkLow Phosphate, High ALP, High PTH, Low 25-OH D
Osteomalacia vs OsteoporosisOsteomalacia: ↓ PO₄, ↑ ALP, ↑ PTH; Osteoporosis: Normal PO₄/ALP, Normal PTH
Vitamin D Loading50,000 IU Weekly × 6-8 Weeks (Severe Deficiency <12 ng/mL)
Maintenance Dose800-2000 IU/day Cholecalciferol
Looser's ZonesPseudofractures (Ribs, Femoral Neck, Pubic Rami) — Pathognomonic
Rachitic RosaryCostochondral Junction Widening (Rickets)
Looser's ZonesPseudofractures — Pathognomonic for Osteomalacia
XLH TreatmentBurosumab (Anti-FGF23 mAb) — 1st Line (Replaces Phosphate + Calcitriol)
Oncogenic OsteomalaciaTumour Resection (Curative); FGF23-Secreting Mesenchymal Tumour
Antacid-InducedAl/Mg/Ca Antacids Bind Phosphate → Chronic Hypophosphataemia
Renal OsteodystrophyHigh Phosphate, High PTH, Low 1,25-(OH)₂D (See Renal Osteodystrophy Note)
Vitamin D Loading50,000 IU Weekly × 6-8 Weeks (Severe Deficiency)
Maintenance800-2000 IU/day Cholecalciferol

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Osteomalacia vs OsteoporosisOsteomalacia = ↓ PO₄, ↑ ALP, ↑ PTH (Mineralisation Defect); Osteoporosis = Normal PO₄/ALP/PTH (Mass Defect)
Rickets vs OsteomalaciaRickets = Children (Open Growth Plates → Deformities); Osteomalacia = Adults
Osteomalacia vs Renal OsteodystrophyRenal = High PO₄, High FGF23, High Creatinine; Osteomalacia = Low PO₄, Low Creatinine
XLH vs OncogenicXLH = Genetic (PHEX); Oncogenic = Acquired Tumour (FGF23) — Both High FGF23
Looser's ZonesPseudofractures — Pathognomonic for Osteomalacia
Rachitic RosaryCostochondral Widening (Rickets)
FGF23Key Mediator: XLH, Oncogenic, ADHR → ↑ FGF23 → ↓ Renal PO₄ Reabsorption
Vitamin D Loading50,000 IU Weekly × 6-8 Weeks (Severe Def <12 ng/mL)
Maintenance800-2000 IU/day Cholecalciferol (Not Calcitriol Unless CKD)

MCQs (10)

  1. Osteomalacia definition:

A. Low bone mass

B. Impaired mineralization of bone

C. High bone turnover

  1. Most common cause:

A. Vit D deficiency

B. Phosphate deficiency

C. Renal failure

D. Anticonvulsants

B. Osteomalacia

C. Paget disease

D. Osteitis fibrosa

C. Phosphate wasting

D. All of the above

A. 400-800 IU/d

B. 10,000 IU/d

C. 50,000 IU/d

D. 100,000 IU/d

A. 1000 IU/d

B. 50,000 IU weekly x 8w

C. 100,000 IU daily

D. 1,000,000 IU monthly

A. Same disease, different age

B. Different diseases

D. Osteomalacia = child

A. Vit D deficiency

B. FGF23 excess

C. Ca deficiency

D. PTH excess

  1. Most common cause in CKD:

C. Vit D deficiency

D. Hyperparathyroidism

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.6.2 Osteoporosis
[!info]
Osteoporosis = Systemic Skeletal Disease with Low Bone Mass & Microarchitectural Deterioration → Increased Fragility Fracture Risk. DEXA T-Score ≤-2.5 = Osteoporosis. FRAX for 10-Year Fracture Probability. Bisphosphonates 1st Line; Denosumab Alternative; Anabolics (Teriparatide/Romosozumab) for Severe.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Diagnose osteoporosis using DEXA T-scores and clinical risk factors
  • [ ] Apply FRAX tool for 10-year major osteoporotic/hip fracture probability
  • [ ] Apply treatment thresholds (NOF, NICE, ESCEO guidelines)
  • [ ] Prescribe first-line (bisphosphonates) and second-line (denosumab, teriparatide, romosozumab) therapies
  • [ ] Manage glucocorticoid-induced osteoporosis (GIOP)
  • [ ] Monitor treatment efficacy and duration (drug holidays)

2. Definition & Diagnosis

WHO Criteria (DEXA T-Scores)

CategoryT-Score (SD from Young Adult Mean)
Normal≥-1.0 SD
Osteopenia-1.0 to -2.5 SD
Osteoporosis≤-2.5 SD
Severe/Established≤-2.5 SD + Fragility Fracture

Measurement Sites: Lumbar Spine (L1-L4) + Total Hip / Femoral Neck (Lowest T-Score Used).

2. Fracture Risk Assessment — FRAX® Tool

FRAX® (WHO) — 10-Year Major Osteoporotic Fracture / Hip Fracture Probability

Input VariablesRequired
Age, Sex, Weight, HeightMandatory
Previous FractureYes/No
Parent Hip FractureYes/No
Current SmokingYes/No
GlucocorticoidsCurrent/Past (>5mg Pred >3mo)
Rheumatoid ArthritisYes/No
Secondary OsteoporosisT1DM, Untreated Hypothyroidism, etc.
Alcohol ≥3 units/dayYes/No
BMD (Femoral Neck)Optional (Improves Accuracy)

Treatment Thresholds (UK / NOGG)

ScenarioIntervention Threshold (10-Year Probability)
Major Osteoporotic Fracture≥7.5% (Age 50-59) → ≥15% (Age 70+)
Hip Fracture≥3% (Age 50-59) → ≥4.5% (Age 70+)

2. Clinical Risk Factors for Fracture

CategoryRisk Factors
Non-ModifiableAge >65, Female, Caucasian/Asian, Family History (Parent Hip Fracture), Previous Fragility Fracture, Early Menopause (<45), Low BMI (<19)
ModifiableLow BMI, Smoking, Alcohol >3 Units/Day, Sedentary, Low Calcium/Vit D Intake, Falls Risk
DiseasesRA, T1DM, Hyperthyroidism, Coeliac, IBD, Chronic Liver/Kidney Disease, Anorexia, Premature Menopause, Premature Andropause

3. Secondary Causes of Osteoporosis (Always Exclude)

CategoryConditions
EndocrineHyperthyroidism, Hyperparathyroidism, Cushing's, Hypogonadism (Male/Female), T1DM, Acromegaly
GICoeliac, IBD, Gastrectomy, Bariatric Surgery, Chronic Pancreatitis
HaematologicalMultiple Myeloma, Lymphoma, Leukaemia
RheumatologicalRA, Ankylosing Spondylitis, SLE
MedicationsGlucocorticoids (>5mg Pred >3mo), Aromatase Inhibitors, AEDs (Enzyme Inducers), PPIs (Long-Term), Heparin, Methotrexate, Depo-Provera, GnRH Analogues
OtherImmobilisation, Organ Transplant, HIV, HIV Meds (TDF), Loop Diuretics

3. Diagnosis & Workup

Essential Investigations

TestPurpose
DEXA (Lumbar Spine + Hip)Gold Standard — T-Score Diagnosis
Lateral Spine X-Ray / VFAVertebral Fracture Assessment (VFA) — Silent Fractures
BloodsCa, Phos, ALP, 25-OH Vit D, TSH, TFTs, FBC, U&E, LFT, FSH/LH/Oestradiol (Women), Testosterone (Men), 25-OH Vit D
Fracture RiskFRAX® (With/Without BMD)
Lateral Spine X-RayIf Height Loss >3cm, Kyphosis, Back Pain

4. Treatment — Pharmacological Therapy

Treatment Indications (NOGG / NICE / ESCEO)

ScenarioTreatment Indicated
Osteoporosis (T ≤-2.5)Yes
Osteopenia (T -1 to -2.5) + FRAX >ThresholdYes
Fragility Fracture (Any T-Score)Yes
Glucocorticoid-InducedYes (If ≥5mg Pred >3mo + T ≤-1.5)

First-Line: Oral Bisphosphonates

DrugDoseAdministrationMonitoring
Alendronate70mg Weekly POFirst-Line; Fast 30min, Upright 30min, Water 200mLDEXA 2-3yr; eGFR if <35
Risedronate35mg Weekly / 150mg MonthlyAlternative (Better GI Tolerance)
Ibandronate150mg Monthly PO / 3mg IV q3moGI Intolerance
Zoledronic Acid5mg IV AnnualAlternative if Oral Contraindicated; eGFR ≥35 (Avoid <35)eGFR ≥35

Bisphosphonate Duration & Drug Holiday

DurationAction
3-5 Years (Oral) / 3 Years (IV)Reassess → Drug Holiday if Low Risk (T-Score >-2.5, No Fracture)
High Risk (Prior Fracture / T ≤-3.0 / Steroid)Continue Beyond 5-6 Years
Drug Holiday MonitoringDEXA q1-2yr; Restart if T-Score ≤-2.5 or Fracture

3. Second-Line / Anabolic Therapies

DrugDoseIndicationAdvantage
Denosumab60mg SC q6mo1st-Line if BP Contraindicated/Intolerant; GIOPNo Renal Adjustment; Potent ↓ Fracture
Teriparatide20µg SC Daily (Max 24 Months)Severe Osteoporosis (T ≤-3.5, Prior Fracture, Failed BP)Anabolic (↑ Bone Formation)
Romosozumab210mg SC Monthly ×12moSevere (Very High Fracture Risk)Anabolic + Antiresorptive
Raloxifene60mg ODPostmenopausal Women; Breast Cancer Risk ReductionSERM
HRTOestrogen ± ProgestogenEarly Postmenopause (<10yr)Symptom Relief + Bone

Teriparatide / Romosozumab Key Points

DrugDurationMonitoringKey Points
TeriparatideMax 24 Months (Rat Osteosarcoma Risk)ALP, Ca²⁺, Renal FunctionAnabolic; ↑ Bone Formation
Romosozumab12 Months Only → Follow with AntiresorptiveALP, Ca²⁺, CV RiskAnabolic + Antiresorptive; CVD Risk (MI/Stroke)

4. Glucocorticoid-Induced Osteoporosis (GIOP)

Risk Stratification

RiskCriteriaAction
High Risk≥5mg Pred >3mo + T-Score ≤-1.5 OR Prior Fracture OR Age >70Start Bone Protection Immediately
Moderate≥5mg Pred >3mo + T-Score >-1.5Consider (If High FRAX)
Low<5mg Pred OR <3moLifestyle + Calcium/Vit D

First-Line for GIOP

DrugDose
Oral Bisphosphonate (Alendronate/Risedronate)First-Line
Zoledronic Acid 5mg IV AnnualIf Oral Contraindicated
Denosumab 60mg SC q6moPreferred if High Fracture Risk / eGFR <35
TeriparatidePreferred if Very High Risk / Prior Fracture (Anabolic Superior in GIOP)
Calcium + Vitamin D Mandatory with All Therapies.

4. Monitoring & Follow-Up

ParameterFrequency
DEXA2-3 Years After Initiation; Then Q2-3yr
HeightAnnual (Vertebral Fracture Screen)
BiochemistryAnnual (Ca, Phos, ALP, 25-OH Vit D, Renal)
AdherenceEach Visit

4. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Osteoporosis DefinitionT-Score ≤-2.5 SD (Lumbar Spine / Femoral Neck)
OsteopeniaT-Score -1.0 to -2.5
FRAX ThresholdMajor Osteoporotic Fracture ≥7.5-15% (Age-Dependent); Hip ≥3-4.5%
First-Line RxAlendronate 70mg Weekly (Oral Bisphosphonate)
Zoledronic Acid5mg IV Annual; eGFR ≥35; Alternative if Oral Contraindicated
Denosumab60mg SC q6mo; No Renal Adjustment; No Drug Holiday (Rapid Bone Loss on Stop)
Teriparatide20µg SC Daily ×24mo Max; Anabolic; Severe Osteoporosis (T ≤-3.5, Fracture)
Romosozumab210mg SC Monthly ×12mo; Anabolic + Antiresorptive; Severe/High Risk
GIOP Threshold≥5mg Pred >3mo + T ≤-1.5 → Treat
Bisphosphonate HolidayAfter 3-5yr (Oral) / 3yr (IV) if Low Risk; No Holiday for Denosumab
Denosumab HolidayContraindicated → Rapid Bone Loss; Transition to Bisphosphonate
TeriparatideAnabolic; Max 24mo; Severe (T ≤-3.5, Prior Fracture)
Romosozumab12 Months Only → Follow with Antiresorptive
DEXA Monitoringq2-3yr After Initiation; Height Annually (Vertebral Fracture)

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Osteopenia vs OsteoporosisOsteopenia: T -1 to -2.5; Osteoporosis: T ≤-2.5
T-Score vs Z-ScoreT-Score = vs Young Adult Mean; Z-Score = vs Age/Sex Matched (Use Z in <50yr)
Bisphosphonate HolidayOral: 3-5yr → Holiday; IV Zoledronic: 3yr → Holiday; Denosumab = NO HOLIDAY
Denosumab HolidayContraindicated — Rapid Bone Loss → Transition to Bisphosphonate
Teriparatide DurationMax 24 Months (Rat Osteosarcoma Risk); Anabolic
Romosozumab Duration12 Months Only → Follow with Antiresorptive
FRAX Without BMDValid (But Less Accurate); Add BMD for Accuracy
Zoledronic Acid RenaleGFR ≥35; <35 → Avoid/Reduce dose
Teriparatide Max Duration24 Months Lifetime Max (Rat Osteosarcoma Data)
Romosozumab Duration12 Months Only → Follow with Antiresorptive

▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.6.3 Paget Disease Of Bone
[!info]
Paget Disease of Bone = Focal Disorder of Bone Remodelling with Excessive Osteoclastic Resorption → Disorganised Osteoblastic Formation. Age >55; Male > Female; UK/Northern Europe Highest Prevalence. 3 Phases: Lytic → Mixed → Sclerotic. ALP = Disease Activity Marker. Bisphosphonates 1st Line (Zoledronic Acid).

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Recognise clinical presentation: bone pain, deformity, deafness, complications
  • [ ] Apply radiological and biochemical diagnosis (ALP, X-Ray, Bone Scan)
  • [ ] Stage disease: Lytic → Mixed → Sclerotic (Burnt-Out)
  • [ ] Apply treatment: Zoledronic Acid 1st Line; Indications for treatment
  • [ ] Recognise complications: OA, Fractures, Nerve Compression, High-Output HF, Osteosarcoma (<1%)

2. Epidemiology & Pathophysiology

FeatureDetails
IncidenceDeclining; ~1-2% of >55yr in UK
Age>55 Years (Rare <40)
SexMale > Female (1.5:1)
GeographyUK/Northern Europe Highest; African/Asian Rare
GeneticsSQSTM1 Mutation (~30% Familial); Viral (Paramyxovirus Hypothesis)
PathophysiologyExcessive Osteoclastic Resorption → Compensatory Disorganised Osteoblastic Formation → Woven Bone (Weak, Deformed)

Three Phases of Paget Disease

PhaseHistologyALPClinical
1. Lytic (Osteolytic)Osteoclasts > Osteoblasts → Osteolysis↑↑↑ (Early Rise)Often Asymptomatic; Bone Pain if Active
2. Mixed (Osteolytic-Osteoblastic)Osteoclasts + Osteoblasts Active↑↑ (Peak)Bone Pain, Deformity, Widening
3. Sclerotic (Osteoblastic/Burnt-Out)Osteoblasts > Osteoclasts → Dense Sclerotic Bone↓ (Towards Normal)Deformity, Fractures, Nerve Compression

2. Clinical Presentation

FeatureFrequencyDetails
Asymptomatic~70%Incidental ALP ↑ or X-Ray Finding
Bone Pain30-40%Deep, Aching, Night Pain (Active Lytic Phase)
Deformity15-20%Bowing Tibia/Femur, Skull Enlargement (Frontal Bossing)
Fractures5-10%Insufficiency Fractures (Long Bones, Vertebrae)
Osteoarthritis20-30%Adjacent Joints (Hip, Knee) — Mechanical Stress
Nerve Compression5-10%CN VIII Deafness (Skull Base), Spinal Stenosis, CN VII Palsy
High-Output Heart Failure<1% (Severe Polyostotic)Arteriovenous Shunting in Vascular Pagetic Bone
Osteosarcoma<1%Malignant Transformation (Late Complication)

2. Biochemical Markers

MarkerFindingSignificance
ALP (Total)Markedly ↑ (Often 3-10x ULN)Best Activity Marker; Disproportionate vs Other LFTs
Bone-Specific ALP (BALP)↑↑More Specific for Bone Turnover
CalciumNormalUsually Normal (Unless Immobilisation/Hypercalcaemia)
PhosphateNormalNormal
PTHNormalNormal
25-OH Vit DNormal/LowNormal (Unless Concomitant Deficiency)
Urinary Hydroxyproline / NTX / CTX↑↑Bone Resorption Markers (If Available)
ALP is Disproportionately Elevated vs Other LFTs (AST, ALT, GGT, Bilirubin Normal).

2. Imaging

ModalityFindings

| Plain X-Ray | Lytic: Osteoporosis Circumscripta (Skull), "Flame-Shaped" Lytic Advancing Edge (Long Bones)

Mixed: Coarse Trabeculae, Cortical Thickening, Bone Expansion

Sclerotic: Dense Sclerosis, "Cotton Wool" Appearance (Skull), Bony Expansion |

Bone Scan (Tc-99m MDP)Intense, Increased Uptake (Polyostotic, Intense "Hot Spots"); Best for Extent Assessment
MRISoft Tissue Extension, Spinal Canal Stenosis, Nerve Compression
CTCortical Thickening, Bone Expansion, Spinal Stenosis Detail

2. Diagnosis

Diagnostic Criteria (Clinical + Biochemical + Radiological)

CriterionRequirement
ClinicalBone Pain, Deformity, Fracture, Deafness, Neurological Signs
BiochemicalALP ↑↑ (Disproportionate); Normal Ca²⁺, PO₄, PTH
RadiologicalLytic → Mixed → Sclerotic Changes on X-Ray/Bone Scan
Bone Scan = Best for Extent (Polyostotic vs Monostotic); X-Ray = Best for Phase (Lytic/Mixed/Sclerotic).

3. Indications for Treatment

IndicationDetails
Symptomatic Bone PainDeep, Aching, Night Pain (Active Disease)
Impending FractureImpending Pathological Fracture (Long Bones)
Neurological ComplicationsNerve Compression (CN VIII, Spinal Cord), Cranial Nerve Palsies
High-Output Heart FailureSevere Polyostotic Disease
Pre-OperativeSurgery on Pagetic Bone (Joint Replacement, Fixation)
Serum ALP >2x ULNAsymptomatic but High Turnover (Prevent Complications)

3. Management

Bisphosphonates (1st Line)

AgentDoseRouteDurationKey Points
Zoledronic Acid5mg IV Single Infusion1st Line (Preferred)Single Dose (Long Duration)Most Potent; Monitor Renal Function (eGFR ≥35)
Risedronate30mg OD × 2 MonthsOral Alternative2-Month CourseLess Potent; Daily Upright 30min
Pamidronate60-90mg IV (Infusion)If Zoledronic UnavailableMultiple InfusionsOutdated by Zoledronic

Monitoring Response

ParameterFrequencyTarget
ALPq3-6 MonthsNormalisation (Remission)
Bone Scan1-2 YearsReduced Uptake
SymptomsEach VisitPain Relief, Functional Improvement

Relapse / Retreatment

ScenarioAction
ALP Rise >50% Above NadirRetreat with Zoledronic Acid 5mg IV
Symptomatic RelapseRetreat
Maximum CoursesNot Defined; Repeated Courses Safe

3. Complications & Management

ComplicationManagement
OsteoarthritisJoint Replacement (Hip/Knee Common); Pre-Op Bisphosphonate
Pathological FractureInternal Fixation (IM Nailing); Post-Op Bisphosphonate
Nerve Compression (CN VIII)Hearing Aids (1st Line); Cochlear Implant (Severe); Surgery Rare
Spinal Stenosis / Cord CompressionDecompressive Laminectomy ± Instrumentation; Pre-Op Bisphosphonate
High-Output Heart FailureDiuretics, Afterload Reduction, Bisphosphonate (Reduces Vascular Shunt)
OsteosarcomaMultimodal: Surgery (Amputation/Limb-Salvage) + Chemo (Cisplatin/Doxorubicin)

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Paget DiseaseFocal Bone Remodelling Disorder; Age >55, Male>Female, UK High Prevalence
Three PhasesLytic (Osteolytic) → Mixed → Sclerotic (Burnt-Out)
ALPDisproportionately ↑ (Best Marker); Peak in Mixed Phase
Zoledronic Acid5mg IV Single Dose — 1st Line (Most Potent, Long Duration)
Treatment IndicationsPain, Impending Fracture, Nerve Compression, High-Output HF, ALP >2x ULN
Skull FindingsOsteoporosis Circumscripta (Lytic); "Cotton Wool" Sclerosis (Sclerotic)
Long Bones"Flame-Shaped" Lytic Edge (Advancing Osteolytic Front); Coarse Trabeculae (Mixed)
Bone ScanBest for Extent — Intense Uptake, Polyostotic
CN VIII DeafnessCommon (Skull Base Involvement); Hearing Aids / Cochlear Implant
Osteosarcoma<1% Risk; Late Complication; Multimodal (Surgery + Chemo)
High-Output HFSevere Polyostotic → AV Shunting in Pagetic Bone
Zoledronic Acid5mg IV Single Dose — Preferred; Monitor eGFR (≥35)
Risedronate30mg OD × 2 Months (Oral Alternative)
RelapseALP Rise >50% Above Nadir → Retreat
ALP in PagetDisproportionately ↑ vs Other LFTs; Best Activity Marker

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Paget vs OsteoporosisPaget = Focal, ↑ ALP, Deformity; Osteoporosis = Generalised, Normal ALP, Fracture Risk
Paget vs OsteomalaciaPaget = Normal Ca/PO₄/PTH, ↑ ALP; Osteomalacia = ↓ PO₄, ↑ ALP, ↑ PTH
Lytic vs Sclerotic PhaseLytic = ↑↑ ALP, Expanding Lytic Edge; Sclerotic = ↓ ALP, Dense Bone
ALP in PagetDisproportionate ↑ vs Other LFTs (AST/ALT/GGT Normal)
Bone Scan vs X-RayBone Scan = Extent (Polyostotic); X-Ray = Phase (Lytic/Mixed/Sclerotic)
Zoledronic vs RisedronateZoledronic = Single IV Dose (Preferred); Risedronate = 30mg OD × 2mo (Oral)
Osteosarcoma Risk<1% (Late); Multimodal (Surgery + Chemo)
CN VIII DeafnessCommon (Skull Base); Hearing Aids / Cochlear Implant; Surgery Rare
High-Output HFSevere Polyostotic → AV Shunting; Treat with Bisphosphonates + HF Rx
Zoledronic Acid RenaleGFR ≥35 Required; Avoid if <35

CN VIII DeafnessCommon; Hearing Aids / Cochlear Implant
Osteosarcoma<1%; Late; Surgery + Chemo (Cisplatin/Doxorubicin)
High-Output HFAV Shunting in Pagetic Bone; Bisphosphonate + HF Rx
Zoledronic Acid5mg IV Single Dose; Monitor eGFR (≥35)
RelapseALP >50% Nadir → Retreat with Zoledronic
ALPDisproportionate ↑ vs AST/ALT/GGT/Bili
