▼  Show infographic image click to expand
▸ 19.6.4 Renal Osteodystrophy
[!info]
CKD-MBD = Systemic Disorder of Mineral & Bone Metabolism due to CKD. Universal in CKD G4-5D. Triad: Abnormal Ca/PO₄/PTH, Bone Turnover Abnormalities, Vascular Calcification. KDIGO 2017 Targets: PTH 2-9x ULN, Ca 2.1-2.5, PO₄ 0.8-1.5, Ca×P <4.5.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Explain the CKD-MBD pathophysiology cascade (Phosphate → FGF23 → Vit D → Ca → PTH)
  • [ ] Apply KDIGO 2017 targets for PTH, Calcium, Phosphate, Ca×P Product
  • [ ] Select and sequence phosphate binders (calcium-based vs non-calcium)
  • [ ] Select vitamin D analogues for CKD G4-5D (Alfacalcidol, Calcitriol, Paricalcitol)
  • [ ] Apply calcimimetic (Cinacalcet) indications and monitoring
  • [ ] Recognise and manage adynamic bone disease and calciphylaxis

2. Pathophysiology — The CKD-MBD Vicious Cycle

CKD (↓ GFR)
    │
    ├─→ **Phosphate Retention** (↓ Filtered Load)
    │       │
    │       ├─→ **FGF23 ↑** (Osteocyte Response) → ↓ 1α-Hydroxylase → **↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D**
    │       │       │
    │       │       └─→ **↓ Intestinal Ca²⁺ Absorption** → **Hypocalcaemia**
    │       │
    │       └─→ **Direct PTH Stimulation** (Phosphate → PTH Gene Expression)
    │
    └─→ **Hypocalcaemia** (↓ Ca²⁺ Absorption + ↓ Vit D) → **PTH ↑↑** (Secondary HPT)

Key Mediators

MediatorChange in CKDEffect
Phosphate↑↑ (Retention)Direct PTH Stim; FGF23 ↑
FGF23↑↑↑ (Early Rise)↓ 1α-Hydroxylase; ↓ 1,25-(OH)₂D
1,25-(OH)₂D (Calcitriol)↓↓↓↓ Intestinal Ca²⁺ Absorption → Hypocalcaemia
Calcium↓↑ PTH Secretion
PTH↑↑↑ (Secondary HPT)Bone Resorption; Phosphate Excretion

2. Stages of CKD-MBD (KDIGO)

CKD StageGFR (mL/min)PhosphateFGF231,25-(OH)₂DPTHBone Turnover
G3a (45-59)MildNormal↑Normal/↓↑ (1-2x ULN)Normal/High
G3b (30-44)Moderate↑↑↑↓↑↑ (2-5x ULN)High
G4 (15-29)Severe↑↑↑↑↑↓↓↑↑↑ (5-10x ULN)High/Adynamic
G5 (<15) / DialysisFailure↑↑↑↑↑↑↑Absent↑↑↑↑ (10-50x ULN)Adynamic/Mixed

2. KDIGO 2017 Targets (CKD G3-5D)

ParameterTarget (CKD 3-5D)Target (Dialysis)
PTH2-9x ULN2-9x ULN
Corrected Calcium2.1-2.5 mmol/L2.1-2.5 mmol/L
Phosphate0.8-1.5 mmol/L (Stage 3-4)1.1-1.5 mmol/L (Dialysis)
Ca × P Product<4.5 mmol²/L²<4.5 mmol²/L²
25-OH Vitamin D≥30 ng/mL (75 nmol/L)≥30 ng/mL
Alkaline PhosphataseMonitor TrendsMonitor Trends
Note: PTH Target is Wide (2-9x ULN) — Avoid Over-Suppression (Adynamic Bone Disease).

2. Management Algorithm (KDIGO 2017) — Stepwise

CKD-MBD Diagnosed (CKD G3-5, Abnormal Ca/Phos/PTH)
         │
         ▼
STEP 1: **PHOSPHATE BINDERS** (With Meals)
         │
         ├── **Calcium-Based** (Carbonate/Acetate) — **1st Line if Ca²⁺ Normal/Low**
         │       Dose: 0.5-1g with Meals; Max 1.5-2g Elemental Ca/day
         │       Watch: Hypercalcaemia, Vascular Calcification
         │
         ├── **Non-Calcium-Based** (Sevelamer, Lanthanum, Sucroferric Oxyhydroxide)
         │       **1st Line if Ca²⁺ High / Vascular Calcification / Adynamic Bone**
         │       Sevelamer 800-2400mg TDS with Meals
         │
         └── **Ferric Citrate** (Newer; Also Treats Anaemia)
                 Dose: 1g TDS with Meals
                 │
         ▼
STEP 2: **VITAMIN D ANALOGUES** (If PTH Still >9x ULN after Phosphate Control)
         │
         ├── **Alfacalcidol (1α-OH D3)** 0.25-1µg/day (or 1µg Alternate Days)
         ├── **Calcitriol (1,25-(OH)₂D)** 0.25-1µg/day (or 1µg Alternate Days)
         ├── **Paricalcitol** (Selective VDR Agonist) 1-2µg 3x/week (Post-HD)
         │       Advantage: Less Hypercalcaemia/Hyperphosphataemia
         │
         ▼
STEP 3: **CALCIMIMETICS** (If PTH Still >9x ULN Despite Above)
         │
         ├── **Cinacalcet** 30-180mg/day (BD) — CaSR Agonist
         │       Mechanism: ↓ PTH Secretion; Effect: ↓ PTH, ↓ Ca, ↓ Phos
         │       Adverse: Hypocalcaemia, Nausea, QTc Prolongation
         │       Advantage: **↓ PTH, ↓ Ca, ↓ Phos** (Unique Triple Effect)
         │
         └── **Etelcalcetide** (IV, Post-HD) 5-15mg 3x/week (HD Only)

2. Phosphate Binder Selection Algorithm

Patient Profile1st Line BinderRationale
Normal Ca²⁺, No Vascular Calcification, eGFR ≥30Calcium Carbonate/AcetateCheap, Ca²⁺ Supplement
Hypercalcaemia / Vascular Calcification / Adynamic BoneNon-Calcium (Sevelamer / Lanthanum / Sucroferric / Ferric Citrate)Avoids Ca²⁺ Load
Dialysis + HyperphosphataemiaSevelamer / Lanthanum / Ferric CitrateFerric Citrate → Also Treats Anaemia
Key Principle: Avoid Calcium-Based Binders if Ca²⁺ High or Vascular Calcification Present.

2. Vitamin D Analogues in CKD

AgentIndicationDoseAdvantage
Alfacalcidol (1α-OH D3)CKD G3-50.25-1µg/dayRapid 1α-Hydroxylation; Reliable
Calcitriol (1,25-(OH)₂D₃)CKD G4-5, Dialysis0.25-1µg/dayActive Form; Short t½
ParicalcitolCKD G4-5D / Dialysis1-2µg 3x/week (Post-HD)Selective VDR → Less Hypercalcaemia/Phosphataemia
DoxercalciferolCKD G4-510-30µg TIW1α-OH D2 Analogue
Key: Nutritional D2/D3 (Cholecalciferol/Ergocalciferol) INSUFFICIENT in CKD G4-5/Dialysis — Requires Renal 1α-Hydroxylation.

2. Cinacalcet (Calcimimetic)

FeatureDetails
MechanismCaSR Agonist → ↓ PTH Secretion
Dose30-180mg/day (BD); Start 30mg BD, Titrate q2-4wk
Effect↓ PTH, ↓ Ca, ↓ Phos (Unique Triple Effect)
Adverse EffectsHypocalcaemia, Nausea, QTc Prolongation
MonitoringCa²⁺ q1-2wk (Start); PTH q1-3mo; QTc ECG
Etelcalcetide (IV, HD Only)5-15mg 3x/week Post-HD; No Oral Absorption Issues

3. CKD-MBD Management Algorithm (KDIGO 2017)

CKD G3-5 / Dialysis + Abnormal Ca/Phos/PTH
         │
         ▼
STEP 1: DIETARY PHOSPHATE RESTRICTION (800-1000 mg/day)
         │
         ▼
STEP 2: PHOSPHATE BINDERS (With Meals)
         │       (See Selection Algorithm Above)
         │
         ▼
STEP 3: VITAMIN D ANALOGUES (If PTH >9x ULN Despite Phosphate Control)
         │       Alfacalcidol / Calcitriol / Paricalcitol
         │
         ▼
STEP 4: CALCIMIMETICS (If PTH >9x ULN Despite Above)
         │       Cinacalcet (PO) / Etelcalcetide (IV HD)
         │
         ▼
STEP 5: PARATHYROIDECTOMY (Refractory SHPT)
         │       Indications: PTH >800-1000 pg/mL; Ca >2.75; Phos >1.8; Calciphylaxis
         │       Procedure: Subtotal (3.5-Gland) + Autotransplant

3. Adynamic Bone Disease — Over-Suppression

FeatureRecognitionManagement
CluePTH <2x ULN (or <100-150 pg/mL) + Low ALP + Low Bone TurnoverStop/Reduce Vitamin D Analogues & Calcimimetics
RiskFracture ↑ (Low Bone Turnover), ↑ Vascular CalcificationPTH Target 2-9x ULN (Not Lower)
DiagnosisBone Biopsy (Gold Standard); Low PTH + Low ALPPTH Target 2-9x ULN (Not Lower)

3. Calciphylaxis (Calcific Uraemic Arteriolopathy)

FeatureManagement
DiagnosisPainful Violaceous Skin Lesions → Necrosis/Ulceration; Biopsy (Medial Calcification)
Risk FactorsCa×P >4.5, Obesity, Diabetes, Warfarin, High PTH, High Calcium/Phosphate
Emergency ManagementUrgent Parathyroidectomy (If Severe SHPT) + Intensive Wound Care
MedicalSodium Thiosulfate 25g IV 3x/week (Post-HD); Cinacalcet (↓ PTH, Ca, Phos); Bisphosphonates (IV Zoledronic)
Wound CareMultidisciplinary (Nephrology, Dermatology, Surgery, Plastics)
Mortality50-80%

3. Monitoring Targets (KDIGO)

ParameterCKD G3-4CKD G5 / Dialysis
PTH2-9x ULN (q3-6mo)2-9x ULN (Monthly)
Corrected Calcium2.1-2.5 mmol/L (q3-6mo)2.1-2.5 mmol/L (Monthly)
Phosphate0.8-1.5 mmol/L (q3-6mo)1.1-1.5 mmol/L (Monthly)
Ca × P Product<4.5 mmol²/L²<4.5 mmol²/L²
25-OH Vit D≥30 ng/mL (q6-12mo)≥30 ng/mL (q6mo)
Alkaline PhosphataseAnnual (Bone Turnover)q3-6mo

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Vit D in DialysisNutritional D2/D3 Ineffective (No Renal 1α-Hydroxylase) → Use Active Analogues
PTH Target2-9x ULN (Wide Range); <2x = Adynamic Bone
CalciphylaxisUrgent PTX + Thiosulfate + Cinacalcet
SGLT2i in HDDapagliflozin/Empagliflozin Approved (No Dose Adjust)
Insulin in HDReduce 30-50%; Dose Post-HD
Levothyroxine in HDNo Dose Reduction (Protein Bound, Not Dialysable)
Non-Ca BindersSevelamer, Lanthanum, Ferric Citrate, Sucroferric Oxyhydroxide
Adynamic BonePTH <2x ULN; Stop Vit D Analogues / Calcimimetics
CalciphylaxisMedical Emergency; PTX + Sodium Thiosulfate + Cinacalcet
Cinacalcet SEHypocalcaemia (Monitor Ca q1-2wk Initially)

9. Mind Map

Renal Osteodystrophy / CKD-MBD
Pathophysiology
Phos ↑ → FGF23↑ → VitD↓ → Ca↓ → PTH↑
Targets: PTH 2-9xULN, Ca 2.1-2.5, Phos 0.8-1.5, Ca×P<4.5
G1-3: Cholecalciferol OK; G4-5/HD: Active Analogues
Binders
Ca-based (Ca normal) vs Non-Ca (Ca high/Calcification)
Sevelamer, Lanthanum, Ferric Citrate, Sucroferric
Cinacalcet: CaSR Agonist → ↓PTH,↓Ca,↓Phos; Watch Hypocalcaemia
Adynamic Bone: PTH<2xULN → Stop VitD/Calcimimetic
Calciphylaxis: Ca×P>4.5 → Urgent PTX + Thiosulfate + Cinacalcet
CKD Stages
G3a: Mild; G3b: Mod; G4: Severe; G5/HD: Failure
PTH: 1-2x → 2-5x → 5-10x → 10-50x ULN
FGF23: ↑ early; Then 1,25-(OH)2D ↓
Vit D
G1-3: Cholecalciferol OK
G4-5/HD: Active Analogues (Alfa/Calcitriol/Paricalcitol)
Paricalcitol: Selective VDR (Less HyperCa/Phos)
Monitoring
PTH 2-9xULN; Ca 2.1-2.5; Phos 0.8-1.5 (HD 1.1-1.5)
Ca×P <4.5; 25-OH Vit D ≥30 ng/mL
ALP trends for bone turnover
Calciphylaxis
Ca×P>4.5 → PTX + Thiosulfate + Cinacalcet
Mortality 50-80%
Adynamic Bone
PTH<2xULN → Stop VitD/Calcimimetic
Fracture risk ↑

Summary

Renal Osteodystrophy: Core definitions, stepwise diagnosis, algorithmic management, critical thresholds, monitoring, red flags.

MCQs (10)

  1. Renal osteodystrophy definition:

A. Low bone mass in CKD

B. Bone mineral/structural changes in CKD

C. Osteoporosis in CKD

D. Osteomalacia in CKD

Answer: B

  1. CKD-MBD triad:

A. Bone, Vascular, Mineral

B. Bone, Heart, Kidney

C. Bone, Liver, Lung

D. Vascular, Heart, Kidney

Answer: A

  1. CKD Stage 3-5 labs:

A. Low Ca, High Phos, High PTH, Low Vit D

B. High Ca, Low Phos, Low PTH, High Vit D

C. Normal

D. High Ca, High Phos, Low PTH, High Vit D

Answer: A

  1. Secondary HPT mechanism:

A. Low Ca -> PTH up

B. Low Vit D -> PTH up

C. High Phos -> PTH up

D. All of the above

Answer: D

  1. Adynamic bone disease:

A. High PTH, High turnover

B. Low PTH, Low turnover

C. Normal PTH, High turnover

D. Low PTH, High turnover

Answer: B

  1. Osteitis fibrosa:

A. Low PTH

B. High PTH, High turnover

C. Low turnover

D. Normal turnover

Answer: B

  1. Mixed uremic osteodystrophy:

A. Pure adynamic

B. Pure osteitis fibrosa

C. Mixed high + low turnover

D. Normal turnover

Answer: C

  1. KDIGO PTH target:

A. PTH 2-9x ULN

B. PTH <2x ULN

C. PTH >9x ULN

D. Normalize PTH

Answer: A

  1. Calcium-based binder:

A. Sevelamer

B. Lanthanum

C. Calcium carbonate

D. Lanthanum carbonate

Answer: C

  1. Non-calcium binder:

A. Calcium carbonate

B. Sevelamer

C. Aluminum hydroxide

D. Magnesium carbonate

▸ 19.7 Other Topics 1
▸ 19.7.1 Cerebral Salt Wasting
[!info]
Cerebral Salt Wasting (CSW) = Renal Salt Wasting secondary to Intracranial Disease. Hypovolaemic Hyponatraemia with High Urine Sodium. Key Differentiator from SIADH: Volume Status (Hypovolaemic). Management = Saline Resuscitation + Fludrocortisone (Opposite of SIADH).

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Differentiate CSW from SIADH using volume status assessment
  • [ ] Recognise CSW in the context of intracranial disease
  • [ ] Apply saline resuscitation and fludrocortisone therapy
  • [ ] Identify at-risk patient populations (neurosurgical, SAH, TBI)

2. Pathophysiology

MechanismDescription
Primary EventIntracranial Disease (SAH, TBI, Neurosurgery, Tumour, Infection)
Proposed Mechanisms1. Brain Natriuretic Peptide (BNP) Release → ↓ Renal Na⁺ Reabsorption
2. Sympathetic Overactivity → Renal Vasoconstriction → ↓ Renal Perfusion
3. Impaired Renal Sympathetic Regulation → Loss of Sodium Conservation
ResultRenal Salt Wasting → Volume Depletion → 2nd ADH Release → Hyponatraemia

2. Clinical Context & Risk Factors

Risk FactorDetails
Subarachnoid Haemorrhage (SAH)Most Common Setting (Incidence 10-20% Post-SAH)
Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI)Post-Neurosurgery, Severe TBI
NeurosurgeryEspecially Pituitary/Tumour Resection
Intracranial TumoursPituitary, Craniopharyngioma, Metastases
CNS InfectionsMeningitis, Encephalitis, Brain Abscess
Intracerebral HaemorrhageHypertensive, Amyloid Angiopathy

2. Clinical Presentation

FeatureCSWSIADH (For Comparison)
Volume StatusHypovolaemicEuvolaemic
HyponatraemiaYesYes
Urine Sodium>20 mmol/L (Often >100)>20 mmol/L
Urine Osmolality>100 mOsm/kg>100 mOsm/kg
JVPLowNormal
Skin TurgorDryNormal
Postural BPDrop >20 mmHgNormal
Urine OutputHigh (Polyuria)Low/Normal
Serum Uric AcidHighLow/Normal
Underlying DiseaseIntracranial PathologyMalignancy, Drugs, Pulmonary, CNS

3. Diagnostic Criteria

CriterionCSW Requirement
1. Intracranial DiseasePresent (SAH, TBI, Neurosurgery, Tumour)
2. HyponatraemiaSerum Na⁺ <135 mmol/L
3. Volume StatusHypovolaemic (Low JVP, Dry Mucosa, Postural Hypotension)
4. Urine sodium>20 mmol/L (Often >100)
5. Urine Osmolality>100 mOsm/kg (Inappropriately Concentrated)
6. No DiureticsExclude Recent Diuretic Use
All Criteria Must Be Met for Diagnosis.

3. SIADH vs CSW — Side-by-Side Comparison

FeatureSIADHCSW
Volume StatusEuvolaemicHypovolaemic
JVPNormalLow
Skin TurgorNormalDry
Postural BPNormalPostural Drop >20 mmHg
Urine OutputLow/NormalHigh (Polyuria)
Urine Na⁺>20>20 (Often Higher)
Urine Osm>100>100
Serum Uric AcidLow/NormalHigh
BUN/CreatinineNormal/LowElevated (Pre-renal)
PathophysiologyADH Excess → Water RetentionRenal Salt Wasting → Volume Depletion → ADH Release
ManagementFluid RestrictionSaline Resuscitation (+ Fludrocortisone)
Key: Volume Status is the Key Discriminator — SIADH = Euvolaemic; CSW = Hypovolaemic.

3. Management

Acute Resuscitation

StepAction
1. IV 0.9% NaCl1-2L Bolus → Then 150-200 mL/hr (Goal: Euvolaemia)
2. TargetUrine Output >0.5 mL/kg/h; JVP Normal; Postural BP Normal
3. Fludrocortisone0.05-0.2mg OD (Mineralocorticoid Replacement)
4. Salt SupplementationNaCl Tablets 1-2g TDS (If Ongoing Losses)
5. MonitorNa⁺, K⁺, Volume Status, UOP q2-4h

Duration of Therapy

PhaseDuration
Acute Phase1-2 Weeks Post-Insult (Peak Salt Wasting)
WeaningGradual Over 1-2 Weeks as CNS Recovers
DiscontinuationWhen Euvolaemic + Stable Na⁺ + No Ongoing Salt Loss

3. Complications & Monitoring

ComplicationPrevention / Management
Rapid Na⁺ CorrectionMax 8-10 mmol/L/24h (ODS Risk)
Volume OverloadMonitor JVP, CVP, Lungs; Adjust Fluids
HyperkalaemiaFludrocortisone → Monitor K⁺
HypertensionFludrocortisone → Monitor BP
Recurrent HyponatraemiaContinue Fludrocortisone Until CNS Recovery

3. Differential: CSW vs SIADH vs Other

FeatureCSWSIADHHypovolaemic (GI/Renal)Adrenal Insufficiency
VolumeHypovolaemicEuvolaemicHypovolaemicHypovolaemic
Urine Na⁺High (>20)High (>20)Low (<20) if Extra-renalHigh (>20)
Urine Osm>100>100>100 (If Renal)>100
Postural BPDrop >20NormalDrop (If Severe)Drop
Uric AcidHighLow/NormalNormal/HighNormal/High
CortisolNormalNormalNormalLow
ACTHNormalNormalNormalHigh
Key DiscriminatorHypovolaemia + High Urine Na⁺ + CNS DiseaseEuvolaemiaUrine Na⁺ <20 (Extra-renal)Low Cortisol, High ACTH

3. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
CSW DefinitionRenal Salt Wasting from Intracranial Disease → Hypovolaemic Hyponatraemia
Most Common SettingSubarachnoid Haemorrhage (SAH) (10-20% Post-SAH)
CSW vs SIADHVolume Status = Key Discriminator (CSW = Hypovolaemic; SIADH = Euvolaemic)
CSW Key FeaturesHypovolaemia + High Urine Na⁺ + High Urine Osm + CNS Disease
CSW vs SIADHCSW = Hypovolaemic + Polyuria + High Uric Acid; SIADH = Euvolaemic + Low Urine Output
CSW ManagementSaline Resuscitation + Fludrocortisone (Opposite of SIADH)
Fludrocortisone Dose0.05-0.2mg OD (Mineralocorticoid Replacement)
SAH + HyponatraemiaThink CSW (Peak Day 7-10); Differentiate from SIADH
Post-Operative HyponatraemiaCSW Common Post-Neurosurgery; Differentiate from SIADH
Fludrocortisone Dose0.05-0.2mg OD (Monitor BP, K⁺, Volume)
PathophysiologyBNP Release → Renal Salt Wasting; Sympathetic Overactivity
CSW vs SIADHVolume Status = Key (CSW = Hypovolaemic; SIADH = Euvolaemic)
Uric AcidHigh in CSW (vs Low/Normal in SIADH)
Postural DropCSW: >20 mmHg; SIADH = Normal
CSW Uric AcidHigh (vs Low/Normal in SIADH)

8. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
CSW vs SIADHVolume Status is Key: CSW = Hypovolaemic; SIADH = Euvolaemic
Urine Na⁺ in BothBoth Have High Urine Na⁺ (>20); Volume Status Differentiates
CSW ManagementSaline + Fludrocortisone (Not Fluid Restriction!)
CSW vs SIADHCSW = Hypovolaemic + Polyuria; SIADH = Euvolaemic + Low Urine Output
CSW SettingsSAH > TBI > Neurosurgery > Tumours > CNS Infection
FludrocortisoneMineralocorticoid → Salt Retention; Monitor BP, K⁺
BNP in CSW↑ BNP → Natriuresis (vs SIADH where BNP Normal)
CSW vs SIADHVolume Status: CSW = Hypovolaemic; SIADH = Euvolaemic
Uric AcidHigh in CSW; Low in SIADH
Postural BPCSW: Postural Drop >20 mmHg
